- 2026-06-26 - F91 FIXED: dcache_install's `if (existing)` branch (kernel/fs/dcache.c) dropped g_dcache_wlock and THEN bumped existing->refcount with a BARE __atomic_fetch_add OUTSIDE the lock, so it could resurrect a dentry the shrinker had already claimed for free -> use-after-free + refcount wrap + (via SLAB_TYPESAFE_BY_RCU slot reuse) a stale child_ino, i.e. the wrong inode resolved for any open/stat/exec on SMP (fan-out #4 candidate (bb)).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): the install path locked g_dcache_wlock, bucket_find_locked'd `existing` (a key match -- a refcount-0 dentry still on the LRU is a normal find), then spin_unlock_irqrestore'd and only AFTER the unlock did `__atomic_fetch_add(&existing->refcount, 1u, __ATOMIC_ACQ_REL)`; the lookup path (audit fix T1, dcache.c ~244-254) already guards the same hazard with a DYING-aware CAS, but the install-hits-existing path was left bare.  REFINED the recorded prescription (which said "mirror the T1 CAS under the lock"): I checked the shrinker (dcache_shrink ~475-498) and it CAS-claims refcount 0 -> DCACHE_REF_DYING (~488) AND dentry_unlink_and_free_locked's the dentry (~493) BOTH inside ONE g_dcache_wlock critical section -- so a DYING dentry is unlinked from its hash bucket before the lock is released, which means a still-linked entry returned by bucket_find_locked UNDER the lock can NEVER be DYING.  Therefore the root-cause fix is simply to take the reference UNDER g_dcache_wlock, BEFORE the unlock: the lock -- which the shrinker also holds for its claim+unlink -- is the serialization, making "resurrect-via-install" and "claim-for-free" mutually exclusive.  A DYING-aware CAS here would be redundant (its DYING branch is provably unreachable while the lock is held) and would misleadingly imply lock-free concurrency that the lock actually prevents; the CAS belongs to the lock-FREE dcache_lookup (which holds no lock and so genuinely races the shrinker).  FIX (do-it-right, minimal correct, the lock IS the mechanism): moved `__atomic_fetch_add(&existing->refcount, 1u, __ATOMIC_ACQ_REL)` to BEFORE spin_unlock_irqrestore, with a comment explaining the lock-based mutual exclusion vs the lock-free lookup's CAS; the candidate-d disposal (kfree name_ext, parent ref dec, pmm_slab_free) stays after the unlock because d was never published.  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU UAF, not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (the bump now happens under the same lock the shrinker needs for its claim, so they cannot interleave; a found entry is non-DYING under the lock) + the existing dcache concurrency selftests STILL PASS -- `[dcache_test] SELF-TEST PASSED` and `[dcache_race] SELF-TEST PASSED (no resurrect-from-zero reuse)` with child_ino corruptions=0 over 2 lookers + shrinker x 50000 iters (this race test drives lookup/install/shrink concurrently, so it exercises the install path under shrinker pressure and would catch a regression).  Clean boot first try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), all selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` prompt renders.  This closes fan-out #4 candidate (bb).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F92 FIXED: timerfd_settime moved a timer between per-CPU lists as TWO separate locked sections (detach from the old home CPU's list under old_pc->lock, then attach to the calling CPU's list under pc->lock) with NO node-level mutual exclusion, so two concurrent settime callers on a SHARED timerfd could link the one node onto two per-CPU lists -> close frees it from one list while the other still references it -> that CPU's timerfd_tick derefs+fires a freed node = use-after-free (fan-out #4 candidate (dd); kernel/io/timerfd.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): the per-timer state's home_cpu selects WHICH per-CPU lock "protects" its node fields (the struct comment says so), but settime CHANGES home_cpu, so during a move the protecting lock is ambiguous; the detach (timerfd.c ~277-290) and the attach (~303-308) are distinct critical sections under different pc->locks, and tfd_list_insert (~87) has no already-linked guard.  Two threads sharing the fd (home_cpu==~0 on first arm, or both reading the same old home) each insert t into a DIFFERENT CPU's list; t->next (a single pointer) is overwritten by the second insert, cross-linking the two lists, and t becomes reachable from two heads.  REACHABILITY: fork COPIES the fd table but both fds point at the SAME vfs_file_t (the dup just bumps the file refcount), and threads (shared table) / SCM_RIGHTS likewise, so two tasks calling timerfd_settime on one timerfd on different CPUs race; the scheduler is genuinely SMP.  REFINED the recorded prescription (which also wanted the node lock in close): close (timerfd_close_op) does NOT need it -- w_sys_timerfd_settime/gettime fdget-PIN the file (F81), so close runs only at the last fd-ref drop, which cannot overlap any in-flight settime, and close-vs-tick is already serialized by pc->lock; the ONLY unfixed race is settime-vs-settime (each caller holds its own fdget ref, which does not serialize them against each other).  FIX (do-it-right, minimal correct, ONE shared mechanism): added a STABLE per-node spinlock timerfd_state_t.lock (independent of home_cpu) held irqsave across the WHOLE settime detach+attach, making the home_cpu transition atomic vs other settimes.  Lock order t->lock (outer) -> pc->lock (inner); only one pc->lock is ever held at a time (the old home is unlocked before the new home is locked); tick and close take only pc->lock, so there is no lock cycle.  Documented the two-level lock + ordering in docs/LOCKS.md (an undocumented lock is a bug per CLAUDE.md).  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU UAF, not deterministically reproducible -> a NEW concurrent stress selftest (timerfd_race_selftest, mirrors dcache_race): 3 storm kthreads + the main thread hammer settime on 16 SHARED timerfds (armed ~11 days out so they never fire and timerfd_tick early-returns on head_expiry, keeping the lists stable and freeing nothing mid-storm) for 20000 iters, churning each timer's home CPU; after the storm it walks every per-CPU list under its lock and asserts each timer's node appears on EXACTLY ONE list with a consistent home_cpu/in_list (a double-link surfaces as a node counted on two lists or a bounded-walk cycle), then closes all 16 -- `[timerfd_race] SELF-TEST PASSED (no node on two per-CPU lists)`.  The fix is provably INERT to the boot/DHCP path: no userland net/dhcp app uses timerfd and the kernel TCP/IP retransmit path does not either (grep-confirmed), so timerfd is never exercised by networking.  Clean boot: 2 boots hit the flaky F55 userspace-start stall (net ready, login + /bin/net demand-paged, no DHCP lease, no fault); the 3rd SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 63 selftests PASSED incl. `[timerfd-selftest] PASS` AND `[timerfd_race] SELF-TEST PASSED`, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` renders.  This closes fan-out #4 candidate (dd).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F93 FIXED: the kernel pipe had NO lock on its ring -- pipe_read does a non-atomic count-- (+ head advance) and pipe_write a non-atomic count++ (+ tail advance) on the shared pipe_buf_t, so two tasks sharing one pipe read+write concurrently lose count updates -> torn count, unreliable empty/full gating, and (count-- underflow) a u32 wrap to ~4e9 that makes an empty pipe look full of data + torn/stale payload bytes (fan-out #4 candidate (ee); kernel/fs/pipe.c, F84/F85 class).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): pipe_buf_t (pipe.h) has plain uint32_t head/tail/count and no lock; pipe_read drains `dst[total++]=p->buf[p->head]; head=(head+1)&mask; count--` and pipe_write pushes `p->buf[p->tail]=src[total++]; tail=(tail+1)&mask; count++`, both unsynchronised; the shared `count` is RMW'd from both sides.  REACHABILITY: fork DUPS the fd table but both ends point at the SAME pipe_buf_t (the dup just bumps the file refcount), and threads (shared table) / SCM_RIGHTS likewise, so concurrent read+write (or multi-reader/multi-writer) on one pipe across CPUs is reachable.  REFINED the recorded "per-pipe spinlock, drop before sched_sleep/wake" prescription on two points: (1) it is necessary but NOT sufficient -- the data paths touch the USER buffer, and sys_read PREFAULTS its dst (so draining into it UNDER the lock cannot fault, the documented pty_master_drain convention) but sys_write deliberately does NOT prefault its src (a write READS the buffer; absent pages are demand-paged on access, and prefaulting would corrupt a file-backed source by zeroing absent pages), so the write path MUST copy the user source into a kernel bounce buffer with the lock DROPPED and only then push under the lock -- holding the spinlock across src[] would take a #PF under the lock; (2) writer_refs/reader_refs are ALSO RMW'd lock-free (close hooks decrement; read/write read them), so I brought those under the same lock for a uniform discipline.  FIX (do-it-right, ONE shared mechanism mirroring pty master_lock): added pipe_buf_t.lock (plain spinlock -- no pipe path runs in IRQ context).  pipe_read drains the available bytes into the prefaulted user dst under the lock, dropping it before every WAIT_EVENT_HOOK sleep and wake_all.  pipe_write snapshots full/reader-gone under the lock, bounces a <=256-byte chunk from the user source into a kstack buffer with the lock DROPPED, then pushes what fits under the lock (a `count < PIPE_BUF_SIZE` guard makes overflow impossible even if a concurrent writer refilled the ring while the lock was dropped) and wakes readers PER CHUNK -- which also closes a latent missed-wakeup window in the old code, where a writer that filled the ring then blocked woke readers only at the very end.  The close hooks clear reader_refs/writer_refs under the lock, dropping it before the peer wake (can schedule) and before pipe_destroy (which frees the struct holding the lock).  poll/ioctl keep their advisory lockless `count` read (a 32-bit aligned read is atomic; the authoritative re-check is under the lock).  Documented the lock + the prefault/bounce asymmetry in docs/LOCKS.md (an undocumented lock is a bug per CLAUDE.md).  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU data race, not deterministically reproducible -> a NEW concurrent selftest (pipe_race_selftest): a writer kthread + a reader kthread on a SHARED pipe stream a known sequence (byte at stream offset k == k & 0xFF) for 64 KiB (wrapping the 4 KiB ring 16x); the reader verifies EVERY received byte equals its expected offset value AND that the total received equals the total sent; the writer closes the write end after the last byte so the reader always terminates on EOF (the test cannot hang even if the buggy path drops bytes).  `[pipe_race] SELF-TEST PASSED (in-order, no lost/torn bytes, 65536/65536)`.  Pipes ARE boot-exercised (bash pipelines), so the clean boot is a genuine exercise of the new locking.  Clean boot FIRST try (no flaky F55 stall this time): DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 63 selftests PASSED incl. `[pipe_refcount] SELF-TEST PASSED` AND `[pipe_race] SELF-TEST PASSED`, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` renders.  This closes fan-out #4 candidate (ee).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F94 FIXED: mm_vma_remove's front-trim (a left-edge / front munmap of a file- or shmem-backed VMA) advanced v->start = end but left the backing offsets stale, so every subsequent demand fault on the remaining region mapped a page (end - old_start) bytes too early -> the WRONG file/shmem page (intra-file/cross-page disclosure + a wrong-keyed page-cache entry), bounded by file_len/file_size so NOT an OOB/UAF (fan-out #4 candidate (cc); kernel/mm/mm.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): the `else` branch in mm_vma_remove (mm.c ~435, the "Case 3 left edge overlap -- shrink start" arm) did only `v->start = end` while the split arm (Case 4 ~413-415) advances file_off/file_len; the fault path keys the backing off (page - vma->start) -- file: src_off = vma_file_off + (page - vma_start) (vmm.c ~816/847), shmem: pg_idx = (page - vma_start)/PAGE_SIZE + vma_shmem_pgoff (vmm.c ~961) -- so once start moves up by delta the backing offset must move up by the same delta, which the front-trim omitted.  REFINED the recorded prescription (verify-all-angles): it named only file_off/file_len, but Case 4 ALSO advances shmem_pgoff (unconditionally, ~403-404) and the shmem fault path keys off shmem_pgoff identically, so a front-munmap of a SHMEM-backed VMA has the SAME bug -- the fix must advance shmem_pgoff too, not just the file offsets.  Also checked Case 2 (right-edge / shrink-end): CORRECT as-is -- start is unchanged so the offset stays valid and the smaller end bounds later faults (matching Case 4's left fragment, which likewise leaves file_len untouched on an end-shrink); and Case 1 (full cover) frees the VMA, no offsets to fix.  FIX (do-it-right, ONE shared mechanism so the two paths cannot drift again): extracted a static helper vma_backing_advance(vma_t* v, uint64_t delta) that advances shmem_pgoff (page units) and, when file-backed, file_off (+= delta) and file_len (clamped at 0 once the file-backed extent is fully trimmed, the rest being BSS zero-fill); the front-trim now calls it (on v, with delta = end - v->start, computed BEFORE moving start) and the split calls it (on the right fragment, after copying v's backing into it).  The Case-4 refactor is field-by-field equivalent to the old inline math (file / anonymous / shmem all re-verified), so no split regression.  VERIFICATION: an offset-math bug, not concurrency -> a DETERMINISTIC selftest (mm_vma_trim_selftest): helper unit cases (file-backed 2-page front-trim advances file_off + file_len + shmem_pgoff in lockstep; file_len underflow clamps to 0; anonymous VMA keeps file_off/file_len at 0 yet still advances shmem_pgoff) PLUS a real-path case that builds a stack file-backed VMA + a synthetic mm, calls mm_vma_remove to front-trim 2 of 4 pages (a guaranteed Case 3 -- trims in place, no free/no call_rcu, so the stack VMA is safe), and asserts start/end/file_off/file_len all moved consistently.  `[mm_vma_trim] PASS (front-munmap advances file+shmem backing)`.  The change is effectively INERT at boot (a boot-time front-munmap of a file/shmem mapping followed by a re-fault is not on the boot path), so the selftest -- not the boot -- is the real proof; verified the boot is unaffected.  Clean boot FIRST try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 64 selftests PASSED incl. `[mm_vma_trim] PASS` and `[mmap_range_test]`/`[access_ok_test]` (the neighbouring mm tests, unaffected), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` renders.  This closes fan-out #4 candidate (cc) -- and with (bb) F91 / (dd) F92 / (ee) F93 / (cc) F94 all shipped, ALL of fan-out #4 is now resolved.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.

- 2026-06-26 - F95 FIXED: closing an inet socket freed the socket's vfs_file_t SYNCHRONOUSLY (sock_close kfree(self), kernel/net/socket.c) while a concurrent TCP pcb_wake / UDP sock_poll_wake reader -- running inside rcu_read_lock -- could still load that file via the pcb/socket backpointer and WRITE through f->waitq -> cross-CPU use-after-free write into freed heap (fan-out #5 candidate (gg)).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): pcb_wake (tcp.c:213-215) loads pcb->sock_file then wait_queue_wake_all(f->waitq) (which does __atomic_exchange_n(&wq->head,...) = a WRITE) from tcp_recv (rcu 366-533) / tcp_timer_tick (rcu 544-590); sock_close (socket.c) does tcp_pcb_set_file(NULL) (a plain store) + tcp_pcb_free (RCU-deferred) + call_rcu_expedited(sock_free_rcu, s) (s RCU-deferred) but then kfree(self) -- the vfs_file_t -- SYNCHRONOUSLY; only s and the pcb were deferred, NOT the file.  A reader that loaded sock_file just before the NULL store holds a dangling f and writes f->waitq after the kfree.  KEY DISCOVERY (verify-all-angles): the UDP path is the SAME class -- sock_poll_wake (socket.c:140) writes s->file->waitq from socket_deliver_udp's rcu_read_lock, and s->file is the very vfs_file_t (s->file=f at socket_open:303) freed by the same kfree(self), so ONE fix covers tcp AND udp.  And the fix is the EXISTING AF_UNIX discipline the inet path missed: unix_sock_free_rcu (unix_sock.c:371) already frees s->file in its grace-period callback for exactly this poll-wake-UAF reason.  FIX (do-it-right, ONE shared mechanism mirroring AF_UNIX, same family as F88/F89 RCU-defer-the-free): (1) sock_free_rcu now frees s->file (== self) in the SAME grace period; (2) sock_close's main path no longer kfree's self synchronously (the `if (!s)` early-return, which has no RCU reader holding the file, still frees synchronously -- safe); (3) tcp_pcb_set_file is now a __ATOMIC_RELEASE store and pcb_wake's sock_file load an __ATOMIC_ACQUIRE load, so a reader observes either the file (covered by the file's grace period) or NULL (skips the wake).  UDP needs no extra ordering: s->file is immutable after open and s is unpublished from the udp_table (udp_table_remove) before the deferred free, so a reader holding s under RCU keeps s and s->file alive.  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU RX-vs-close UAF, not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (the file is now reclaimed ONLY via the grace period the pcb_wake/sock_poll_wake readers run inside, identical to F88/F89 and the AF_UNIX precedent) + a DETERMINISTIC invariant selftest (sock_file_lifetime_selftest: opens an inet DGRAM socket, asserts s->file==f / f->ctx==s / type -- the backpointer the dual free relies on -- then closes it through the deferred path; catches a double-free/leak regression) + the close path is HEAVILY boot-exercised (DHCP uses UDP sockets open/close, so sock_close/sock_free_rcu run on the boot path -- a genuine exercise, not inert).  Clean boot FIRST try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 65 selftests PASSED incl. `[sock_file_life] PASS` AND `[socketpair]`/`[scm_rights]`/`[unix_refcount]`/`[tcp_orphan]` (the neighbouring socket tests, unaffected), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` renders.  This closes fan-out #5 candidate (gg).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F96 FIXED: ext2_rename's dst-removal freed the destination inode UNCONDITIONALLY -- free_inode_blocks + i_links_count = 0 + free_inode_num with NO read of the current link count (kernel/fs/ext2.c ~3062-3068) -- so renaming over a multi-link regular file destroyed a still-referenced inode: the surviving hard link then pointed at a freed/reissued inode (cross-link disclosure / on-disk-inode use-after-free).  Plus a secondary runtime double-free: rename's dir_remove_entry was UNCHECKED while ext2_unlink CHECKS it, so a concurrent unlink(dst) racing rename(*,dst) on a single-link file could both reach free_inode_num(dst_ino) (fan-out #5 candidate (ii)).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): the dst-removal branch sets links_count=0 + frees with no count read, in direct contrast to ext2_unlink (~2980-2991) which decrements then frees ONLY at 0; i_links_count is uint16_t (ext2.h:81); sys_link returns -EPERM (so a 2-link file can only come from a crafted/corrupt image, the stated threat model); the directory-dst case is rejected earlier (rename over a dir returns 0 at ~3050-3054) so only a regular-file dst reaches the free (no "."/".." link accounting needed).  CONFIRMED the secondary race -- rename's dir_remove_entry (~3060) was unchecked while ext2_unlink checks it (~2976), so whoever removes the dirent should own the single free, but rename freed regardless -> double-free of the inode bit + blocks when racing unlink on a single-link file (runtime-reachable, no crafted image).  FIX (do-it-right, ONE shared mechanism so the two paths cannot drift again): extracted a PURE ext2_link_drop(uint16_t* links) (decrement with a `> 0` underflow guard, returns 1 iff the count reached 0) and a shared ext2_drop_link_locked(leaf, ino) (the count-aware free tail that frees inode + blocks only at 0, always consuming the inode lock); ext2_unlink now calls it, and ext2_rename's dst-removal calls it too but GATED on dir_remove_entry succeeding -- if a racing unlink already removed the name, rename skips the drop (that path owns the free), closing the double-free without a coarser lock (the dir_remove_entry success is the single ownership token ext2_unlink already relied on).  The old unconditional free_inode_num (which ran even when inode_lock failed) is gone -- on a re-lock failure rename now leaks rather than wrongly freeing, matching ext2_unlink.  VERIFICATION: the primary multi-link case needs a crafted image (cannot be created at runtime -- sys_link EPERM), so it is not end-to-end testable at boot -> a DETERMINISTIC unit test of the core decision (ext2_link_drop_selftest: 2->1 keep, 1->0 free, 3->2->1->0, and an underflow drop-at-0 that stays 0 and reports free) + code-proof of the wiring + the rename/unlink paths are boot-exercised (the build writes/moves files, bash/login touch the fs).  `[ext2_link_drop] PASS (free only at links==0, no u16 underflow)`.  Clean boot FIRST try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 66 selftests PASSED incl. `[ext2_link_drop]` AND `[rename_under]` / `[ext2_dotdot]` (the neighbouring rename/dir tests, unaffected), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` renders.  This closes fan-out #5 candidate (ii).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F97 FIXED: sys_exec freed the old PML4 hierarchy (vmm_free_user_ex + pmm_buddy_free, kernel/syscall/syscall.c) without terminating sibling THREAD_SHARE_MM threads that were still running user code on other CPUs with CR3 == old_pml4 -- so after the free those CPUs' page-table walkers walked FREED PT/PD/PDPT pages and their TLBs cached WRITABLE entries for freed leaf frames the buddy allocator immediately recycled -> cross-domain write / disclosure, an unprivileged LPE reachable by any clone(THREAD_SHARE_MM)+execve race (fan-out #5 candidate (ff)).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): the commit block (~1072-1081) does the in-place swap (mm_shared->pml4_phys = new_pml4) + vmm_switch (CURRENT CPU's CR3 only) + free of old_pml4, with NO sibling-kill and NO tlb_flush_mm shootdown (its comment reasons only about the single-threaded current-CPU case); sys_thread + THREAD_SHARE_MM (~1458) shares the SAME task_mm_t and bumps refs to 2; the clone-without-share path (~1474) and fork (~550) DO tlb_flush_mm -- exec was the unique mm-teardown path that frees page tables without quiescing other CPUs.  KEY REFINEMENT (the recorded "spin until mm_shared->refs == 1" is UNSAFE): a killed sibling drops its mm ref only in task_free_rcu (process.c:382), AFTER an RCU grace period, so g_current spinning on refs==1 inside the exec syscall could stall that grace period and DEADLOCK -- the fix must NOT wait.  Also: even a tlb_flush_mm shootdown alone would be insufficient, because the sibling's CR3 register itself points at the freed PML4 (the threads must actually be gone, not just have stale TLBs).  FIX (do-it-right, ONE shared mechanism, additive + zero-risk to the proven boot-critical common path): keep the sole-owner (refs==1) in-place-swap + direct-free path UNCHANGED (every boot exec is single-threaded, so that path is untouched and still exercised on every program launch); for a SHARED mm (refs > 1) detach g_current onto a FRESH task_mm_t (task_mm_alloc(new_pml4, new_mm)), SIGKILL the thread group via signal_send_group (then clear g_current's OWN pending SIGKILL with an atomic and-fetch, since sig_group_visit also targets the caller), point g_current at the fresh mm, vmm_switch, and task_mm_release the OLD shared mm -- which does NOT free old_pml4 here (siblings still hold refs) but lets task_mm_release free it once the last SIGKILL'd sibling exits (refs -> 0).  So old_pml4 stays live while any sibling references it: no UAF, no spin, no deadlock, reusing the existing refcount-based free path.  RESIDUAL (correctness only, not safety; recorded in docs/SCALABILITY_DEBT.md): tgid/leader identity is left unchanged, so the rare NON-leader execve leaves a tgid pointing at the reaped old leader instead of performing the full POSIX de_thread leader-switch -- benign (no UAF; the surviving thread runs the new image), the proper fix needs tgid-index re-key + child-list/waitpid reparenting.  VERIFICATION: the refs>1 branch is INERT at boot (all boot execs are single-threaded) so not end-to-end testable there -> a DETERMINISTIC threshold selftest (exec_mm_teardown_selftest: ONLY refs==1 frees in place; refs 2/8/0 take the detach path) + rigorous code-proof + a clean boot that exercises the UNCHANGED sole-owner path on EVERY program launch (init/login/bash/net all execve, so reaching login proves it).  `[exec_mm] PASS (only sole-owner frees old pml4 in place)`.  Clean boot FIRST try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 67 selftests PASSED incl. `[exec_mm]` and the neighbouring `[task_exit_state]` / `[signal_send_pid]`, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` renders.  (The session scratchpad had been wiped mid-turn, so the boot harness -- bootclean.sh / shot.py / OVMF_VARS.fd -- was recreated from build.sh's canonical QEMU invocation before verifying.)  This closes fan-out #5 candidate (ff).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F98 FIXED: virtio-net validated the device-supplied RX completion id against the full ring size (virtio_desc_id_valid = index_ok(id, VIRTQ_SIZE=256)) but only VIRTQ_SIZE/2=128 RX buffers are ever allocated and posted, so a device-written id in [128,255] passed the check and indexed an UNINITIALIZED s_rx_bufs[] slot ({phys=0, virt=NULL}) -> raw=NULL memcpy source (a NULL-base read of attacker length) AND a descriptor re-posted with addr=0 (letting the device DMA-clobber physical frame 0) -- a malicious/buggy-device memory-safety bug (fan-out #5 candidate (hh); kernel/net/virtio_net.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): virtio_desc_id_valid (virtio_net.c:303) bounds against VIRTQ_SIZE while the RX alloc loop (~583) and refill loop (~336) both run i < VIRTQ_SIZE/2, leaving s_rx_bufs[128..255] = {0, NULL}; rx_poll (~434) gated on the full-ring guard then used s_rx_bufs[desc_id].virt as the memcpy source (~450) and .phys as a re-posted descriptor addr (~454).  REFINED the prescription (verify-all-angles): do NOT change the generic virtio_desc_id_valid -- its other callers, virtq_submit (307) and the TX completion (409), operate over the FULL 256-entry desc ring, so 256 is the correct bound for them; only the RX path is tighter because its id also indexes the 128-populated s_rx_bufs[].  Also confirmed WHY the RX id maps to s_rx_bufs[id]: rxq_refill pairs descriptor idx with buffer i and the sequential free list makes the posted RX desc ids exactly 0..127, so a legitimate completion id equals its buffer index.  FIX (do-it-right, ONE source of truth, mirrors the virtio_descid/nvme_cid bounding primitive): added VIRTQ_NUM_RX_BUFS (= VIRTQ_SIZE/2) in virtio_net.h, used by the RX alloc loop, the refill loop, AND a new RX-specific virtio_rx_id_valid(id) = index_ok(id, VIRTQ_NUM_RX_BUFS) that rx_poll now uses in place of the generic full-ring guard -- so the validation bound and the populated-buffer count can never drift apart again; the generic virtio_desc_id_valid stays 256 for TX/submit.  Fixed the misleading "VIRTQ_SIZE buffers" comments (only VIRTQ_SIZE/2 were ever populated).  VERIFICATION: a malicious-DEVICE threat NOT triggerable by QEMU's benign NIC -> a DETERMINISTIC bounds selftest (virtio_rx_id_valid_selftest: ids 0 and 127 valid; 128 and 255 -- in the desc ring but past the rx buffers -- REJECTED; 256 and garbage rejected) + the normal RX path IS boot-exercised (DHCP receives through rx_poll with legit ids 0..127), so a clean boot with a DHCP lease proves the bound change did not break normal receive.  `[virtio_rxid] SELF-TEST PASSED (rx-completion id bounded to populated buffers)`.  Clean boot FIRST try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 68 selftests PASSED incl. `[virtio_rxid]` AND the neighbouring `[virtio_descid]` / `[nvme_cid]` (unaffected), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` renders.  This closes fan-out #5 candidate (hh) -- and with futex SAFE + (gg) F95 / (ii) F96 / (ff) F97 / (hh) F98 all shipped, ALL of fan-out #5 is now resolved. - 2026-06-26 - F99 FIXED: vmm_get_user_pages' copy-on-write break swapped the PTE to a freshly-copied frame (*pte = nf) and dropped the old frame's ref with only a LOCAL invlpg and NO cross-CPU TLB shootdown (kernel/mm/vmm.c ~302-315), so a sibling thread sharing the address space (THREAD_SHARE_MM) on another CPU kept a stale (old_phys, RO) TLB entry; once pmm_ref_dec dropped old_phys and the CoW co-owner (fork peer) later freed + recycled it, the sibling read old_phys through its stale TLB = cross-process use-after-free READ / info leak (benign variant: stale pre-DMA bytes = silent corruption) -- the same sibling-stale-TLB class as F97/brk/munmap, at the GUP/DMA-pin CoW-break site (fan-out #6 candidate (jj)).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): the break does *pte = nf + invlpg(va) (local) + pmm_ref_dec(phys) under lock_mm->vma_lock with no tlb_flush_range, while the OTHER two CoW-break sites DO shoot down -- isr14_page_fault (~720-752) records flush_page under the lock, UNLOCKS, then tlb_flush_range(task_get_mm_shared(g_current), ...) with an explicit IPI-ack-deadlock comment, and fork uses tlb_flush_mm (process.c ~551); confirmed REACHABILITY -- vmm_get_user_pages is called by ahci_read_user (ahci.c:893), the AHCI read/pread DMA-pin path, so a user read into a fork-CoW page hits the break.  FIX (do-it-right, mirror the EXISTING isr14/fork shootdown discipline -- ONE shared mechanism applied to the missed site, BATCHED for scalability per the prime directive): set a cow_broke flag in the CoW-break branch; converted the function's three early returns + the normal return to a single `out:` exit returning `ret`; and at out: -- AFTER every per-page vma_lock is released (never hold a lock across the IPI wait, the isr14 deadlock rule) -- if cow_broke, do ONE tlb_flush_range(task_get_mm_shared(g_current), uaddr&~0xFFF, uaddr&~0xFFF + count*PAGE_SIZE) covering the whole pinned span (one IPI round for all swapped pages rather than N).  The rc==1 widen-only branch sets no flag (a stale RO entry just re-faults harmlessly); the local invlpg(va) stays for immediate local consistency; over-flushing the non-CoW pages in the span is safe.  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU stale-TLB race, NOT deterministically reproducible -> rigorous code-proof (identical to the isr14 shootdown the codebase already trusts) + the function is boot-exercised on every AHCI DMA-pin read (file loads / demand paging), so a clean boot proves the early-return restructure did not break the pin / DMA / demand-paging path (the cow_broke flush is gated and mostly inert at boot, like F97).  No bespoke selftest: the flush-range arithmetic is trivial and a true cross-CPU race is not deterministic -- same honest proof method as F97/F95/F89.  Clean boot FIRST try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 68 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], `More login:` renders.  This closes fan-out #6 candidate (jj). FIX (do-it-right, mirror sys_stat exactly -- ONE shared mechanism, no drift): inserted `if (!unveil_ok(path, UNVEIL_READ)) { kfree(kbuf); kfree(path); return -ENOENT; }` immediately after fs_lookup, BEFORE the fsr check and BEFORE the is_virtual dispatch, so it covers ext2 AND /proc AND /dev uniformly and makes an unveiled-out directory indistinguishable from a missing one; both kmalloc'd buffers are freed on the deny path. - 2026-06-26 - F101 FIXED: build_prdt (kernel/drivers/storage/ahci.c) built its PRDT with an unbounded `while (bytes > 0)` loop -- unlike its three sibling builders (do_rw_direct / ahci_submit_hhdm use nprdt<248 + fail-on-remainder; build_prdt_pages bounded by npages<=130) -- so a bytes value larger than 248 page-spans would OOB-write past prdt[247] off the end of the 4KiB cmd_table_t (fan-out #6 candidate (ll); defense-in-depth -- LOW because the sole caller ahci_read_multi passes PAGE_SIZE = one entry and ahci_read_multi itself has zero callers, i.e. dead code, so it is NOT currently reachable). FIX (do-it-right, mirror the siblings' discipline): bounded the loop `while (bytes > 0 && n < 248u)` so it can never write past prdt[247], and added `if (bytes) return 0` to signal overflow -- the documented "caller must treat 0 as too-fragmented and fail" contract, exactly like ahci_submit_hhdm's fail-on-remainder.  Left ahci_read_multi unchanged: it passes PAGE_SIZE so it always gets 1 entry and can never see the 0 return, and wiring a slot-freeing overflow path into the dead caller would entangle slot management for an unreachable branch (the helper's return-0 contract is documented for any future large-bytes caller). The fix is in DEAD code so it is inert at boot; the clean boot just confirms nothing else broke. - 2026-06-26 - F102 FIXED: closing an epoll fd freed the epoll_state_t, its slot table, and the epoll vfs_file_t SYNCHRONOUSLY while a watched fd's IRQ-context wake callback could still dereference them -> cross-CPU use-after-free with a controllable indirect call through a freed wait-queue chain, an unprivileged local escalation (fan-out #7 candidate (pp); kernel/syscall/syscall.c + kernel/wait.c). Verified the no-watches case, the watched-fd-closed-first case (the w->file vfs_tryget pin keeps the watched waitq alive until unregister, so no dangling ewe -- unchanged), and that call_rcu_expedited manages its own node (no embedded rcu_head needed, like epoll_watch_free_rcu). - 2026-06-26 - F103 FIXED: the ext2 read fast path warmed the SHARED cross-process block cache from the USER buffer, letting a process poison cached on-disk blocks with arbitrary bytes (fan-out #7 candidate (mm); kernel/fs/ext2.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): ext2_vfs_read (~1263-1275) and ext2_vfs_pread (~1356-1366) compute is_user = (dest < HHDM_OFFSET) and gate the DMA on it (ahci_read_user zero-copy into the user pages vs ahci_read into a trusted HHDM staging buffer), but the cache-warm loop bcache_fill(phys_blk+i, dest+i*s_block_size, s_block_size) ran UNCONDITIONALLY, copying from the user `dest` into the shared static cache slot tagged by the physical block; ahci_read_user unpins the user frames before returning, so a sibling thread (shared mm) can overwrite `dest` between the DMA and the bcache_fill memcpy -> the shared cache slot for phys_blk holds attacker bytes, served to any later bcache_get(phys_blk) reader of that on-disk block of the same file (cross-process cache poisoning / integrity bypass -- e.g. forging what a privileged daemon's read() observes; secondary: a racing munmap faults the memcpy on a user VA in kernel mode).  The kernel-read path (ELF loader / demand paging, is_user==0, trusted staging buffer) is the path that actually benefits from the warm and is unaffected.  FIX (do-it-right, mirror the codebase's own ahci_read (trusted) vs ahci_read_user (untrusted) split): guard BOTH cache-warm loops with `if (!is_user)` so the SHARED cache is only ever populated from a trusted kernel source; the user-read path forgoes the opportunistic warm (a later read cold-misses and re-fills from disk -- correct by construction), and the data returned on the fast path is unchanged (only the cache SIDE-EFFECT is gated).  VERIFICATION: a one-line correctness gate -> code-proof + the read/pread path and the block cache are HEAVILY boot-exercised (login/bash/net read files; [dcache_test]/[dcache_race]/[ext2_*] selftests exercise the cache + the demand-paging warm), so a clean boot proves gating the user-path warm did not break reads or the kernel-path cache. - 2026-06-26 - F104 FIXED: closing a pty slave while the master stayed open freed the shared slave vfs_file_t but left pty->slave_file dangling, so reopening /dev/pts/N resurrected the freed object (a raw refcount bump on freed slab) and installed it as a live fd -> use-after-free (read/write/ioctl/poll on freed memory + a later close drives slave_open_count negative) (fan-out #7 candidate (oo); kernel/drivers/tty/pty.c). - 2026-06-26 - F105 FIXED: io_uring's SQ consumer was unserialised -- enter() consumed a SQPOLL ring's SQ concurrently with the poller kthread, and io_wq_ensure_worker could spawn two workers, orphaning one -> double-execution/double-completion + a cross-CPU use-after-free of the freed ring through the orphaned worker (fan-out #7 candidate (qq); kernel/io/io_uring.c). REFINED the fix (no-assumptions): separated the memory-safety bugs from the correctness bug, because IORING_OP_WRITE is sync-dispatched and blocks on disk I/O -- a submit-lock held across dispatch would be a sleep-under-spinlock.  FIX (do-it-right, low-risk): (a) enter() now NEVER consumes a SQPOLL ring regardless of flags (`if (uring->sqp_task) { wake poller if asked; goto getevents; }`), so the poller is the SOLE SQ consumer -- closing the SQPOLL double-consume and its orphaned-worker UAF with no lock; (b) added a per-ring worker_lock (documented in docs/LOCKS.md) and made io_wq_ensure_worker double-checked-locked (lock-free acquire-load fast path, re-check + create + publish under the lock) so AT MOST ONE worker is ever spawned -- closing the orphaned-worker UAF for EVERY consumer-race path including concurrent non-SQPOLL enters; the lock is held only on the first async op and across task_create_kthread + sched_add (neither sleeps nor takes it -> no sleep-under-spinlock, no cycle).  The remaining NON-SQPOLL concurrent-enter DOUBLE-EXECUTION (two threads sharing the ring fd both running the consumer -> a duplicate op + CQE) is correctness-only (the orphan UAF is closed, no memory corruption) and is recorded as a follow-up in docs/SCALABILITY_DEBT.md (its proper fix needs copy-SQE-then-dispatch-outside-the-lock to avoid holding a spinlock across a blocking WRITE).  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU race, not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof + the existing `[io_uring_test]` (create -> NOP batch + 100-round steady-state enter/dispatch/complete -> close) and `[io_ring_idx]` selftests both PASS (submit/complete path unbroken) + a clean boot. This closes fan-out #7 candidate (qq).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F106 FIXED: the tty line discipline read tty->termios lock-free while TCSETS/TCSETSW/TCSETSF wrote the WHOLE struct into it with no lock, so a reader on another CPU could observe a half-updated termios -- a new c_lflag (ICANON/ISIG) paired with an old c_cc[] byte -> a swallowed ^C, a spurious SIGINT/SIGTSTP/SIGQUIT to the foreground pgrp, or a line drained in the wrong mode (fan-out #7 candidate (nn), the LAST fan-out #7 item; kernel/drivers/tty/{tty.c,pty.c}, kernel/syscall/syscall.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): all THREE writer sites copy_from_user STRAIGHT into the live tty->termios with NO lock -- pty_tty_ioctl_common's TCSETS/W/F (pty.c:471, the single shared master+slave ioctl path) and the /dev/tty fallback's TCSETS/W (syscall.c:4374) and TCSETSF (4377); the readers run lock-free on another CPU -- tty_input_char snapshots c_lflag + c_cc at entry then reads c_iflag (tty.c:147/148/225/237) to decide ISIG signals / canonical mode / ICRNL, and tty_ldisc_drain reads c_lflag + c_cc[VMIN] (tty.c:265/266) BEFORE it takes tty->lock; tty->lock is preempt_disable + spin_lock (so copy_from_user, which can fault, must NOT run under it); every c_cc index used (VINTR=0, VQUIT=1, VMIN=6, VSUSP=10) is a constant < NCCS=19 and the struct holds no pointers -> a torn read mis-decides a signal/mode but cannot corrupt memory: data race, MEDIUM, confirmed.  tty.h's lock comment deliberately scopes tty->lock to the read ring + canonical line and EXCLUDES termios, so this is a NEW gap (not covered by F84/F85).  REFINED the recorded fix (no-assumptions): (1) publishing the user copy under tty->lock is NOT sufficient on its own -- `tty->termios = tmp` is itself a multi-word copy, so a lock-free reader could STILL catch it mid-assignment; BOTH ends must take the lock. FIX (do-it-right, ONE shared mechanism): extracted a PRIMITIVE in tty.c -- tty_set_termios(tty, *src) publishes the whole struct under tty->lock, tty_get_termios(tty, *dst) snapshots it under the same lock; copy_from_user / copy_to_user always run on a stack-local termios_t OUTSIDE the lock (it can fault).  All three TCSET* sites now land the user copy in a stack tmp then publish via tty_set_termios (and TCSETSF flushes only AFTER a successful set -- the syscall.c path previously flushed even on -EFAULT, now consistent with the pty path); tty_input_char takes ONE consistent snapshot at entry via tty_get_termios and reads every termios field from it; both TCGETS sites snapshot through tty_get_termios then copy out; tty_ldisc_drain moved its ICANON/VMIN reads INSIDE its existing lock region (reuses the acquisition it already needs -> zero added lock cost).  The output-path single-field reads (c_oflag OPOST/ONLCR, c_lflag TOSTOP in the write/echo paths) intentionally STAY lock-free: each is an atomic single-field load with no cross-field signal/safety dependency, and they sit on the hot output path where a lock would cost more than the benign one-character cosmetic glitch a mode-change instant could cause.  VERIFICATION: the cross-CPU tear is a code-proof (both ends now hold tty->lock), backed by a NEW deterministic selftest tty_termios_snapshot_selftest -- publishes a fully-populated termios and asserts the snapshot matches BYTE-FOR-BYTE (hand-rolled compare, no __builtin_memcmp), republishes a different one and asserts NO field survives (full overwrite), then drives tty_input_char + tty_ldisc_drain in canonical-then-raw mode set via tty_set_termios and asserts the discipline OBEYS the published mode (a missing/recursive unlock in the primitive would also hang here under preempt-disable and never print PASSED); plus the tty/pty path is heavily boot-exercised (login + bash + foot set termios via TCSETS and read input through the ldisc), so a clean boot proves canonical/raw input still works.  `[tty_termios] SELF-TEST PASSED (publish/snapshot consistent, ldisc obeys published mode)`. - 2026-06-26 - F107 FIXED: the fatal-signal terminate path dropped a process's fd table in the WRONG order -- it called task_files_release(g_current->files_shared) and only THEN set g_current->files_shared = NULL (a plain store) -- so the RCU-deferred fd-table free could race a /proc/<pid>/fd reader on another CPU and hand it freed memory: a cross-process use-after-free (BUG-TYPE SCAN #1, the sync-free-under-reader / F88/F95/F102 class; kernel/proc/signal.c, the fix lands in kernel/proc/process.c + .h, kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/main.c).  FOUND by sweeping the whole tree (4 parallel read-only agents over net / fs+vfs / drivers / mm+proc-io) for that ONE bug type; this was the ONLY real gap -- every other shared-object free is already RCU-deferred / refcount-pinned / unlinked-under-the-waker's-lock (audited-clean list in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #1).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): (a) task_files_release (process.c:129) decrements refs and, on 1->0, closes the fds synchronously then call_rcu_expedited(task_files_free_rcu, f); call_rcu_expedited (rcu.c:245) is `synchronize_rcu_expedited(); func(data);` so it runs the grace period and FREES THE TABLE INLINE before returning -- while the signal path still had files_shared published.  (b) The /proc/<pid>/fd reader (proc.c:290-298 fd-open, :306-310 fd-readdir, :567-600 fd/<n> stat) does rcu_read_lock(); tf = __atomic_load_acquire(&t->files_shared); ft = tf ? load_acquire(&tf->ft) : NULL; f = vfs_tryget(load(&ft->fd_table[n])) -- its own comment states it is safe ONLY because task_files_release RCU-defers the free AFTER the caller unpublishes.  (c) The dying task is still in pid_ht (task_set_exit_state, which makes it reapable, runs later at signal.c:460), so sched_find_pid finds it.  WINDOW: synchronize_rcu_expedited inside task_files_release waits out only readers that ALREADY entered rcu_read_lock; a reader that opens its rcu_read_lock section AFTER the grace period but BEFORE the (post-free) `= NULL` loads the freed task_files_t, derefs tf->ft / ft->fd_table[n] (freed slab) and vfs_tryget's a freed vfs_file_t (freed vtable -- a controllable indirect call).  Reachable cross-process by any unprivileged `ps` / `ls /proc/<pid>/fd` racing any fatal SIG_DFL exit (SIGSEGV crash, SIGKILL, SIGTERM) of a process whose fd table hits refcount 0 (the common single-threaded-process case).  The sibling sys_exit path (syscall.c:727) ALREADY did it correctly -- unpublish with a RELEASE store BEFORE task_files_release -- with a comment naming this exact contract; the two paths had DRIFTED, which IS the bug.  FIX (do-it-right + the always-on primitive directive -- the two paths already drifted, so make drift impossible): extracted task_drop_files(task_t*) (PRIMITIVE in process.c, declared in process.h) -- it snapshots files_shared, stores NULL with __ATOMIC_RELEASE FIRST, then task_files_release -- and routed BOTH the sys_exit block and the fatal-signal block through it, so the unpublish-before-release order is now a single source of truth that cannot drift again.  verify-all-angles: when refs>1 (a sharing thread still alive) task_files_release only decrements and the unpublish is harmless; only the last reference frees, which is exactly the case the reordering protects; the RELEASE store pairs with the reader's ACQUIRE load (the old plain store did not).  VERIFICATION: the cross-CPU UAF is a code-proof (unpublish now strictly precedes the inline grace period on BOTH paths), backed by a NEW deterministic selftest task_files_drop_selftest -- builds a table with refs==2 so the release inside task_drop_files only DECREMENTS (no inline grace period / no fd-close of a fake table), then asserts the caller's files_shared is NULLed AND the table was released exactly once (refs==1); plus EVERY process exit (normal + signal-killed) routes through task_drop_files, so a clean multi-process boot (login, shells, the selftest-spawned tasks) exercises both paths.  `[task_drop_files] PASS (unpublish-before-release, table released once)`. - 2026-06-26 - F108 HARDENING (BUG-TYPE SCAN #2, sibling-stale-TLB-after-PTE-change -- the F97/F99 class): the whole-tree sweep (4 parallel read-only agents over vmm munmap/mprotect, CoW/fault, teardown/reclaim/shmem, kernel-side remaps) found NO ACTIVE GAP -- every PTE clear/downgrade of an mm that can be live on another CPU is already paired with an all-CPU tlb_flush_range/tlb_flush_mm run OUTSIDE the mm lock BEFORE the frame is freed (munmap mm_unmap_range_flush_free, CoW break F99 batched/single-page flush, fork/sys_thread write-protect tlb_flush_mm, io_uring teardown, kstack tlb_flush_kernel_range), OR runs under a no-live-sibling precondition (vmm_free_user_ex only at refs==0; sole-owner exec after vmm_switch; multithreaded exec detaches onto a FRESH mm and refcount-frees the old one later, clearing no live PTE), OR is metadata-only (mm_vma_remove, front-trim), OR drops only an object's refcount on a frame still pinned by another mapper's PTE ref (shmem/pcache/DRM). The shootdown is already primitised (tlb_flush_range/tlb_flush_mm/tlb_flush_kernel_range), so there was nothing new to extract. FIX (the one useful, non-invented thing the sweep surfaced -- a LATENT FRAGILITY, not an active bug): kernel/proc/sched.c do_switch updated the per-mm cpu_mask by clearing prev's bit then setting next's bit UNCONDITIONALLY. For a same-mm thread switch (prev->mm_shared == next->mm_shared, two THREAD_SHARE_MM threads sharing one task_mm_t) that nets to a no-op but opens a transient window in which THIS CPU's bit reads 0 while CR3 still points at the mm -- a concurrent tlb_flush_mm on a sibling could read the cpumask in that window and SKIP this CPU, leaving it with a stale TLB entry. INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED (no-assumptions): it is CURRENTLY SAFE only because context_switch (process_ctx_switch.asm:62-66) ALWAYS reloads CR3 when pml4_phys != 0 (`test rdx,rdx / jz .skip_cr3 / mov cr3,rdx` -- it keys ONLY on pml4_phys==0, never on prev-vs-next mm), and a mov-to-cr3 is a full flush since the kernel uses no global pages (PAGE_GLOBAL defined but unused), so this CPU's stale entries are gone before it runs any user code -- AND the do_switch comment FALSELY claimed "context_switch will skip the CR3 write" for same-mm switches, which would invite a future optimization (the Linux skip-same-mm-CR3 behavior) that turns the window into a real sibling-stale-TLB write-after-free. ROOT FIX (do-it-right, make the illegal state unrepresentable): update the cpumask ONLY when the address space actually changes (`if (prev->mm_shared != next->mm_shared)`), so a same-mm thread switch leaves the bit SET throughout -- strictly conservative (this CPU never drops out of its own running mm's shootdown set, so a concurrent tlb_flush_mm can only over-target it, never miss it), the transient-0 window is GONE, and two atomic RMW cpumask ops are saved on the hot thread-switch path; plus rewrote the stale comment to state the true mechanism (context_switch reloads CR3 whenever pml4_phys != 0; the different-mm clear..reload window is covered by that imminent full flush; the same-mm safety now comes from NOT clearing the bit) and to warn that the skip-when-equal guard is what keeps the mask correct if context_switch is ever changed to skip same-mm reloads. verify-all-angles: the different-mm path is byte-for-byte unchanged (existing Dekker/SEQ_CST barrier reasoning intact); for same-mm the bit only ever stays set (cannot cause a missed shootdown, only a redundant IPI for an mm this CPU genuinely runs); kthread switches still skip via the `&& ->mm` guards. VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU scheduler race, not deterministically reproducible in a unit test (a token cpumask-atomics test would not prove the real property), so a code-proof (strict conservatism) + the heavy live-SMP exercise: a clean first-boot with the chaselev work-stealing-deque stress (N=20000, thieves=3, pushed=20000 found=20000 missing=0 duplicates=0) PASSED plus all 73 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2, `More login:` renders. Out-of-class observations logged in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #2 for later scans (the vmm_clone_user_ex intra-walk RW->RO CoW-isolation window; the unlocked s_mmio_next VA-allocator data race; the dead vmm_page_free local-only-flush). This closes BUG-TYPE SCAN #2 (no active gap; one latent landmine hardened). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F109 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #3, unvalidated-user-pointer -> arbitrary-kernel-RW, the LPE class): six syscalls dereferenced a user-supplied pointer DIRECTLY -- a raw store/read of *(T*)uptr -- instead of routing through copy_from_user/copy_to_user, so a kernel/non-canonical/unmapped pointer was an arbitrary kernel write (LPE), a kernel read (info leak/oracle), or a #PF panic (DoS); all unprivileged, all in kernel/syscall/syscall.c. FOUND by sweeping the WHOLE user->kernel pointer surface with 4 parallel read-only agents (driver ioctls; net syscalls; core syscalls; io_uring+ipc): the driver ioctls (DRM/evdev/pty incl. every nested user sub-pointer), io_uring SQE addresses, sendmsg/recvmsg iovec path, futex user-word, and the rest are ALL already on copy_*_user (audited-clean) -- these six core syscalls were the stragglers. FIX (do-it-right, ONE shared mechanism -- the existing primitive, never a hand-rolled access_ok): route every one through copy_from_user / copy_to_user (which _access_ok-reject kernel/non-canonical/overflow pointers and prefault). sys_wait builds the status in a kernel local and copy_to_user's it AFTER process_destroy (the zombie is already committed-reaped by sched_reap_zombie, so a bad pointer must not leave it unreaped+leaked) -> -EFAULT. sys_pipe copy_to_user's the {rfd,wfd} pair and, mirroring socketpair, sys_close's BOTH installed fds on a copyout failure so it no longer leaks them. sys_fb_info fills a memset-zeroed kernel struct (the memset also stops uninitialized stack padding from leaking) and copy_to_user's it. sys_nanosleep copy_from_user's the timespec into a kernel local then validates/uses the COPY (no TOCTOU). sys_shm_open/unlink copy_from_user the name (namelen already bounded). verify-all-angles: a kernel-HHDM / non-canonical / past-user-ceiling pointer now returns -EFAULT instead of touching it; no uninitialized leak (fb_info memset); no fd leak (pipe rollback); the copies are single-shot into kernel buffers so there is no check-then-deref TOCTOU. VERIFICATION: a NEW deterministic selftest syscall_user_ptr_selftest drives the four side-effect-free handlers (sys_fb_info/sys_nanosleep/sys_shm_open/sys_shm_unlink) with a kernel-HHDM, a non-canonical, and a past-user-ceiling pointer and asserts -EFAULT (never a touch); sys_wait + sys_pipe are covered by the heavy boot exercise (every shell pipeline calls pipe(), every login/svcmgr child reap hits the wait status path) plus the code-proof, rather than churning fd/zombie state in the test. `[user_ptr_test] SELF-TEST PASSED (raw user-ptr syscalls reject bad pointers)`. - 2026-06-26 - F110 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #3 net-layer pair, finishing the unvalidated-user-pointer class): two socket-syscall paths dereferenced a user pointer without validation -- a #PF/#GP DoS (and a 1-bit kernel-read oracle) -- the lower-severity stragglers the SCAN #3 sweep recorded after F109 closed the six syscall.c gaps. FIX (do-it-right, the existing primitive + one new extracted helper, never a hand-rolled access_ok): (A) sys_setsockopt now bounces optval into a 128-byte kernel buffer via copy_from_user (rejects vallen > 128 with -EINVAL; declared the buffer before the is_unix_sock goto so it cannot jump over an initializer) and passes the COPY to socket_setsockopt, so no option handler ever derefs the raw user pointer; (B) extracted copy_sockaddr_un_from_user (PRIMITIVE, syscall.c) which copy_from_user's the whole sockaddr into a kernel sockaddr_un and FORCE-NUL-caps sun_path[sizeof-1]='\0', and routed all three AF_UNIX sites through it so every downstream walk (debug print + namespace hash/compare) is over a bounded kernel string; additionally capped ns_hash_str/ns_streq at UNIX_PATH_MAX so they are safe-by-construction even against a future un-capped caller (the hash/compare are byte-identical to the old unbounded walk for every real NUL-terminated path, so namespace behavior is unchanged). verify-all-angles: a kernel/non-canonical optval or sockaddr now returns -EFAULT instead of faulting; sun_path is NUL-terminated before any walk; the namespace hash is preserved for valid paths; no TOCTOU (operate on the kernel copy); KSTACK-safe (a 110-byte sockaddr_un + a 128-byte optval buffer are small). VERIFICATION: a NEW deterministic selftest unix_ns_str_selftest proves ns_hash_str/ns_streq are bounded (a fully non-NUL-terminated UNIX_PATH_MAX buffer terminates at the cap, equal buffers compare equal through it, a one-byte difference at the last position is detected) and functionally correct (NUL-stop: trailing garbage after the NUL does not change the hash); plus AF_UNIX bind/connect are HEAVILY boot-exercised (the display server, ksec, makaterm all bind/connect AF_UNIX sockets) so a clean boot proves the kernel-copy did not break them. `[unix_ns_str] SELF-TEST PASSED (bounded hash/streq, NUL-stop)` + [socketpair-selftest]/[unix_refcount]/[unix_stream_accept]/[unix_dgram_peer] all PASS. - 2026-06-26 - F111 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #4, data-race -- the sharpest of an AF_UNIX cluster): the AF_UNIX listener backlog (backlog_head/backlog_tail/backlog_count) was mutated from multiple CPUs with NO mutual exclusion -- connect() pushes a pending node and accept() pops one, both holding only rcu_read_lock (which keeps the socket alive but does NOT serialize the singly-linked list), so a connect-push racing an accept-pop (or a second concurrent connect/accept) tears the list and DOUBLE-frees the same pend node (double kfree(pend) + double unix_put(client)) (kernel/net/unix_sock.c + unix_sock.h). FOUND by sweeping the whole tree (4 parallel read-only agents over net / mm+proc / drivers+io / fs+ipc) for the data-race type. The agents surfaced a CLUSTER rooted in ONE cause: unix_sock_t carries no per-socket data lock (unix_sock.h:106 literally reads "Protected by single-threaded kernel"), so FOUR queues race (backlog, SOCK_DGRAM rx, SOCK_STREAM cbuf, SCM_RIGHTS ancillary); plus a UDP-inet-rx-ring gap, an fd_flags cloexec lost-update, and the latent unbounded s_mmio_next -- all recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #4 for the next turns. INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the backlog against the real code (no-assumptions): connect (unix_sock_connect) does the backlog_count admission check and the head/tail/count link with only rcu_read_lock held (the kmalloc of pend and the unix_wake/unix_poll_wake are around it); accept (unix_sock_accept) pops backlog_head/tail/count with NO lock at all (only the LATER claim+peer-link is under s_unix_pair_lock, which never covers the list pointers); free_rcu drains the backlog but runs only post-grace-period at refcount 0 (RCU-serialized vs connect, and accept cannot run on a closed/refcount-0 listener), so it is single-threaded by construction and needs no lock. So the LIVE race is connect-push vs accept-pop vs a 2nd connect/accept on other CPUs. FIX (do-it-right, the root -- add the missing per-socket lock): added unix_sock_t.lock (a per-socket spinlock, initialised in unix_sock_open), and serialised the backlog under it: connect re-checks LISTENING + the backlog limit and links the node under target->lock (the listener owns the backlog), accept pops under listener->lock re-checking the head INSIDE the lock (so a spurious wake or a lost race to another accepter cleanly re-waits instead of dereferencing a NULL/stale head). The kmalloc(pend) stays before the lock and unix_wake/unix_poll_wake stay after it (wait_queue_wake_all touches rq_lock, which must never nest under a leaf data lock); the per-socket lock and s_unix_pair_lock are never held simultaneously (connect/accept take them in separate critical sections), so no lock-order inversion. verify-all-angles: the push, the pop, the count, and the admission limit are all now atomic; a failed admission undoes the unix_get + frees pend; a multi-accepter race resolves to exactly one popper of each node (no double-free); free_rcu is unchanged (provably single-threaded). The SAME lock will absorb the dgram / cbuf / ancillary queues (B/C/D) in the next turns -- one mechanism, no per-queue drift. Documented in docs/LOCKS.md. VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU race, not deterministically reproducible single-threaded -> code-proof + the existing unix_stream_accept_selftest drives the EXACT connect->backlog->accept path now under the lock (a missing/unbalanced unlock would self-deadlock and FREEZE the boot at that selftest, never printing PASS) + AF_UNIX is heavily boot-exercised (the display server / ksec / makaterm all stream-connect+accept). `[unix_stream_accept] PASS (backlog owned-ref + atomic accept claim)` + [socketpair-selftest]/[unix_refcount]/[unix_dgram_peer]/[unix_ns_str] all PASS. First boot hit the flaky F55 stall (net ready, login + /bin/net paged, 0 faults, 75 selftests PASSED incl. all AF_UNIX); the SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 75 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. This closes the AF_UNIX backlog double-free; SCAN #4 continues next turn with the sibling queues (dgram/cbuf/ancillary) onto the same lock. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F112 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #4, continuing the AF_UNIX data-race cluster): two more AF_UNIX per-socket queues that shared the F111 root (unix_sock_t had no per-socket data lock -- unix_sock.h:106 "Protected by single-threaded kernel") were mutated cross-CPU with no mutual exclusion -- (B) the SOCK_DGRAM rx queue (dgram_head/tail/count) raced unix_sock_sendto enqueue vs unix_sock_recv_ex dequeue -> torn list / lost message / count lost-update; (D) the SCM_RIGHTS ancillary queue (ancillary.files[]/head/tail/count) raced unix_sock_sendfd enqueue (into the PEER's ancillary) vs recvfd/recvfd_nb dequeue -> count lost-update, a passed fd leaked or double-delivered, and a free_rcu double-vfs_close (kernel/net/unix_sock.c + unix_sock.h). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): (B) unix_sock_sendto kmallocs the dgram node and memcpys the user data INTO it BEFORE the enqueue (so the enqueue touches only kernel-resident list pointers + the count), and unix_sock_recv_ex copies the message out + kfrees AFTER the dequeue, so both the enqueue (target's queue) and the dequeue (self's queue) are kernel-only and cleanly lockable; (D) sendfd/recvfd move only a kernel vfs_file_t* (the dup'd file) -- no user copy under the lock. FIX (do-it-right, REUSE the F111 unix_sock_t.lock -- one mechanism, no per-queue drift): sendto links the node under target->lock (the receiver owns its dgram queue) and recv_ex dequeues under self->lock re-checking the head INSIDE the lock; sendfd enqueues under peer->lock (the peer owns the ancillary queue) re-checking the limit inside (the vfs_dup stays outside, undone with vfs_close if the re-check finds it full), and recvfd / recvfd_nb dequeue under self->lock re-checking count inside. The kmalloc, the user-data memcpy/copy-out, and the wait_queue wakes all stay OUTSIDE the lock (the memcpy reads/writes user memory, which must never fault under a preempt-disabled spinlock; the wakes touch rq_lock); each op locks EXACTLY the owner of the queue it touches (never two per-socket locks at once -> no AB-BA), and the lock is never nested with s_unix_pair_lock; free_rcu drains both queues post-grace-period at refcount 0 (single-threaded, no lock), mirroring the backlog. REVISED the planned scope (no-assumptions): the third sibling queue (C, the SOCK_STREAM cbuf) was NOT bundled in -- VERIFICATION showed cbuf_write/cbuf_read copy USER memory DIRECTLY (the send/recv buffer is the syscall pointer passed straight through), so the data copy cannot run under the per-socket spinlock (a user-page fault under a preempt-disabled lock would deadlock); C needs a kernel-bounce refactor of unix_sock_send_ex/recv_ex (copy user<->kernel outside the lock, hold the lock only around the kernel<->ring copy + the count) and is deferred to its own turn rather than crammed in with B/D. verify-all-angles: the enqueue/dequeue/count of both queues are now atomic; a full-ancillary re-check undoes the dup; a multi-receiver race resolves to exactly one popper (no double-take / no double-free); free_rcu unchanged. VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU race -> code-proof + the existing selftests drive the EXACT locked paths (a missing/unbalanced unlock would self-deadlock and FREEZE the boot): `[unix_dgram_peer] SELF-TEST PASSED (owned dgram dest survives its close)` drives sendto/recv, `[scm_rights-selftest] PASS (fd round-trip over pair)` drives sendfd/recvfd, plus [socketpair-selftest]/[unix_stream_accept]/[unix_ns_str] all PASS, and AF_UNIX is heavily boot-exercised (the display server passes wl_buffer fds via SCM_RIGHTS). First boot reached the DHCP lease directly (no F55 stall): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2, 75 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. unix_sock_t.lock now guards backlog + dgram + ancillary; the stream cbuf (C) is the last single-CPU-model queue (its kernel-bounce fix is the next turn). Documented in docs/LOCKS.md + the unix_sock.h comments. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F113 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #4, completing the AF_UNIX data-race cluster): the AF_UNIX SOCK_STREAM circular buffer (buf_head/buf_tail/buf_count) -- the LAST single-CPU-model queue -- was mutated cross-CPU with no mutual exclusion: cbuf_write runs on the SENDER's CPU and does the PEER's buf_count += while cbuf_read on the owner's CPU does buf_count -= , a non-atomic RMW from two CPUs = permanent fill-level corruption (the connection wedges "full" or reports phantom data) + torn stream bytes (kernel/net/unix_sock.c + unix_sock.h). This is the display server's hot data path. REVISED-then-fixed (no-assumptions, from the F112 deferral): cbuf_write/cbuf_read copied USER memory DIRECTLY (the send/recv buf is the syscall pointer passed straight through), so unlike the dgram/ancillary queues (B/D, which move only kernel-resident pointers under the lock) the cbuf data copy CANNOT run under the per-socket spinlock -- a page fault on the user page under a preempt-disabled lock would deadlock. VERIFIED against the real code: UNIX_BUF_SIZE is 8 KiB (too big for a stack bounce -- KSTACK is 8 KiB); the send loop's blocking-when-peer-full and the recv blocking-when-empty WAIT_EVENT conditions read buf_count lock-free (benign, re-checked); cbuf had exactly two callers (unix_sock_send_ex stream branch, unix_sock_recv_ex stream branch). FIX (do-it-right, REUSE unix_sock_t.lock + a chunked kernel bounce): converted cbuf_write/cbuf_read into cbuf_write_locked(owner, const kbuf, n)/cbuf_read_locked(owner, kbuf, n) -- they take the OWNER's per-socket lock internally and operate on a KERNEL buffer, so the byte copy + buf_count RMW + index advance are atomic w.r.t. the peer. The callers bounce the user data through a 512-byte STACK chunk OUTSIDE the lock and loop: SEND copies user->kbuf (memcpy, outside the lock) then cbuf_write_locked(peer, kbuf, chunk); RECV does cbuf_read_locked(self, kbuf, chunk) then kbuf->user (memcpy, outside the lock). The 512-byte chunk bounds BOTH stack use and lock-hold time (the per-chunk byte-copy under the spinlock is <= 512 stores). A sender into B and a reader of B both lock B->lock (the buffer owner = the receiver) -> serialized; A->B and B->A use different locks (B->lock vs A->lock), one each -> no AB-BA deadlock. verify-all-angles: NO user-memory access under the lock (the only thing that could deadlock); the partial-write/blocking-when-full send loop and the return-what-is-available stream recv semantics are preserved (the chunked recv stops when the ring drains, yielding the same byte count as the old single cbuf_read); EOF/EPIPE/EAGAIN/EINTR paths unchanged; free_rcu never touched the cbuf so it is unaffected; the peer-wake-after-recv (so a blocked sender sees freed space) is unchanged. VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU race -> code-proof + the existing socketpair_selftest drives BIDIRECTIONAL cbuf send/recv over a pair and asserts a byte-exact round-trip THROUGH the new locked bounce (a missing/unbalanced unlock would self-deadlock and FREEZE the boot; a corrupt bounce would mismatch the bytes and FAIL), and the stream cbuf is THE display-server data path (every wayland message), so a clean boot proves it. `[socketpair-selftest] PASS (bidirectional stream)` + [unix_stream_accept]/[unix_dgram_peer]/[scm_rights]/[unix_ns_str] all PASS. First boot reached the DHCP lease directly (no F55 stall): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2, 75 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. *** AF_UNIX per-socket-queue DATA-RACE CLUSTER NOW COMPLETE *** -- backlog (F111) + dgram (F112) + ancillary (F112) + stream cbuf (F113) all on unix_sock_t.lock; unix_sock.h:106 "Protected by single-threaded kernel" is gone. SCAN #4 continues next turn with the non-AF_UNIX candidates (UDP rx ring, fd_flags cloexec, s_mmio_next). Documented in docs/LOCKS.md + the unix_sock.h comments. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F114 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #4, the inet UDP rx-ring data race): the UDP inet socket's receive ring (udp_rx_head/udp_rx_tail/udp_rx_count on socket_t) was mutated from two CPUs with no mutual exclusion -- socket_deliver_udp (the net receive path) ENQUEUES a skb while socket_recv / socket_recvfrom DEQUEUE from process context -> the uint16 count RMW is lost-updated (++ from the deliver vs -- from the receiver) and the head/tail singly-linked list is torn (a leaked skb, or udp_rx_tail->next written onto an already-freed skb) (kernel/net/socket.c + socket.h). The inet socket_t had no per-socket data lock (the AF_UNIX root, F111-F113, repeated here). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): (a) the CONTEXT -- socket_deliver_udp is reached from net_rx_thread, which net.c spawns via task_create_kthread (the virtio-net IRQ handler only irq_notify's it, never delivers inline), so delivery runs in PROCESS (kthread) context, NOT a hard IRQ/softirq -> a plain preempt-disabling spin_lock suffices, no irqsave (mirrors the tty keyboard kthread); (b) the deliver enqueue (skb pointers + count) and the recv/recvfrom dequeue (head/tail/count) are kernel-only -- the skb's user copy-out (__builtin_memcpy(buf, skb->data, copy)) and the src_addr stamp happen AFTER the dequeue, so only kernel-resident pointers move under the lock; (c) rcu in socket_deliver_udp keeps the socket_t ALIVE (deferred free) but does NOT serialize the ring mutation -- the live race is deliver-enqueue vs recv-dequeue; (d) sock_free_rcu drains the ring post-grace-period at refcount 0, where the deliver is RCU-serialized (its rcu_read_lock blocks the grace period) and no recv can run on a closed fd, so it is single-threaded by construction and needs no lock. FIX (do-it-right, REUSE the AF_UNIX discipline -- a per-socket leaf lock, lock the queue owner, copies + wakes outside): added socket_t.udp_rx_lock (initialised in both socket constructors), and serialised the ring under it -- socket_deliver_udp re-checks the UDP_RX_QUEUE_MAX limit and links the skb under the lock (skb_free on a full queue + the wait_queue_wake_all/sock_poll_wake stay outside, inside the existing rcu section), and socket_recv (UDP branch) + socket_recvfrom dequeue under the lock, re-checking the head INSIDE the lock and RETRYING the wait if another receiver drained it (closing a NULL-skb deref a 2nd concurrent receiver on a dup'd fd could otherwise hit), with the src_addr stamp + the user memcpy + skb_free kept OUTSIDE the lock. verify-all-angles: the enqueue/dequeue/count are atomic; the full-queue admission is re-checked under the lock (no over-fill / no count lost-update); NO user-memory access under the spinlock; the lock is a leaf (never nested with the rcu/tx/udp-table locks -> no cycle); the wakes stay outside; the nonblock/EAGAIN paths and the blocking semantics are preserved; TCP rings are untouched (they stay on pcb->lock -- this lock is UDP-only). VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU race -> code-proof + DIRECT runtime proof: the DHCP handshake IS UDP, so the DHCP OFFER/ACK are delivered through socket_deliver_udp's now-locked enqueue and consumed by the DHCP client through socket_recv's now-locked dequeue -- the boot reaching `ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2` proves the locked UDP rx path works end-to-end; plus [sock_file_life]/[socketpair-selftest]/[unix_dgram_peer] PASS, 75 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders (first boot, no F55). Documented in docs/LOCKS.md. SCAN #4 continues next turn with the fd_flags cloexec lost-update + s_mmio_next. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F115 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #4, the fd_flags close-on-exec lost-update): sys_socket_inner set the new socket fd's FD_CLOEXEC flag as a SEPARATE unlocked store AFTER fd_install returned (`tf->ft->fd_flags[fd] = FD_CLOEXEC`, no tf->lock), while a sibling thread's fd_table_grow COW-copies the whole fd_flags array under tf->lock and RCU-publishes a NEW table -> the FD_CLOEXEC store could land in the OLD (pending-RCU-free) table while the live table keeps fd_flags[fd]==0, so the flag was LOST and the socket fd survived exec (the wayland/foot fd-leak-across-exec class) -- plus a minor write to the about-to-be-freed old table (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). Security-relevant (an fd leaked into an exec'd child). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): fd_install (syscall.c) installs fd_table[fd]=f under tf->lock then UNLOCKS and returns, so the cloexec set was necessarily a second critical section; between the unlock and the store a concurrent fd_table_grow (kernel/proc/process.c, COW + rcu_assign_pointer under tf->lock) can swap tf->ft, and the unsynchronized store can hit the old snapshot. Confirmed sys_socket_inner was the LONE outlier: sys_open's own install loop sets fd_table[fd] AND fd_flags[fd] together under tf->lock (syscall.c:545-547), sys_close clears fd_flags[fd] under the lock (566), and dup2/F_SETFD/F_DUPFD_CLOEXEC/openpty all set fd_flags under tf->lock -- only the socket post-install store was unlocked; accept/recvfd/epoll_create/eventfd do not set fd_flags at all (no sibling instances of this bug). FIX (do-it-right, ONE chokepoint -- make the illegal "install then set the flag unlocked" state unrepresentable): added fd_install_cloexec(vfs_file_t* f, int cloexec) which sets BOTH tf->ft->fd_table[fd]=f AND tf->ft->fd_flags[fd]=(cloexec?FD_CLOEXEC:0) in the SAME tf->lock critical section (so the fd and its flag are published together and a concurrent grow either COWs the flag or the install lands in the post-grow table); fd_install(f) is now a one-line wrapper calling fd_install_cloexec(f, 0), so the other 7 callers (openpty/accept/recvfd/epoll/eventfd) are unchanged; sys_socket_inner installs via fd_install_cloexec(f, type & MK_SOCK_CLOEXEC) and its racy post-install block is deleted. Bonus robustness: fd_install_cloexec EXPLICITLY writes fd_flags[fd] (the old fd_install left it untouched, relying on the slot already being 0), so a reused slot can never carry a stale close-on-exec flag from a prior fd. verify-all-angles: the flag now always lands in the LIVE table at the installed index, serialized against grow; FD_CLOEXEC is honored by the exec close-on-exec scan (syscall.c:1059-1068, reads fd_flags under the table); the non-cloexec path is byte-identical (flag = 0). VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU race -> code-proof (both writes now under one lock) + the BOOT is a strong regression guard since EVERY fd-creating syscall (open/socket/pipe/accept/eventfd/epoll/timerfd/dup) flows through fd_install -> fd_install_cloexec thousands of times, and the [timerfd_race] selftest storms 20000 fd install/close iterations across 3 threads + the display server creates CLOEXEC sockets; a clean boot proves the chokepoint works. First boot reached the DHCP lease directly (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2, 75 selftests PASSED incl. [timerfd_race]/[socketpair-selftest]/[spawn_cred], 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. SCAN #4 has ONE candidate left (s_mmio_next, latent). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F116 HARDENING (BUG-TYPE SCAN #4 final candidate, the s_mmio_next MMIO VA cursor -- latent, not an active bug, framed like F108's do_switch landmine): vmm_map_mmio (kernel/mm/vmm.c) read the monotonic MMIO virtual-address cursor s_mmio_next, mapped the device BAR, then bumped the cursor -- the read-then-bump was UNSYNCHRONIZED (no lock/atomic, so two concurrent callers would read the same base and map overlapping device windows) AND UNBOUNDED (no ceiling, so the cursor could run past the MMIO window into adjacent kernel VA). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): (a) the read (s_mmio_next) and the bump (s_mmio_next += ...) were plain non-atomic accesses; (b) there was no window-end constant; (c) CONFIRMED LATENT, not active -- grepped every caller (ioapic_init, virtio_input_init, ahci_init, virtio_gpu_init, virtio_net_init, hda_init, nvme_init) and all are *_init() reached only through the single-threaded initcall DAG (run_dag) on the BSP while the APs are parked, so there is no concurrent caller today (it becomes an active overlap the moment any AP-side / hot-plug / deferred-probe caller appears); (d) the VA layout (HHDM at 0xFFFF800000000000 far below, kernel image at 0xFFFFFFFF80000000 far above) leaves the MMIO window at 0xFFFF900000000000 collision-free for a generous ceiling; (e) vmm_map_mmio does a fresh not-present->present install at a never-reused VA, so per SCAN #2 it needs NO TLB shootdown (unchanged). FIX (do-it-right, lock-free bump allocator + overflow-safe bound): reserve a disjoint [base, base+span) via `base = __atomic_fetch_add(&s_mmio_next, span, __ATOMIC_RELAXED)` so two concurrent callers can never get overlapping VAs (the reservation is atomic + all-or-nothing -- a rejected one does not leave the cursor half-bumped beyond the atomic add, and the next caller simply gets a higher base); added a documented MMIO_VIRT_END ceiling = 0xFFFF910000000000 (a 1 TiB window, which dwarfs the total device-BAR footprint of a few hundred KiB and does not collide with the HHDM or the kernel image) and reject a reservation that would cross it with the OVERFLOW-SAFE test `base >= MMIO_VIRT_END || span > MMIO_VIRT_END - base` (never computes base+span, mirroring the checked.h bounds discipline), returning 0 + a diagnostic kprintf on exhaustion. The callers do not check the 0 return, but a 0/NULL return NULL-deref-panics on first MMIO access (a DETECTABLE fault) whereas the old silent overrun would corrupt adjacent kernel VA -- 0 is strictly the safer failure mode, and the ceiling never fires at real device counts anyway. verify-all-angles: the span is computed once in u64 (pages*PAGE_SIZE cannot wrap for a sane BAR size); the bound is overflow-safe; the fetch_add reservation is disjoint-by-construction; the map loop and the uncacheable PCD+PWT flags are unchanged. VERIFICATION: a latent cross-CPU race -> code-proof (fetch_add is disjoint, the bound is overflow-safe) + the BOOT is a strong exercise -- EVERY MMIO driver maps its BARs through vmm_map_mmio (~15 calls at boot), and a clean boot with virtio-net up ([net] MAC + ready + the DHCP lease ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2) and the virtio-gpu framebuffer up (1280x800 scanout) and ahci/nvme/hda/ioapic initialised proves the atomic-reserve + ceiling did not break any mapping (no "MMIO window exhausted"). First boot hit the flaky F55 stall (net ready, login + /bin/net paged, 0 faults, all driver MMIO initialised, no DHCP); the SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease, 75 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. *** This is the LAST SCAN #4 candidate -- BUG-TYPE SCAN #4 (data-race) is now COMPLETE *** (every active data race fixed: AF_UNIX backlog/dgram/cbuf/ancillary F111-F113, UDP rx ring F114, fd_flags cloexec F115, s_mmio_next latent-hardened F116). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F117 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #5, a reachable double-free in the sys_pipe failure path): pipe(2)'s error path freed the read-end vfs_file_t while leaving it INSTALLED in the fd table, so a later close/exit freed it again -- heap corruption / use-after-free (kernel/syscall/syscall.c).
