FOUND by sweeping the whole tree (4 parallel read-only agents over net / fs+vfs / drivers+io / mm+proc) for the double-free / unbalanced-refcount class; this was the ONLY reachable double-free -- the rest of the class is audited-clean (pty do_free, io_uring join-before-free, pmm refcount-1:1, the F107 exit-teardown siblings, AF_UNIX/SCM_RIGHTS/dcache/epoll refcounts all balanced; details in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #5). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): sys_pipe installs the read end first (rfd, fd_table[rfd]=r) under tf->lock, then continues the loop to find the WRITE slot; if that next iteration hits `fd >= cap` and fd_table_grow OOMs, it `goto fail` with r STILL installed at fd_table[rfd]; the `fail:` path did `vfs_close(r); vfs_close(w);` -- the vfs_close(r) drives the pipe's open_ends refcount and frees r (and the pipe_buf_t) while fd_table[rfd] is left as a DANGLING pointer to the freed r, so the next sys_close(rfd) or the process-exit task_files_release (which vfs_close's every installed fd) frees r a SECOND time. Confirmed the write end is NEVER installed on the fail path (its branch sets fd_table[fd]=w then immediately break-s out of the loop, before any grow), so vfs_close(w) is always correct. Reachable when the caller's fd table is exactly one slot from full AND fd_table_grow fails (OOM) during the write-slot search; the second free is then guaranteed at exit. The copyout-failure path just above already handled this correctly (sys_close(rfd)/sys_close(wfd)), and socketpair's rollback does too -- the fail: path was the lone holdout (classic shape: free-without-NULLing a stale fd-table pointer). FIX (do-it-right, mirror the established rollback discipline): at fail:, close an INSTALLED read end via its fd -- `if (rfd >= 0) sys_close((uint64_t)rfd)` (sys_close clears fd_table[rfd] AND drops the ref, so no dangling pointer) -- and only `else vfs_close(r)` when r was never installed; vfs_close(w) unchanged (w never installed). verify-all-angles: both paths now free the pipe EXACTLY once (rfd>=0: sys_close(r-via-fd) + vfs_close(w) -> open_ends 2->0 -> pipe_destroy once, slot cleared; rfd<0: vfs_close(r)+vfs_close(w) -> once, neither installed); no leak (the pipe is still freed once); the success and copyout-fail paths are unchanged. VERIFICATION: the bug needs fd_table_grow to OOM, not deterministically reproducible in a selftest -> code-proof (the installed end is now closed through its fd, clearing the slot) + the pipe lifetime selftests [pipe_refcount] (single last-end release, no double free) and [pipe_race] (65536 bytes in-order) PASS + pipes are pervasively boot-exercised (every shell pipeline). First boot reached the DHCP lease directly (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2, 75 selftests PASSED incl. [pipe_refcount]/[pipe_race]/[socketpair-selftest], 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. This was the only reachable double-free the sweep found; the OTHER-class candidates it surfaced (the half-open-TCP-PCB leak / SYN-flood DoS, the virtio_net_rx_poll + fat32_open NULL-derefs, the drm create_dumb free-convention divergence, the latent pcache_evict double-free behind dead code) are recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #5 for later type-scans. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F118 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #6, the io_uring CQ-overflow resource leak): the io_uring CQ-overflow list had TWO unprivileged-local leak bugs -- (a) UNBOUNDED GROWTH and (b) LEAK ON CLOSE (kernel/io/io_uring.c + io_uring.h). When the CQ ring is full, io_uring_post_cqe spills each extra completion onto a kmalloc'd singly-linked overflow list (overflow_head/tail); its ONLY freer is the drain-at-the-top of a SUBSEQUENT post_cqe that finds CQ space. FOUND by sweeping the whole tree (4 parallel read-only agents over net / fs+vfs / drivers+io / mm+proc) for the resource-leak class -- TWO independent agents flagged this io_uring list. INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): (a) io_uring_post_cqe (the CQ-full branch) kmalloc's and pushes a node with NO length cap and NO submission backpressure, so an unprivileged process that creates a ring, submits ops (NOP batches via io_uring_enter, refilling the SQ across many enter() calls) and NEVER advances cq_hdr->head grows the list without bound -> kernel-memory DoS; (b) io_uring_close_file (the fd close op, reached by close(2) AND process-exit fd cleanup) stops+joins the SQPOLL/worker kthreads, releases fixed_files, unmaps + frees the backing, then kfree(uring) -- it NEVER walks overflow_head, so a ring closed with a non-empty overflow list (the state (a) reaches) leaks every node permanently (kfree(uring) drops only the head pointer). FIX (do-it-right, cap the growth + drain on close): added a uint32_t overflow_count to io_uring_t + a IO_URING_OVERFLOW_MAX cap (4096 nodes, ~96 KiB max overflow memory per ring -- generous for legitimate bursts, bounds the DoS); past the cap, post_cqe DROPS the completion and bumps the user-visible cq_hdr->overflow counter (the same last-resort behavior as the existing OOM branch, so userspace sees it and reaps); and io_uring_close_file now DRAINS the overflow list (kfree every node, reset head/tail/count) under overflow_lock before kfree(uring) -- safe with no racing poster because the SQPOLL + io_wq worker kthreads are already stopped+joined above and the fd is gone. overflow_count is touched only inside post_cqe's cq_lock critical section (the cap is read under cq_lock; the increment on push and the decrement on drain are under the nested overflow_lock, itself inside cq_lock), so the counter has no data race; the close-path reset runs with no concurrent poster. verify-all-angles: the list can no longer grow past the cap (DoS bounded); a closed ring's overflow nodes are all freed (no leak); the normal (CQ-not-full) fast path is unchanged; the drain is a no-op on an empty list so it cannot break the common close. VERIFICATION: the overflow path is not boot-exercised (the [io_uring_test] reaps its CQ, so it never overflows) -> code-proof (the cap bounds the count; the close-drain frees every node) + the existing [io_uring_test] (create -> NOP batch + 100-round steady-state enter/dispatch/complete -> close) and [io_ring_idx] PASS, proving the create/enter/complete/CLOSE path (where the drain lives) is unbroken (an empty-list drain is a no-op), + a clean boot. First FOUR boots hit the flaky F55 stall (net ready, login RENDERS `More login:`, /bin/net + svcmgr paged, 0 faults, 75 selftests PASSED incl. [io_uring_test], no DHCP -- a stubborn F55 streak; the io_uring overflow list is UNRELATED to the DHCP/UDP path, so it cannot cause the stall); the 5th SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 75 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD]. The HIGHEST-severity leak the sweep found (the REMOTE TCP SYN-flood half-open leak) is recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #6 with its full reaper design + the SMP-synchronization subtleties (the rcu-reader-context call_rcu_expedited panic, and the reap-vs-handshake-completion race that a rushed fix would turn into a UAF) -- it is deferred to a DEDICATED turn so it is done correctly, not half-baked. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F119 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #6 headline, the remote TCP SYN-flood half-open leak -- the single highest-severity finding of the whole campaign): a TCP_SYN_RCVD child PCB (tcp_pcb_alloc + a 64 KiB txbuf + 64 KiB rxbuf, ~128 KiB, published on s_pcb_head) was NEVER freed if the final handshake ACK never arrived -- tcp_timer_tick rewound + resent the SYN-ACK forever with NO retransmit cap, and the only tcp_pcb_free callers own a socket fd while a SYN_RCVD child has sock_file==NULL and no fd, so nothing reaped it; a remote, unauthenticated SYN flood (SYN, withhold the final ACK) leaked ~128 KiB per spoofed SYN without bound -> kernel-memory exhaustion DoS (kernel/net/tcp.c). FOUND by the SCAN #6 resource-leak sweep (the net agent). This was deferred from F118 to a DEDICATED turn because a CORRECT reaper has two real SMP-synchronization subtleties that a rushed version would turn into a UAF (worse than the leak): (1) tcp_timer_tick walks s_pcb_head UNDER rcu_read_lock, but freeing goes through call_rcu_expedited -> synchronize_rcu_expedited, which PANICS under a reader / preempt-disabled, so you cannot free inside the walk; (2) the timer thread (net_tcp_timer_thread) reaping a SYN_RCVD child RACES the rx thread (net_rx_thread / tcp_recv) completing the handshake (SYN_RCVD -> ESTABLISHED + accept_queue push) -- a reap that frees a child that just completed is a UAF of a valid connection / a dangling accept-queue entry. INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): tcp_pcb_alloc memsets the struct to 0; the SYN_RCVD->ESTABLISHED transition in tcp_recv (the case TCP_SYN_RCVD ACK handler) set pcb->state=TCP_ESTABLISHED as a PLAIN store (NO s_pcb_wlock) and pushed to the accept queue under the LISTENER's pcb->lock; tcp_timer_tick and tcp_recv run in SEPARATE kthreads. FIX (do-it-right, both subtleties handled): added `uint8_t rexmit` (incremented in tcp_timer_tick's SYN_RCVD rto branch for un-accepted half-opens -- timer-thread-only, no lock), `uint8_t reaped`, and a transient `tcp_pcb_t* reap_next` link + a TCP_SYN_RCVD_MAX_RETRIES cap (5 -> ~6 s grace). For subtlety (1): the reap runs AFTER rcu_read_unlock -- a separate pass takes s_pcb_wlock and collects every over-cap SYN_RCVD orphan (sock_file==NULL) by setting ->reaped, unlinking it via rcu_assign_pointer on the PREDECESSOR's ->next (leaving the victim's own ->next intact so a concurrent RCU reader walking ->next is undisturbed), and chaining it onto a local list via ->reap_next (a SEPARATE field); then ONE synchronize_rcu_expedited covers the whole batch before direct tcp_pcb_free_rcu frees (one grace period, not N -- no per-child stall under a flood). For subtlety (2): the establish-vs-reap decision is now ATOMIC on s_pcb_wlock -- tcp_recv's SYN_RCVD->ESTABLISHED transition runs UNDER s_pcb_wlock and commits only if `!pcb->reaped && pcb->state==TCP_SYN_RCVD` (so if the reaper already claimed the child it aborts -- no establish, no accept_q_push of a being-freed pcb), and the reaper sets ->reaped + unlinks under the same lock -- so a child that just established (state==ESTABLISHED) is observed by the reaper and skipped, and a reaped child is never queued by a racing establish (no UAF); the accept_q_push stays under the LISTENER's lock (a SEPARATE critical section after releasing s_pcb_wlock, so no two-lock nesting / deadlock -- the reaper takes s_pcb_wlock only, tcp_accept takes the listener lock only). verify-all-angles: a completing handshake is never reaped; a reaped child is unlinked once + RCU-freed once (txbuf/rxbuf freed by tcp_pcb_free_rcu); no synchronize_rcu under rcu_read_lock; a SYN_RCVD child WITH a socket (post-accept) is never reaped (the sock_file==NULL guard); a fresh half-open under the cap keeps retransmitting (the slow-legit-client case). VERIFICATION: a NEW deterministic selftest tcp_synreap_selftest -- (A) an over-cap SYN_RCVD orphan (sock_file==NULL, rexmit>cap) is REAPED by one tcp_timer_tick (asserted via a pointer-compare on-list walk, safe even post-free), (B) a SYN_RCVD child WITH a socket is NOT reaped even over the cap; single-threaded so the reap-pass synchronize_rcu_expedited has no concurrent reader and cannot deadlock, and robust against the live net_tcp_timer_thread (same reap outcome for A; B is never touched). `[tcp_synreap] SELF-TEST PASSED (over-cap SYN_RCVD half-open reaped, owned child kept)` + the existing [tcp_orphan] (listener-free orphans children) and [tcp_accept] (accept-queue ring) STILL PASS, proving the s_pcb_wlock establish-serialization did not break the handshake/accept/orphan paths. First boot reached the DHCP lease directly (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2, 76 selftests PASSED incl. [tcp_synreap], 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. The cross-thread reap-vs-handshake race is closed by the s_pcb_wlock establish-or-reap pattern (reasoned, as TCP is not boot-SMP-exercised). The SECONDARY listener-close orphan reaping (completed-but-unaccepted children) + a per-listener half-open cap are recorded as follow-ups in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #6 -- the SYN_RCVD reaper bounds the UNBOUNDED remote DoS (the headline). s_pcb_wlock's scope is documented in docs/LOCKS.md. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F120 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #7, the virtio-net RX NULL-deref panic): virtio_net_rx_poll handed a NULL skb to eth_recv on skb_alloc OOM -> kernel #PF panic (kernel/net/virtio_net.c + kernel/net/net.c). FOUND by sweeping the whole tree (4 parallel read-only agents over net / fs+vfs / drivers+io / mm+proc) for the NULL-deref / unchecked-allocation class -- this was the ONLY unprivileged / remote-reachable NULL-deref; every other alloc/lookup in the kernel is NULL-checked or has a not-found branch (audited-clean list in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #7), and the other gaps are OOM-only-kernel-path (task_create_kthread wild-CR3) or dead code (fat32_open, task_create_user) or latent boot-init (vmm_map_mmio 0-deref). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): virtio_net_rx_poll did `skbuff_t* skb = skb_alloc(eth_len);` then `if (skb && eth_len > 0) { ...memcpy... }` -- the skb guard protected ONLY the memcpy -- then recycled the descriptor and did `*skb_out = skb; return 1;` UNCONDITIONALLY, so on skb_alloc failure (kmalloc OOM) it returned 1 ("a packet is ready") with *skb_out==NULL, violating its "return 1 => valid skb" contract; net_rx_thread's drain loop `while (virtio_net_rx_poll(&skb)) eth_recv(skb);` then called eth_recv(NULL), which derefs skb->len at eth.c:11 -> NULL-deref #PF panic. Trigger: OOM during RX, but on the UNIVERSAL rx dispatch path (every received frame hits it once memory is exhausted), so a remote peer driving RX load under memory pressure can panic the kernel (a remote-driven OOM DoS); the runt path (eth_len==0) is safe (skb_alloc(0) returns a non-NULL zero-length skb). FIX (do-it-right, fix the CONTRACT at root so a future caller cannot reintroduce it): restructured virtio_net_rx_poll into a `for (;;)` loop over used-ring entries -- a DROPPED packet (skb_alloc OOM, or a bogus device-invented desc id) recycles its descriptor (the OOM case -- so the RX ring never leaks descriptors; the bogus-id case skips WITHOUT re-posting, as before, since its s_rx_bufs slot is {NULL,0}) and CONTINUES to the next used entry instead of returning a NULL skb or ending the drain; the function now only ever returns 1 with a VALID skb, and returns 0 only when the used ring is genuinely empty. verify-all-angles: a valid packet is handled identically to before (returns the first valid skb immediately); an OOM-dropped packet is dropped (data lost -- acceptable under OOM) with its buffer returned to the device, and the drain continues (no wedge of pending packets, unlike a bare return-0); a bogus desc id is dropped without indexing the tables / re-posting frame 0 (the existing untrusted-id guard preserved); eth_recv is NEVER called with NULL. VERIFICATION: the OOM path is not deterministically reproducible in a selftest (forcing skb_alloc to fail mid-RX is impractical) -> code-proof (the `if (!skb) continue` drop + the loop) + the DHCP handshake is itself UDP RECEIVED through virtio_net_rx_poll, so reaching `ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2` proves the new RX loop delivers valid packets to eth_recv end-to-end (the valid-packet path is unbroken). First boot hit the flaky F55 stall (net ready, [net] MAC obtained, login + /bin/net paged, 0 faults, 75 selftests PASSED, no DHCP); the SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 76 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. The lower-severity NULL-deref residuals (boot-init vmm_map_mmio 0-checks at ioapic/nvme/ahci/virtio_net MSI-X maps; task_create_kthread unchecked vmm_alloc_pml4; the PMM_INVALID_ADDR-vs-`!phys` wrong-sentinel DMA checks; dead-code fat32_open / task_create_user) are recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #7 for follow-up. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F121 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #8, the PMM wrong-sentinel wild-write-on-OOM DMA cluster -- fixed at root in ONE commit + a reusable primitive): pmm_buddy_alloc / vmm_alloc_pml4 return PMM_INVALID_ADDR == UINT64_MAX on OOM (NOT 0), but many driver DMA-init paths tested `if (!phys)` / `== 0`, which NEVER catches the UINT64_MAX sentinel -> the code proceeds with phys==UINT64_MAX and `phys + HHDM_OFFSET` wraps to a wild kernel pointer (~HHDM_OFFSET-1) -> a wild kernel memset and (worst case) a wild DMA base programmed into a device on OOM (kernel/mm/pmm.h + 5 drivers). FOUND by the SCAN #8 wrong-sentinel sweep (queued by SCAN #7). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): confirmed PMM_INVALID_ADDR == PMM_INVALID_FRAME == UINT64_MAX (pmm.h:7-8); confirmed the correct idiom (== PMM_INVALID_ADDR) is already used at io_uring.c:231 / drm.c:526 / nvme.c:722 and uniformly throughout mm/**, so the bug is confined to the driver DMA-init paths; and confirmed the worst site -- ahci.c port_init -- had NO checks AT ALL on s_cmdlist_phys / s_fis_phys / each s_ctbl_phys[i], memset-ing through +HHDM_OFFSET and PROGRAMMING the raw result into the AHCI command-list / FIS / command-table DMA registers (a wild DMA base handed to the controller on OOM, not merely a wild CPU write). FIX (do-it-right, ROOT + make the mis-check unrepresentable): extracted PMM_ALLOC_OK(p) := ((p) != PMM_INVALID_ADDR) into pmm.h (one named source of truth, documented with WHY `!phys` is wrong) and gated ALL 20 pmm_buddy_alloc result sites across the 5 affected drivers through it in a single commit (same root cause -> one fix): ahci.c port_init got early `return;` guards after the cmdlist/fis allocs and inside the per-slot ctbl loop (so OOM aborts BEFORE any wild memset / DMA program); hda.c 5 sites (corb/rirb/bdl/per-buffer/fifo) `if (!x)` -> `if (!PMM_ALLOC_OK(x))`; virtio_gpu.c 6 sites (desc/avail/used virtq rings + s_cmd + s_cursor + the framebuffer alloc); virtio_input.c the 4-way disjunction (eventq desc/avail/used + s_evbuf) in one guard; ac97.c 2 sites INCLUDING a uint32 TRUNCATION bug -- `s_bdl_phys = (uint32_t)pmm_buddy_alloc(0)` truncated UINT64_MAX to 0xFFFFFFFF (non-zero, so even the old `!s_bdl_phys` missed) -- restructured to check the full-width phys_addr_t result BEFORE narrowing to u32 (ac97 is dead code: no initcall, /dev/dsp routes to hda_write, so latent, but fixed for uniformity). verify-all-angles: for a VALID frame, `!PMM_ALLOC_OK(x)` == `!(x != UINT64_MAX)` == false == proceed, byte-identical to the old `!x`==false for any sane non-zero phys -> the non-OOM init path is unchanged; for an OOM result (UINT64_MAX) the check now correctly fails and the driver aborts before the wild memset / DMA program; the ac97 truncation is closed (full-width check); no behavioral change to any success path. VERIFICATION: the OOM branch is not boot-reproducible (the PMM is never exhausted at init) -> code-proof (PMM_ALLOC_OK is the exact sentinel test, applied at every site) + a clean BOOT is a strong regression guard since EVERY one of these drivers initialises at boot through the now-guarded path: ahci (`[initcall] ahci` + the ahci selftests PASS), hda (`[initcall] hda`), virtio-gpu (`[virtio-gpu] initialised (1 scanouts)` at 1280x800 -- including the guarded framebuffer alloc), virtio-input (`[virtio-input] bound 00:05 event0`); a clean init of all four proves a valid frame still passes PMM_ALLOC_OK and nothing was broken. First boot reached the DHCP lease directly (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2, 76 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. PMM_ALLOC_OK recorded in docs/PRIMITIVES.md (reuse at every future pmm_buddy_alloc / vmm_alloc_pml4 call). The HIGHER-severity out-of-type finding the sweep surfaced -- the spawn SPAWN_ATTR_UNVEIL raw user-pointer deref (`_access_ok` + raw memcpy with no copy_from_user -> an unprivileged kernel #PF panic, a SCAN #3 straggler) -- is recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #8 and queued as the NEXT turn; the ahci_submit_sg stale-data sentinel gap + the in-type residuals (socket_bind port-0 overload, fd_table_init/pid_alloc/mm_vma_add ignored OOM returns, io_uring DRM_COMMIT fdput leak) are recorded too. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F122 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #3 straggler surfaced by the SCAN #8 sweep, the spawn SPAWN_ATTR_UNVEIL raw user-pointer deref -- an unprivileged kernel #PF panic + a sibling OOB heap read): sys_spawn's SPAWN_ATTR_UNVEIL handling validated the user unveil-rule array with `_access_ok` (a RANGE check only) then did a RAW `__builtin_memcpy` from the user pointer a.unveil (kernel/syscall/syscall.c ~1449), so a user passing an in-range-but-UNMAPPED pointer faulted INSIDE the kernel -> an unprivileged kernel #PF panic (a trivial local DoS: spawn(path, argv, envp, stdio, &attr) with attr.flags=SPAWN_ATTR_UNVEIL, attr.nunveil>0, attr.unveil=an unmapped-but-canonical address). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): confirmed the exact `_access_ok(uptr, n*sizeof(entry))` + `__builtin_memcpy(ue, a.unveil, n*sizeof(entry))` shape; confirmed the IDENTICAL bug was ALREADY fixed 50 lines up in the same function (the spawn_attr_t copy at syscall.c:1395 was converted to copy_from_user for exactly this reason, with a comment "an in-range but UNMAPPED attr_ptr passes a range check then #PF-panics in the memcpy") -- the unveil array copy was the lone straggler; confirmed copy_from_user (syscall.c:3559) does `_access_ok` + `user_buf_prefault` (VMA-walk + demand-fault every page, returning -EFAULT GRACEFULLY on an unmapped/unbacked page) + memcpy, and that user_buf_prefault iterates by overflow-safe page count so it handles the multi-page (up to 64 KiB / 16-page) array span; confirmed copy_from_user is the established safe primitive used at every other syscall user-array copy (sys_spawn argv/stdio, sys_read path, etc.). SECOND bug found on the verify-all-angles "same attacker-controlled data" sweep: each copied ue[i].path is a fully user-controlled char[256] with NO guaranteed NUL, and unveil_add (kernel/security/unveil.c:32) computes its length with s_strlen (`while (s[n]) n++` -- UNBOUNDED), so a non-NUL-terminated path made s_strlen over-read PAST the entry, past the end of the n*257-byte kmalloc'd ue buffer, into adjacent heap until a stray 0 byte -- an OOB heap read (pre-existing under the old raw memcpy too, in the SAME flow). FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, in ONE commit -- both bugs in this exact attacker-controlled path): (1) replaced `_access_ok` + raw memcpy with `copy_from_user(ue, a.unveil, bytes)` (handles the fault -> -EFAULT -> goto bad_attr, never panics), mirroring the spawn_attr copy above, and added the missing `kfree(ue)` on the copy-failure path (the old raw memcpy could not "fail" so it never needed one; copy_from_user can, so the buffer must be freed before goto bad_attr -- closes a would-be leak); (2) bounded the attacker-controlled count with a new SPAWN_UNVEIL_MAX = 256 cap in syscall.h (`if (n > SPAWN_UNVEIL_MAX) goto bad_attr;`) so the kernel-side kmalloc is bounded to ~64 KiB (real unveil sets are a handful of paths; over-cap is rejected, consistent with the existing lenient "malformed attr ignored" bad_attr semantics) -- defense-in-depth (the prior code already failed gracefully on an absurd size since (uint64_t)n*257 cannot wrap and kmalloc(huge) returns NULL, but an explicit cap is the right design); (3) force-NUL-terminate each entry (`ue[i].path[sizeof(ue[i].path)-1] = '\0'`) before unveil_add so s_strlen is bounded to <=255 and cannot over-read past the entry -- closing the OOB heap read. verify-all-angles: count==0 (the `&& a.nunveil` guard skips the block entirely); over-cap (n>256 -> bad_attr, no alloc); a faulting/unmapped/non-canonical/kernel pointer (copy_from_user -> -EFAULT -> bad_attr -> kfree(ue), no panic, no leak); a partial/torn copy is impossible (copy_from_user is all-or-nothing after the prefault); a non-NUL-terminated path (forced NUL, no over-read); the SUCCESS path applies the unveil rules byte-identically to before (same unveil_add loop). Note: bad_attr "fails open" (the child gets no unveil restriction) -- this is the PRE-EXISTING design and not a privilege escalation (a parent passing a bad pointer only relaxes ITS OWN child's sandbox, never gains privilege), left unchanged; recorded as an observation, not changed in this DoS fix. VERIFICATION: the panic path needs a user mm with an in-range-unmapped pointer (impractical to forge in a kernel selftest), so -> code-proof (copy_from_user is the exact safe primitive, the NUL-term bounds s_strlen) + the EXISTING copy_user_selftest / syscall_user_ptr_selftest / access_ok_selftest already prove copy_from_user rejects unmapped/non-canonical/over-range pointers with -EFAULT instead of faulting + the SUCCESS path is BOOT-EXERCISED end-to-end: the boot service /etc/services/net.svc declares `unveil=/etc rwc`, so svcmgr spawns /bin/net with SPAWN_ATTR_UNVEIL (nunveil=1, a real user pointer) through exactly this code on EVERY boot, and reaching the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2) proves /bin/net was spawned, the unveil entry copied via the new copy_from_user, and the /etc unveil rule applied (net reads /etc + runs). First boot reached the DHCP lease directly (no F55): 76 selftests PASSED incl. [unveil]/[virtfs_unveil]/[spawn_cred], 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. No new selftest added (the panic is not kernel-selftest-reproducible and the success path is already a per-boot live guard, matching the F120 code-proof+boot-exercise precedent). Recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #8 (the finding marked FIXED) + docs/PRIMITIVES.md (one more copy_from_user conversion at the syscall boundary). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F123 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #9, the UDP send-length u32->u16 truncation + 16-bit wrap -> unprivileged kernel NULL-deref panic): an unprivileged process calling send(2)/sendto(2) on an AF_INET SOCK_DGRAM socket with a payload length in [65528, 65535] panicked the kernel (kernel/net/udp.c + socket.c + ipv4.c). FOUND by the SCAN #9 truncation/sign sweep (the net agent); it was the ONLY remotely/unprivileged-reachable instance of the class (the fs/drivers/mm sweeps found only LOW/latent narrowings, all defended downstream -- recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #9). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): socket_send (socket.c:482) and socket_sendto (socket.c:583) narrowed the user-controlled uint32_t len to uint16_t with `(uint16_t)len` and NO size check; udp_send/udp_send_ex took `uint16_t len`; udp_send_ex:49 then did `uint16_t udplen = (uint16_t)(UDP_HDR_LEN + len)`, so for len in [65528,65535] the sum 65536..65543 WRAPS to udplen in [0,7]; `skb_alloc(udplen + IPV4_HDR_LEN)` (udp.c:50) then under-allocates (e.g. 27 bytes), `skb_reserve(IPV4_HDR_LEN)` consumes 20, leaving 7, and the FIRST `skb_put(skb, UDP_HDR_LEN=8)` (udp.c:54) exceeds the tail so skb_put returns NULL (skbuff.h bounds-checks), and the immediately following `hdr->src_port = ...` (udp.c:55) writes through NULL -> kernel #PF -> panic. Confirmed reachable: user_buf_check validates the full u64 len against the user address space, so a user just mmaps a >=64 KiB buffer and sends it; there was NO MTU/size validation anywhere before udp_send_ex. Confirmed IPv4 sets Don't-Fragment (ipv4.c flags_frag=0x4000) so the IP total_len field (also a 16-bit field formed as `(uint16_t)(IPV4_HDR_LEN + payload_len)`, ipv4.c:126) is a SIBLING wrap of the same class. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, single chokepoint per layer, in ONE commit): (1) widened udp_send/udp_send_ex to take `uint32_t len` (full width -- the narrowing is eliminated, not pushed around) and added `if (len > UDP_MAX_PAYLOAD) return -EMSGSIZE;` as the FIRST statement of udp_send_ex (the single sink both senders funnel through), where UDP_MAX_PAYLOAD = 65507 (a new udp.h constant = 65535 - IPV4_HDR_LEN(20) - UDP_HDR_LEN(8), the exact largest payload that overflows NEITHER 16-bit length field); with len bounded <= 65507, `UDP_HDR_LEN + len <= 65515 < 65536` so udplen cannot wrap. (2) Added the UNIVERSAL L3 backstop at the IP chokepoint: `if (skb->len > 0xFFFF - IPV4_HDR_LEN) return -EMSGSIZE;` at the top of ipv4_send_ex, so the IP total_len field cannot wrap for ANY L4 protocol (UDP/TCP/ICMP all funnel through here -- one shared correct mechanism). (3) The socket callers now pass the full-width len (no cast) and surface the size error -- `if (r < 0) return (r == -EMSGSIZE) ? r : -EIO;` -- so an oversize send returns -EMSGSIZE (POSIX "Message too long") instead of silently truncating + lying about the byte count (the old `(uint16_t)len` for e.g. len=100000 sent 34464 bytes but returned 100000). (4) Added EMSGSIZE (90) to errno.h (was missing; the Linux-numbered gap at 90). verify-all-angles: len==0 rejected earlier (`!len` -> -EINVAL in both senders); len exactly UDP_MAX_PAYLOAD accepted with udplen=65515 (no wrap) and IP total=65535 (no wrap); len in the old wrap window [65528,65535] now -EMSGSIZE (no panic); a huge len (100000, UINT32_MAX) -EMSGSIZE; skb_alloc OOM still NULL-checked (udp.c:51, unchanged); DHCP and all legit small datagrams (<1500 B) far below the cap so the valid path is byte-identical; the IP backstop never fires for DHCP/ARP/TCP (their skbs are tiny) so no TX regression; skb_put/skb_alloc/skb_reserve all take uint32_t so widening len introduces no NEW narrowing. VERIFICATION: a NEW deterministic selftest udp_send_size_selftest (registered in main.c) asserts (a) the cap is the exact no-wrap boundary for BOTH 16-bit fields, and (b) udp_send_ex returns -EMSGSIZE for len in {UDP_MAX_PAYLOAD+1, 65528, 65535, 100000, UINT32_MAX} -- the reject path returns at the first statement so it never touches the network or the dummy buffer, making it a pure, side-effect-free unit test of the wrap fix. `[udp_size] SELF-TEST PASSED (oversize UDP rejected, no u16 wrap)`. The VALID send path is boot-exercised end-to-end: DHCP IS UDP sent through socket_sendto -> udp_send_ex and the IP backstop, so reaching `ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2` proves the full-width-len path delivers correctly. First two boots hit the flaky F55 userspace-start stall (net MAC up, login renders `More login:`, /bin/net + /bin/login paged, 0 faults, 77 selftests PASSED incl. [udp_size], no DHCP -- F55 is unrelated to the UDP send path: DHCP packets are ~300 B, far below the cap, so the valid path is unchanged and a real break would be deterministic not flaky); the 3rd SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease at ~3s, 77 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. The sibling LOW/latent truncations the sweep found (fs ext2_vfs_pread u64->u32 offset [bounded by i_size], dir_remove_entry name_len u8 clamp asymmetry [gated by dir_lookup], the `(uint32_t)(len-total)` read/write loop casts [clamped per-block]; mm/syscall shmem/mmap page-count u64->u32 [bounded by shmem_get_page]; the eth/ipv4 TX-path under-send casts [now backstopped by the IP guard]) are recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #9 as audited-not-reachable. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F124 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #10, the sys_readdir kernel-heap info-leak): readdir(2) on any directory an unprivileged process can read disclosed up to ~64 KiB of uninitialized kmalloc heap (freed kernel objects, pointers, other files' data) to userspace (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). FOUND by the SCAN #10 info-leak sweep -- flagged INDEPENDENTLY by TWO agents (the fs+vfs and the mm+proc+syscall sweeps), strong corroboration. INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): sys_readdir allocates `kbuf = kmalloc(max_entries * sizeof(ext2_entry_t))` (syscall.c:1776) -- plain kmalloc, NOT zeroed (confirmed kmalloc at kheap.c:66 returns raw memory; kzalloc does not exist in this kernel; contrast sys_stat/sys_fstat which __builtin_memset their out struct). ext2_entry_t (ext2.h:113-118) is `char name[256] + uint32 inode_num + uint32 size + uint8 is_dir`, NOT packed -> sizeof 268 with 3 trailing pad bytes (offsets 265-267). Every directory filler -- ext2_readdir (ext2.c), dev_readdir (virtfs.c), proc_readdir (proc.c), and the inline /proc + /dev root-injection (syscall.c:1819-1824) -- writes only name[0..nlen]+NUL plus inode_num/size/is_dir, leaving name[nlen+1..255] AND the 3 pad bytes uninitialized; then copy_to_user(ubuf, kbuf, count * sizeof(ext2_entry_t)) (syscall.c:1833) ships the FULL 268-byte struct per entry. Leak per entry = (255 - nlen) name-tail bytes + 3 pad bytes of stale heap; max_entries capped at 256, so one call discloses up to ~64 KiB. Reachable by any unprivileged process on any readable directory (CWD, /, /proc, /dev). FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, single chokepoint -- no per-filler drift): `__builtin_memset(kbuf, 0, max_entries * sizeof(ext2_entry_t))` immediately after the alloc, BEFORE any filler runs, so every entry's name-tail + padding is zero regardless of which of the 4+ fillers (in 3 files) populates it -- one zeroing at the copy-out owner covers them all (the directive's "zero the buffer, do not per-field-patch the fillers that drift"). verify-all-angles: the happy path is unchanged (fillers overwrite name[0..nlen]+fields into the now-zeroed slots; the copied bytes are identical except the previously-stale tail is now 0); the OOM/lookup/unveil/ENOTDIR early-returns are untouched; only `count` entries are copied but zeroing the whole allocation is correct + simplest (cost: a <=68 KiB memset per readdir, negligible vs the disk I/O). VERIFICATION: a stale-heap disclosure is not a panic so there is no fault to catch -> code-proof (the buffer is zeroed before any user-visible byte is written) + a NEW deterministic selftest out_struct_zerofill_selftest (PINS sizeof(ext2_entry_t)==268 so a future field-add that creates uncovered padding fails the build-boot, and asserts that after the zero-before-fill the name-tail + the 3 pad bytes are 0) + the readdir SUCCESS path is BOOT-EXERCISED: svcmgr opendir/readdir's /etc/services every boot, so reaching the DHCP lease (net.svc spawned via readdir) proves the zeroing did not break readdir. First boot reached the DHCP lease at ~3s (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15, 78 selftests PASSED incl. [out_zerofill], 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. Fixed together with F125 (same class -- unzeroed copy-out). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F125 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #10 sibling, the sys_uname kernel-stack info-leak): uname(2) disclosed ~349 bytes of uninitialized kernel stack (saved registers, kernel pointers) to any unprivileged caller (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). FOUND by the SCAN #10 sweep (the mm+proc+syscall agent). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): sys_uname (syscall.c:4090) declares `utsname_t u;` as an UNINITIALIZED stack local; utsname_t (syscall.h:429-436) is 6 x char[65] = 390 bytes, no padding; it is filled by strncpy_k (syscall.c:4074), which -- UNLIKE POSIX strncpy -- copies only strlen+1 bytes per field (`for (i=0; i<n-1 && src[i]; i++) dst[i]=src[i]; dst[i]='\0';`) and does NOT zero-pad the remainder of each 65-byte field; then copy_to_user(buf_ptr, &u, sizeof(u)) (syscall.c:4102) ships all 390 bytes. Written = the 6 short strings + NULs (~41 bytes); leaked = ~349 bytes of stale stack after each field's NUL. Reachable by any unprivileged process, deterministically, every uname() call. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, the file's established zero-then-fill convention): `__builtin_memset(&u, 0, sizeof(u))` before the strncpy_k fills (matching sys_stat/sys_fstat which already memset their out struct), so the tail of every field is zero. Left strncpy_k's contract unchanged (it is uname-only here but changing it to zero-pad like POSIX strncpy could affect other future callers; zeroing the struct is the more future-proof fix -- it also covers any padding a future non-char field would add). verify-all-angles: the returned strings are byte-identical (strncpy_k still writes them); the EINVAL(!buf_ptr)/EFAULT paths are untouched; the struct is now fully defined before the copy. VERIFICATION: code-proof (the struct is zeroed before any field is written) + the out_struct_zerofill_selftest PINS sizeof(utsname_t)==390 and asserts the per-field tail + an untouched field are 0 after the zero-before-fill + a clean boot (the memset cannot break the happy path -- it only zeroes before filling). 78 selftests PASSED incl. [out_zerofill], 0 faults, `More login:` renders. RECORDED (not fixed -- dead): proc_stat (fs/proc.c:538) fills a partial `struct stat` without zeroing it, but it has NO caller anywhere (the live /proc stat path is sys_stat's is_virtual branch, which memsets); a latent footgun if ever wired up, recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #10. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F126 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #11, the fork/spawn/thread fd-table lock-free vfs_dup use-after-free -- a 3-site cluster): copying the parent/source fd table into a new task did `cft->fd_table[i] = vfs_dup(pft->fd_table[i])` with NO lock, so when the fd table is SHARED across threads (THREAD_SHARE_FILES) a sibling thread's concurrent sys_close() could free a file in the window between the slot read and vfs_dup, and vfs_dup then loads f->refcount on freed memory -> an unprivileged use-after-free (kernel/proc/process.c task_fork, kernel/syscall/syscall.c sys_thread, kernel/proc/elf.c resolve_stdio). FOUND by the SCAN #11 TOCTOU sweep (the mm+proc+syscall agent). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): vfs.h:82-84 EXPLICITLY documents that a lock-free observed file pointer MUST use vfs_tryget (CAS-if-nonzero), NOT vfs_dup -- vfs_dup (vfs.h:85-88) does an unconditional `if (refcount>0) fetch_add`, which dereferences f on possibly-freed memory; vfs_close (vfs.h:109-119) frees via f->close(f) on the 1->0 transition; sys_close (syscall.c:558) NULLs the slot under task_files_t.lock then vfs_close()es OUTSIDE the lock, so while the lock is held a non-NULL slot is guaranteed live (its own ref keeps refcount>=1 and close cannot have NULLed+freed it). The three sites' in-code comments justified omitting the lock with "fork runs in the parent's own task context so its own table is only mutated by itself" -- which is FALSE once sibling threads share the table. Confirmed the table itself is also at risk: a concurrent fd_table_grow RCU-frees the old fdtable_t, so the lock-free `pft = ...->ft` snapshot could also go stale. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, single shared mechanism): extracted `fd_table_clone(dst, src)` (process.c) which takes src->lock, snapshots src->ft, fd_table_init(dst, cap), and vfs_dup's every slot + copies fd_flags UNDER the lock, then unlocks -- so a non-NULL slot is always live (safe vfs_dup) and src->ft is pinned against grow; returns 0 on OOM (dst->ft left NULL, which task_files_release handles). task_fork and sys_thread (identical full-clone shape) now call it AND handle the OOM return (the old code ignored fd_table_init's return -> a latent NULL-deref on OOM, fixed here too). resolve_stdio (a single-fd dup, which additionally DOUBLE-FETCHED the slot -- `ft->fd_table[fd]` read once in the `&&` guard then again in vfs_dup) now reads the slot ONCE under g_current->files_shared->lock (vfs_dup(NULL) handles an empty slot). vfs_dup and the fdtable_alloc kmalloc never sleep, so holding the spinlock across them is sound (fd_table_grow already allocates under this same lock; no lock-order cycle -- task_fork/sys_thread/resolve_stdio hold no other lock here, and the fd-table lock is a leaf taken alone by close/install/dup). verify-all-angles: the single-threaded fork/spawn/thread path is unchanged in behavior (same fds dup'd, same flags, same cap); the OOM path now releases cleanly instead of NULL-derefing; resolve_stdio's fd==-2 (/dev/null) and spec==NULL (tty0) early-returns are preserved (they return before the lock); FD_CLOEXEC flags still propagate; no new lock nests with the mm/rcu locks. VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU UAF is not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (the lock makes a non-NULL slot guaranteed-live, mirroring the established sys_close/fd_install discipline) + a NEW deterministic selftest fd_table_clone_selftest (clones a small table and asserts cap + each slot pointer + flags are copied and each cloned file's refcount is bumped -- pins the clone logic) + HEAVY boot-exercise: EVERY process spawn/fork/thread-create clones the fd table through fd_table_clone and resolves stdio through resolve_stdio (svcmgr, /bin/net, /bin/login, shells), so a clean boot with login rendering `More login:` (login spawned with a working tty stdio fd) and the DHCP lease (/bin/net spawned correctly) proves the clone + stdio paths produce correct fd tables. First two boots hit the flaky F55 userspace-start stall (net MAC up, login renders, 0 faults, 79 selftests PASSED incl. [fd_clone], no DHCP -- F55 is unrelated: login spawning correctly PROVES the spawn path works, and a real break would be deterministic); the 3rd SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease at ~3s, 79 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. The OTHER SCAN #11 findings are recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md for follow-up: the sys_spawn stdio_ptr[0] raw re-read double-fetch (syscall.c:1471 re-reads user memory instead of the kernel snapshot stdio[0] -> a sibling munmap in the wide elf_exec window #PF-panics the kernel -- a one-line fix queued next), the 4-site TCP lost-wakeup (check-then-publish-waiter without re-check -> hang), and the HIGH path-TOCTOU on unlink/rename/mkdir/open+O_CREAT (resolve-check-then-resolve-again-by-path -> wrong-directory op; needs a resolve-once-to-inode redesign). io_uring SQE execution is single-fetch-safe (dispatch_exec snapshots the whole SQE) -- the prime double-fetch surface is already mitigated. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F127 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #11, the sys_spawn stdio_ptr double-fetch -> unprivileged kernel #PF panic): sys_spawn copy_from_user'd the user int[3] stdio spec into a kernel local `stdio[]` (syscall.c:1370-1380, with an EFAULT return on a bad pointer), but the job-control branch later RE-READ `((const int*)stdio_ptr)[0]` RAW from user memory (syscall.c:1471) instead of the validated snapshot -> a classic double-fetch TOCTOU: a sibling thread (shared address space) can munmap the stdio_ptr page during the WIDE window (the intervening elf_exec_from_ext2 does ext2 disk I/O + ELF parse + address-space build), making the raw read #PF in kernel mode with no fault-fixup -> an unprivileged kernel panic (DoS); or flip the value so the controlling-tty grant decision disagrees with the stdio the child was actually built from. FOUND by the SCAN #11 TOCTOU sweep (the mm+proc+syscall agent); chosen as this turn's item because the headline TCP lost-wakeup cluster needs a dedicated turn (see the RECORD below). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): stdio[] is `{-1,-1,-1}` by default and is only filled from user memory when stdio_ptr != NULL, and copy_from_user failure returns -EFAULT before line 1471 -- so at the re-read site stdio[] is ALWAYS validly populated (the default for NULL, the validated copy otherwise). The IRONY: line 1372-1374's own comment already says "copy_from_user, not a raw us[i] deref: a kernel/non-canonical/unmapped stdio_ptr would otherwise ... panic the kernel" -- line 1471 reintroduced exactly that raw deref it warns against. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, use the single validated snapshot): replaced `if (!stdio_ptr || (((const int*)stdio_ptr)[0] == -1))` with `if (stdio[0] == -1)`. This is EXACTLY equivalent -- when stdio_ptr is NULL stdio[0] is the default -1 (matching the old `!stdio_ptr`), and when non-NULL stdio[0] holds the copied value (matching the old `[0]==-1`) -- but reads the kernel local, never re-dereferencing user memory. verify-all-angles: NULL stdio_ptr -> stdio[0]==-1 -> grant ctty (same as before); non-NULL inherit (-1) -> grant; non-NULL explicit fd (>=0) -> no grant (same); the copy-failure path already returned EFAULT earlier (unreachable here); no other raw stdio_ptr deref remains (grep confirms 1471 was the only one). VERIFICATION: the panic needs a sibling munmap mid-elf_exec (impractical to forge in a selftest) -> code-proof (the raw user deref is gone; the value used is the already-validated snapshot) + sys_spawn is HEAVILY boot-exercised: svcmgr spawns every service and /bin/login through this exact path, and login rendering `More login:` proves the job-control branch (now reading stdio[0]) correctly grants the controlling tty (login inherits the parent tty, stdio[0]==-1). First boot reached the DHCP lease at ~3s (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15, 79 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. No new selftest (the fix removes a raw user deref in favor of an existing validated local -- not unit-testable, and the spawn path is a per-boot live guard; matches the F122 precedent). DEFERRED + RE-DESIGNED (the SCAN #11 headline, the TCP blocking-wait lost-wakeup, tcp.c 4 sites): VERIFIED the bug is real (pcb_wake gates the wake on a plain-read pcb->waiter, and the 4 consumers check-cond-then-publish-waiter-then-sleep with the publish AFTER the check), but determined the CORRECT fix is NOT a minimal publish-then-recheck on the lockless pcb->waiter: that is a store-load (Dekker) pattern -- consumer `store waiter; load cond` vs producer `store cond; load waiter` with NO common lock around waiter -- so on x86 TSO it needs explicit seq_cst fences on BOTH sides to actually close the window (the sched_sleep wake_pending interlock CANNOT help because the wake is dropped at pcb_wake BEFORE sched_wake is ever called). The robust fix is to converge the 4 sites onto the lock-serialized wait_queue + WAIT_EVENT_HOOK (wait.h) -- which is correct-by-construction (the rq_lock in sched_sleep/sched_wake + the wait_queue serialize publish-vs-wake, no hand-rolled fences) and additionally fixes the pcb->waiter single-waiter limitation -- but that is a substantial refactor of the core net blocking paths (pcb struct + pcb_wake + 4 sites across tcp.c/socket.c) whose blocking-with-contention behavior is NOT strongly boot-exercised, so it needs a DEDICATED turn that also builds a real blocking-wait test harness (a regression there would HANG TCP, worse than the rare race). Recorded with this full design in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #11. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F128 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #11 recorded residual, the io_uring IORING_OP_DRM_COMMIT fixed-file refcount LEAK): the DRM_COMMIT opcode handler took a file reference via sqe_fdget but never released it, so every DRM_COMMIT op leaked one reference on the target file (kernel/io/io_uring.c). FOUND by the SCAN #11 TOCTOU sweep (the drivers+io agent flagged it as an out-of-class refcount leak). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): sqe_fdget (io_uring.c:559) returns a file with its refcount BUMPED -- vfs_tryget for an IOSQE_FIXED_FILE (line 576) or uring_fdget for a regular fd (580) -- and uring_fdput (464) is just vfs_close (the matching unref); the IORING_OP_READ (933-950) and IORING_OP_WRITE (954-964) handlers call uring_fdput(f) on EVERY exit path (the user_buf_check error branch AND the success path), but IORING_OP_DRM_COMMIT (1044-1053) did `f = sqe_fdget(...); if (!f) break; res = drm_ring_atomic(f, sqe->addr); break;` with NO uring_fdput before the break -> the +1 ref taken by sqe_fdget is never dropped. Confirmed DRM_COMMIT was the LONE leaker by auditing all three sqe_fdget call sites (READ/WRITE balanced; DRM_COMMIT not) and confirming the other fd-bearing opcodes do NOT use sqe_fdget at all -- SEND/RECV/CONNECT/ACCEPT route through sys_sendto/sys_recvfrom/sys_connect/sys_accept (which do their own internal fdget/fdput), CLOSE through sys_close, OPENAT through sys_open. Impact: an unprivileged process driving io_uring DRM_COMMIT (the zero-syscall DRM atomic-commit fast path) leaks a file reference per commit; for a FIXED file the leaked ref means its refcount never reaches 0, so IORING_UNREGISTER_FILES / ring teardown can never vfs_close it -> a permanently leaked vfs_file_t (+ its backing DRM object) per commit -> unbounded kernel-memory growth under a commit loop (a local DoS). FIX (do-it-right, mirror the established READ/WRITE balance): added `uring_fdput(f);` before the break in the DRM_COMMIT case, so sqe_fdget's ref is released on the success path (the `if (!f) break` path took no ref, so it needs none) -- now all three sqe_fdget sites are get/put-balanced on every exit. verify-all-angles: the !f (EBADF) path is unchanged (no get -> no put); the success path now puts exactly once; drm_ring_atomic does not consume/store the ref (it uses f transiently, like vfs_read/vfs_write), so the single put after it is correct; no double-put (only one put added, on the one path that got a ref). VERIFICATION: a refcount LEAK is not a crash -> code-proof (the get at sqe_fdget now has a matching put on every path, identical to READ/WRITE) is the direct proof + the io_uring path is boot-exercised -- [io_uring_test] (create -> NOP batch + 100-round steady-state enter/dispatch/complete -> close) and [io_ring_idx] PASS, proving the dispatch/fdput plumbing is unbroken. First boot reached the DHCP lease at ~3s (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15, 79 selftests PASSED incl. [io_uring_test]/[io_ring_idx], 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. No new selftest (a get/put balance is proven by inspection + the existing io_uring test exercises the dispatch path; matches the F118-style refcount-balance precedent). *** This was the FALLBACK item: the turn's PRIMARY target (the recorded HIGH path-TOCTOU on unlink/rename/mkdir/open+O_CREAT) was VERIFIED in depth but DEFERRED -- see the design note in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #11. Key finding from that investigation: the 4 mutating ops have DIFFERENT internal structures -- ext2_unlink/ext2_mkdir/ext2_rename resolve their parent(s) once and operate on them directly (a perm check moved into the op would be clean), but ext2_create DELEGATES the actual creation to ext2_write_file (which re-resolves the path internally AND is shared with ext2_truncate, which has different perm semantics), so a correct ext2_create fix cannot just check ext2_create's own parent_ino -- it needs the check at ext2_write_file's create site without affecting truncate. That, plus the weak boot-exercise of the mutating ops (a regression could break file creation -> boot, or loosen perms), makes the correct 4-op fix need a DEDICATED turn with a create/unlink/mkdir/rename selftest harness. The rename dst-parent permission gap (sys_rename checks only the SRC parent) is recorded there too -- it should be fixed in the same eventual change. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F129 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #11 HIGH headline, the mutating-fs-op path-TOCTOU -- the LAST hard SCAN #11 item, landed with a test harness): unlink/rename/mkdir/open+O_CREAT did TWO independent path resolutions -- the syscall layer resolved the parent dir + checked WRITE|EXEC, then the ext2 op RE-resolved the path from scratch with NO perm re-check -- so a concurrent rename of an intermediate path component between the two could make the destructive op (delete/replace/create) land in a directory whose write permission was never validated: an unprivileged wrong-directory operation (kernel/fs/ext2.c + ext2.h + syscall.c). FOUND by the SCAN #11 TOCTOU sweep (the fs+vfs agent), investigated in depth last turn (the design + the ext2_create wrinkle were captured in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md), executed this turn. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, single shared mechanism + a test harness FIRST): extracted ext2_dir_write_ok(dir_ino, cred) -- reads the dir inode, builds an inode_perm_t, returns vfs_check_perm(WRITE|EXEC) -- and called it INSIDE each mutating op on the parent inode the OP ITSELF resolves and is about to modify, so the permission decision and the modification are on ONE resolution (a swapped intermediate dir is now DENIED by the op's own check instead of acted on): ext2_unlink (gate parent_ino before dir_remove_entry), ext2_mkdir (gate parent_ino before alloc_inode so a denial leaks nothing), ext2_rename (gate BOTH src_parent_ino AND dst_parent_ino under s_rename_lock), and -- the hard one -- ext2_create, which delegates the actual creation to ext2_write_file (which re-resolves the path AND is shared with ext2_truncate): added the check INSIDE ext2_write_file on its CREATE path only (`if (!existing_ino && cred && ext2_dir_write_ok(parent_ino, cred)) return 0;`, on ext2_write_file's own parent_ino -- the real create site), with a NULL-cred sentinel so the OVERWRITE/truncate callers (ext2_truncate / ext2_truncate_to, which act on an EXISTING file and never create) skip it -- so truncate is provably unaffected. All four ops gained a `const void* cred` param (cred_t*); the 4 syscall callers pass &g_current->cred. BONUS (recorded permission gap, fixed in the same change): sys_rename only perm-checked the SRC parent at the syscall layer, so a rename INTO a no-write directory wrongly succeeded; ext2_rename now checks BOTH parents, closing it. DESIGN: the syscall-layer checks are LEFT UNTOUCHED -- they provide the EACCES errno + early reject in the common case; the op-internal check is the authoritative TOCTOU-closer (a lost race returns 0 -> ENOENT, acceptable). The op-internal check uses the IDENTICAL vfs_check_perm(parent, cred, WRITE|EXEC) the syscall used, so in the non-racing case it gives the SAME decision -> ZERO behavior change for normal ops; root bypasses DAC-write and dirs carry the x bit, so boot (all-root) is unaffected. verify-all-angles: root passes (boot unbroken); a non-root denied op still gets EACCES from the syscall check first (unchanged); the racing/dst-gap cases now correctly deny; relative paths + parent==root resolve the same; unveil stays at the syscall layer on the (fixed) path string; rename's same-inode + dir-into-own-subtree guards untouched (the perm check is after the parents resolve, before the dst-removal); the OOM/rollback paths in each op are unchanged; ext2_write_file's overwrite path is byte-identical (NULL cred -> check skipped). VERIFICATION (this is why the turn led with the harness -- the mutating ops are weakly boot-exercised): a NEW deterministic selftest ext2_perm_op_selftest (registered in main.c, runs after ext2 is mounted) exercises create -> resolve -> unlink -> gone, mkdir -> resolve, and create -> rename a->b -> old-gone+new-present -> unlink, ALL with a root cred, asserting every state transition -- so a regression in any of the 4 ops (broken plumbing, wrong inode, a denial of an authorized op) FAILS the selftest. `[fs_permop] SELF-TEST PASSED (root create/unlink/mkdir/rename via in-op perm check)`. First boot hit the flaky F55 stall (net MAC up, login renders `More login:`, /bin/net+svcmgr paged, 0 faults, 80 selftests PASSED incl. [fs_permop], no DHCP -- F55 is unrelated: my change only adds perm checks to the MUTATING ops, the READ path [ext2_open/ext2_vfs_read used by svcmgr to read /etc/services] and the net path are UNTOUCHED, and [fs_permop] passing proves the ops work); the 2nd SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease at ~3s (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2), 80 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. ext2_dir_write_ok recorded in docs/PRIMITIVES.md (the "permission-check on the op's OWN resolution" idiom). *** The path-TOCTOU is the LAST of the two hard deferred SCAN #11 items to be cleared except the TCP blocking-wait lost-wakeup (still deferred -- needs a wait_queue/WAIT_EVENT_HOOK convergence + a blocking-wait test harness). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F130 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #12, the evdev blocking-read dangling-task use-after-free): a blocking read of /dev/input/eventN stored the reader task raw in c->reader and, on a SIGNAL wake, returned -EINTR WITHOUT clearing it -> a later input event sched_wake'd a FREED task_t once the reader exited with the fd kept open (kernel/drivers/input/evdev.c). FOUND by the SCAN #12 UAF sweep (the drivers+io agent). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): evdev_vfs_read's wait loop set `c->reader = g_current` (evdev.c:256) under d->lock, dropped the lock, sched_sleep'd, then `if (signal_has_actionable(...)) return -EINTR` (evdev.c:259-260) -- returning WITHOUT re-taking d->lock and WITHOUT NULLing c->reader; the producer input_device_emit (evdev.c:186, under d->lock, called from the keyboard/mouse IRQ bridge AND the virtio_input drain kthread) does `if (c->reader) { sched_wake(c->reader); c->reader = NULL; }`, and sched_wake (sched.c) immediately derefs the task: cpu_of_task(t), reads t->state, WRITES t->wake_pending=1, and unlinks t->next from a sleep list. Confirmed c->reader has exactly ONE setter (evdev.c:256) and is cleared only by the producer (180/186) + client-init (623), so the -EINTR path was the lone leaver. Trigger (unprivileged, multi-step): open /dev/input/eventN, SHARE the fd (a CLONE_FILES sibling thread or a fork child holds the same vfs_file_t -> the evdev_client_t c outlives the reader task), the reader blocks on the empty ring (sets c->reader), a deliverable signal makes read() return -EINTR (c->reader left dangling), the reader task exits -> task_free_rcu frees the task_t and its slab is reused, but evdev_vfs_close never runs (refcount>0) so c + the stale c->reader survive; the next input event (a keypress / mouse move from the IRQ, or the virtio_input kthread) walks d->clients and sched_wake's the freed-and-reallocated task -> a freed-slab READ + WRITE (wake_pending + sleep-list next) driven asynchronously by a device IRQ -> runqueue/scheduler corruption. signalfd has the CORRECT pattern for exactly this (signalfd_disown_all NULLs the owner under its lock from task_free_rcu); evdev's c->reader EINTR path was the gap. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, disown-under-the-lock on every wake -- mirrors how the producer already clears it + signalfd's disown discipline): after sched_sleep returns, RE-TAKE d->lock and `if (c->reader == g_current) c->reader = NULL;` BEFORE checking the signal / looping, then on -EINTR unlock and return. This makes the read path's c->reader handling EXHAUSTIVE: every blocking-read exit (EAGAIN never set it; data-available -> producer cleared it; signal-EINTR -> now cleared) leaves c->reader not pointing at this task, so when the task later exits it cannot dangle -- and a task is never freed while sleeping in the syscall (it is woken, unwinds through this clear, returns, THEN exits), so the clear always runs first. The `== g_current` guard clears only OUR entry, so a second reader thread that overwrote c->reader (the pre-existing single-waiter limitation) is left intact. verify-all-angles: the producer-wake path is unchanged (c->reader already NULL at the re-check -> the guard is a no-op); the SIGKILL-while-blocked case unwinds through the same EINTR clear before exit; all c->reader accesses (set/clear/producer) are under d->lock so no new race; the nonblock/EAGAIN path never sets c->reader; the data-available path is byte-identical. VERIFICATION: a cross-context UAF (read-EINTR vs a later IRQ-driven wake) is not deterministically reproducible in a kernel selftest -> code-proof (c->reader can no longer point at a task that has left the read path) + the evdev path is BOOT-EXERCISED: event0/1/2 register (PS/2 keyboard + mouse + virtio tablet), the keyboard/mouse IRQ bridges feed input_device_emit, and [evdev_ring] SELF-TEST PASSED (locked emit/drain + client unlink) exercises the producer/ring path. First boot reached the DHCP lease at ~3s (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15, 80 selftests PASSED incl. [evdev_ring], 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. The OTHER new UAFs the sweep surfaced are recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #12 for follow-up: (HIGH) dcache_invalidate frees a dentry UNCONDITIONALLY (no refcount check, unlike the shrinker's DCACHE_REF_DYING CAS) while a path-walk holds it by refcount alone outside RCU -> a freed read of child_ino + a freed WRITE via dcache_put (cascading dentry UAF + LRU corruption); (MED) socket_bind RCU-frees the old TCP pcb while another thread on the same shared fd derefs s->pcb in connect/send/recv outside rcu_read_lock (a freed write into the pcb rings, one-shot); (LOW/latent) mm_clone refs/dups raw VMA-backing pointers snapshotted in a CLOSED rcu section (should shmem_tryget/vfs_tryget like the fault path), signal_setup_frame walks the VMA list without rcu_read_lock (the lone mm_vma_find caller missing it), the pcache_evict_inode lock-order-inversion double-free (dead -- no caller); and a FLAGGED-needs-runtime-check do_switch c->switching_from dangling-write after the reaper (could not be statically confirmed). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F131 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #12, the dcache_invalidate unconditional-free use-after-free): dcache_invalidate / dcache_invalidate_subtree freed a dentry UNCONDITIONALLY (no refcount check), so a dentry a path walk still held BY REFCOUNT could be RCU-freed under its holder -> a freed read + a freed refcount-- WRITE (kernel/fs/dcache.c). FOUND by the SCAN #12 UAF sweep (the fs+vfs agent), recorded last turn as the strongest HIGH follow-up. INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): dentry_unlink_and_free_locked (dcache.c) did `call_rcu_head(&d->rcu_head, dentry_free_cb, d)` with NO refcount check, and BOTH dcache_invalidate (462) and dcache_invalidate_subtree (476) called it directly on whatever dentry bucket_find_locked returned -- including a HELD one. dcache_lookup hands out a REFCOUNT-pinned (not rcu-pinned) handle: it CAS-bumps refcount then `rcu_read_unlock()` BEFORE `return d` (dcache.c:268-269), so a path-walk holder (ext2_lookup_path reads d->child_ino then dcache_put(d), with a preemption point between) is NOT inside any rcu section. The freer: a concurrent unlink/rename/create/mkdir on the SAME (parent_ino, name) -> dcache_invalidate -> call_rcu. With QSBR counting the holder's preemption as a quiescent state, the grace period can close and dentry_free_cb free + pmm_slab_free(d) BEFORE the holder's dcache_put -> the holder reads a freed child_ino AND dcache_put's `__atomic_sub_fetch(&d->refcount,...)` WRITES into a reused SLAB_TYPESAFE_BY_RCU slot, which can drive a DIFFERENT live dentry's refcount to 0, queue it on the LRU while still held+hash-linked, and let the shrinker free it under its real holder -> cascading dentry UAF + LRU corruption. Confirmed the ASYMMETRY: the SHRINKER path was already hardened against exactly this -- it CAS's refcount 0 -> DCACHE_REF_DYING to CLAIM an unreferenced dentry (dcache.c:498-503), and a racing dcache_lookup's resurrect-CAS / dcache_put's last-ref LRU-add lose to it -- but the invalidate path was NOT given the same discipline (it freed regardless of refcount). UNPRIVILEGED, narrow preemption-window race, HIGH consequence. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, fix-BY-ANALOGY to the shrinker -- one shared "claim refcount-0 via CAS, never free a held dentry" discipline): added dentry_invalidate_locked, which the invalidate callers now use instead of the unconditional free. It CAS's refcount 0 -> DCACHE_REF_DYING (the SAME serialization point the shrinker uses vs a concurrent dcache_put's last-ref LRU-add): if the CAS SUCCEEDS the dentry is unreferenced -> dentry_unlink_and_free_locked frees it immediately, exactly as before (so the common unref'd-invalidate case is behavior-identical); if the CAS FAILS the dentry is HELD (refcount > 0) -> it is NOT freed, only UNLINKED FROM THE HASH (the invalidate's real purpose: future lookups miss + re-resolve), and the holder's final dcache_put returns it to the LRU at refcount 0 where the shrinker reclaims it later via its own 0 -> DYING CAS. verify-all-angles: an unref'd dentry (the common case) frees immediately as today; a held dentry is never freed under its holder (the UAF is closed) and is reclaimed exactly once (by the shrinker, refcount 0); future lookups miss immediately (hash-unlinked) and install a fresh/negative dentry; dcache_invalidate_subtree's save-next-before-process iterator is unaffected (the hash-unlink modifies the predecessor's hash_next, not d->hash_next, so the saved `next` stays valid for the RCU walk + the iterator); no double-free (the CAS makes the unref'd free single-winner; the held case never frees in invalidate); no leak (every dentry still freed exactly once); the shrinker path is unchanged (it keeps calling dentry_unlink_and_free_locked after ITS own CAS). VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU UAF (the holder's dcache_put racing the RCU free, requiring a preemption-window quiescence) is not deterministically reproducible single-threaded (the free is RCU-DEFERRED + the callback runs async in rcu_gp_kthread, so synchronize_rcu_expedited cannot force the buggy free inline to make a live_count discriminator reliable) -> code-proof (invalidate now NEVER frees a refcount>0 dentry -- it CAS-claims only refcount-0, identical to the shrinker) + a NEW deterministic behavioral selftest dcache_held_invalidate_selftest (registered in main.c): install a dentry, take a SECOND ref via dcache_lookup (simulate a path-walk holder), dcache_invalidate while held, assert a subsequent dcache_lookup MISSES (hash-unlinked) AND the held dentry is intact (child_ino preserved) AND both dcache_puts complete -- exercising the new held-invalidate branch the boot might not hit deterministically; `[dcache_held] SELF-TEST PASSED (held dentry survives invalidate, hash-unlinked)`. PLUS the dcache is HEAVILY boot-exercised: every path lookup + every unlink/rename/create/mkdir at boot (incl. the F129 ext2_perm_op_selftest's create/unlink/rename) drives dcache_invalidate, and [dcache_test]/[dcache_race] (the existing lookers-vs-shrinker race test) PASS unchanged. First boot reached the DHCP lease at ~3s (no F55): ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15, 81 selftests PASSED incl. [dcache_held]/[dcache_test]/[dcache_race], 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders. The remaining SCAN #12 finding (the MED socket_bind pcb UAF) + the latent ones (mm_clone tryget, signal_setup_frame rcu_read_lock) + the FLAGGED do_switch switching_from (needs a runtime poison check) stay recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #12. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F132 FIXED (BUG-TYPE SCAN #12, the socket_bind TCP pcb use-after-free): socket_bind on a TCP socket FREED + REALLOC'd s->pcb (tcp_pcb_free is RCU-deferred), but every other socket op derefs s->pcb LOCKLESSLY, so a sibling thread on a shared/dup'd fd using the socket while another thread binds it could hold a freed pcb -> a freed write into its 64 KiB rx/tx rings (kernel/net/socket.c + tcp.c + tcp.h). FOUND by the SCAN #12 UAF sweep (the net agent). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): socket_bind (socket.c:336-340) did `tcp_pcb_set_file(s->pcb,NULL); tcp_pcb_free(s->pcb); s->pcb=0;` then tcp_pcb_alloc(port); tcp_pcb_free RCU-defers the free (call_rcu_expedited, unlinks from s_pcb_head). The readers -- sock_poll/socket_connect/socket_send/socket_recv/socket_listen/socket_shutdown/socket_accept -- deref s->pcb with NO rcu_read_lock / socket lock, and socket_bind does NOT drop the file ref (so it is not serialized vs in-flight users). connect/send/recv WRITE into the pcb + its rings. Confirmed Option B (RCU-protect s->pcb) is INFEASIBLE: connect/send/recv BLOCK (sched_sleep), and you cannot hold rcu_read_lock across a sleep, and the pcb is not refcounted -- so pinning the readers would require adding pcb refcounting (very invasive). Confirmed the EPHEMERAL pcb origin: socket_open (socket.c:286) allocs s->pcb = tcp_pcb_alloc(tcp_ephemeral_port()) in TCP_CLOSED state, published on s_pcb_head, with the comment "bind() can override it later"; tcp_ephemeral_port is a bare counter (no reservation table to release). FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, Option C + a POSIX guard -- avoid the free entirely): socket_bind now REBINDS the existing ephemeral pcb's local port IN PLACE via a new accessor tcp_pcb_set_local_port (an atomic store of pcb->local_port -- the pcb is already on s_pcb_head and CLOSED [no traffic], so retargeting demux [pcb_find matches local_port] needs no free/realloc), so s->pcb NEVER changes -> no reader can ever observe a freed pcb. Plus a guard: bind is allowed ONLY on a TCP_CLOSED pcb; a connected/listening pcb (state != CLOSED, reachable with s->bound still 0 since connect()/listen() use the ephemeral pcb without a prior bind) is rejected with -EINVAL (POSIX-correct -- you cannot bind an in-use socket -- AND an in-place port change would corrupt a live connection's/listener's demux; the OLD free+realloc would have DESTROYED such a connection AND hit the UAF). verify-all-angles: the normal socket()->bind()->connect()/listen() flow works (fresh CLOSED pcb, rebound in place); a double-bind is still rejected by the pre-existing s->bound check; UDP bind (the SOCK_DGRAM branch) is untouched; no leak (the pcb is reused, not leaked -- it is freed once at socket close); the only residual is a benign local_port data race on a pathological concurrent bind+connect (a uint16 store, never a UAF, since the pcb is never freed). VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU UAF (a sibling deref racing the RCU free) is not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (s->pcb is never freed by bind) + a NEW deterministic selftest socket_bind_rebind_selftest (registered in main.c): (1) a fresh CLOSED TCP socket bound to a port keeps the SAME s->pcb pointer (rebound in place -- the OLD free+realloc would have CHANGED the pointer) with local_port updated, and (2) a LISTENing socket (s->bound still 0) rejects bind with -EINVAL and keeps its pcb untouched. `[sock_bind] SELF-TEST PASSED (rebind in place; non-CLOSED bind rejected, pcb kept)`. PLUS the TCP path is boot-exercised: [tcp_accept]/[tcp_orphan]/[tcp_synreap] PASS (the accept/listener/reaper paths unbroken) and DHCP (UDP) completes. The first two SELFTESTS=1 boots hit a FLAKY mid-selftest HANG at ext2_perm_op_selftest (the F129 fs-mutation selftest running CONCURRENTLY with userland fs access -- a pre-existing flaky stall in the concurrent fs path, NOT caused by this tcp/socket-only change: the 2nd boot still reached DHCP, only the init_kthread selftest sweep stalled); the 3rd SAME-build re-boot ran ALL selftests incl. [sock_bind]/[fs_permop]/[tcp_*], 81 PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], DHCP ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15, `More login:` renders. *** RECORDED as a HIGH-priority follow-up (a real flaky deadlock/stall): ext2_perm_op_selftest hung 2/3 boots -- ext2_create/unlink/mkdir/rename run in init_kthread concurrently with userland (svcmgr reading /etc/services, net.svc) + the shrinker/pcache kthreads, so a lock-order inversion or deadlock in the concurrent ext2-mutation-vs-read path is the likely cause; since the SAME ops are unprivileged-reachable, a real concurrent-fs deadlock would be a DoS. This is a strong lead for SCAN #13 (lock-ordering/deadlock) -- recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md. - 2026-06-27 - F133 FIXED (SCAN #12 residual, the signal_setup_frame mm_vma_find-without-rcu freed-VMA read): signal_setup_frame called mm_vma_find TWICE (signal.c:246-247) with NO rcu_read_lock, violating the mm_vma_find contract -> a concurrent sibling munmap's async vma_free_rcu could free a vma_t mid-walk -> a freed-vma read (garbage start/end/next) (kernel/proc/signal.c). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): mm_vma_find (mm.c:189-193) documents "RCU reader walk. Caller MUST hold rcu_read_lock() for the lifetime of the returned pointer" and walks `rcu_dereference(v->next)`; every vmm.c caller (vmm.c:469/588/724/815/1138) wraps it in rcu_read_lock; signal_setup_frame was the lone exception (the sigframe VMA-coverage check on the signal-delivery path).
