- 2026-06-27 - F134 FIXED (SCAN #12 residual, the mm_clone snapshot-then-ref-in-a-closed-rcu-section UAF): mm_clone (fork's address-space copy, kernel/mm/mm.c) snapshotted each src VMA's backing pointers (v->shmem, v->file) RAW under one rcu_read_lock, rcu_read_unlock'd, then in a SEPARATE rcu section took the refs (shmem_ref / vfs_dup) -- so a concurrent sibling munmap of the same VMA between the snapshot and the ref could free the shmem/file first, and the ref then INCREMENTED a refcount on freed memory (a freed-memory write). FOUND by the SCAN #12 UAF sweep (the mm+proc agent: "snapshot raw, rcu_read_unlock, then ref in a separate rcu section -- unlike the fault path / vmm_clone_user_ex which tryget under the snapshot rcu section"). INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): the snapshot loop (mm.c:313-326) stored v->shmem/v->file raw and rcu_read_unlock'd at 326; the apply loop (329-352) did shmem_ref(snap[k].shmem)/vfs_dup(snap[k].file) in a NEW rcu section (336-350) that pins only the DST lookup, not the SRC backing object; confirmed shmem_tryget (shmem.h:77, returns int, bumps the ref iff alive) / vfs_tryget (vfs.h:96, returns the ptr or NULL) are the safe primitives the fault path uses, and mm_destroy already releases each VMA's shmem/file backing ref (shmem_unref/vfs_close). Latent today behind the ~10 ms async vma-free latency (vma_free_rcu is call_rcu_head, not expedited), but a genuine UAF that goes live if the clone loop stalls past the free latency or vma_free is ever made expedited. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, mirror the fault path's tryget-while-alive): take the ref INSIDE the snapshot rcu section -- `snap[i].shmem = (v->shmem && shmem_tryget(v->shmem)) ? v->shmem : NULL; snap[i].file = v->file ? vfs_tryget(v->file) : NULL;` -- so the backing object is pinned WHILE the src VMA (which holds it alive) is rcu-protected, and the apply loop just HANDS the already-pinned pointer to the dst VMA (no second ref). verify-all-angles: on mm_vma_add OOM at index k, snap[0..k-1] are already on dst VMAs (mm_destroy releases them) and snap[k..cnt-1] are still pinned only by snap -> the new cleanup loop shmem_unref/vfs_close's them (no leak); the should-not-happen dv==NULL case also releases the pinned refs; a tryget that FAILS (object mid-teardown) stores NULL -> the dst VMA gets no backing, demand-paging re-resolves (correct); the happy path is unchanged in effect (each backing object ref'd exactly once, handed to the dst VMA). VERIFICATION: a fork-vs-munmap cross-CPU UAF is not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (the ref is now taken under the rcu section that keeps the object alive) + the fork/mm-clone path is HEAVILY boot-exercised (login, svcmgr, and every shell fork+clone the mm through mm_clone). Boot reached the DHCP lease, 82 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], `More login:` renders.
  *** REVISED the SCAN #13 ext2_perm_op-hang diagnosis (the prior "lost AHCI completion -> seqlock-held-across-I/O -> forever hang" was INCOMPLETE/WRONG): re-reading the AHCI completion path proved the lost-completion is ALREADY self-healed -- sched_tick (sched.c:1188) calls ahci_poll_completions UNCONDITIONALLY every tick (1000x/s/CPU) -> ahci_rescan_completions, which both sets s_slot_done AND wait_queue_wake_all(s_slot_wq[slot]) (ahci.c:588-589). So a dropped MSI is recovered + the waiter woken within ~1 ms; the forever-hang is NOT a lost AHCI completion. The seqlock-held-across-blocking-I/O is a real latent perf/priority-inversion issue (readers spin during a dir-write I/O) but does NOT explain a 280 s FREEZE (the I/O completes via the tick poll). The TRUE root is still unpinned: the QMP capture showed only the SPINNING reader (CPU#3 in read_inode/irtree_get seqlock retry) + 3 idle CPUs; the ASLEEP seqlock WRITER's blocking point was not captured. NEEDS a deeper dynamic capture (the asleep writer's stack / s_active_mask state / enable SCHED_TICK_HEARTBEAT to tell lost-wakeup-vs-wedge) before a fix can be targeted -- recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SCAN #13 as a dedicated debugging turn. (Flaky, SELFTESTS=1-only -- the shipping disk runs no selftests.) Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F135 FIXED (SCAN #13 ROOT-CAUSED + PROVEN + FIXED: the flaky ext2_perm_op boot HANG was a per-inode seqlock-across-blocking-I/O DEADLOCK): the ext2 per-inode seqlock WRITE side (inode_lock -> seq_write_begin = spin_lock(write_lock) + bump-sequence-ODD) was held across BLOCKING AHCI I/O -- dir_add_entry/inode_writeback/the create+rename publishes do read_block/write_block -> ahci_write -> submit_busy_acquire -> sched_sleep WHILE the leaf's sequence is odd. Meanwhile the seqlock READER irtree_get (inlined into read_inode) spins in seq_begin's cpu_relax INSIDE rcu_read_lock, and rcu_read_lock == preempt_disable. So a reader of that inode spins PREEMPT-DISABLED for the entire time the writer holds the sequence odd. A preempt-disabled spinner cannot be rescheduled, so it MONOPOLISES its CPU; the runnable task needed to release the global AHCI submit lock (s_submit_busy) and wake the sleeping writer can never get that CPU -> a CPU-mediated DEADLOCK that the per-tick AHCI completion self-heal (sched_tick -> ahci_poll_completions) cannot break (the I/O completes, but the writer can never get a CPU to finish + drop the seqlock). This is why the earlier "lost AHCI completion" diagnosis (retracted F134) was wrong about the mechanism while the seqlock-across-I/O instinct was right.
  PROVEN from four independent angles (no-assumptions / real-proof): (1) STATIC: irtree_get wraps seq_begin in rcu_read_lock and writers hold seq odd across write_block; rcu_read_lock==preempt_disable. (2) DISASSEMBLY of read_inode: incl %gs:0x4284 (preempt_disable) at read_inode+0x1b, the pause (cpu_relax) at read_inode+0x94 sits INSIDE that preempt-disabled region (released by decl %gs:0x4284 at +0xa4); the prior live capture RIP read_inode+150 == 0x96 is exactly that pause. (3) LIVE CAPTURE (a temporary inode-lock-hold watchdog + all-task stack dumper, since the existing global-stall watchdog never fires -- the spinner is preemptible so nonidle_switches keeps advancing): trigger=INODE_LOCK_HELD_TOO_LONG, held_by_pid=10 SLEEPING (state=3) holding inode_lock(ino=2) for ~3.4s, with pid=19 RUNNING preempt=1 (preempt-disabled) and the 3 other CPUs idle; the asleep writer's resolved backtrace was dir_add_entry(ext2.c:2034) -> write_block(ext2.c:736) -> submit_busy_acquire(ahci.c) -> sched_sleep, and cpu2 showed nr=1 (a runnable task starved behind the spinner). (4) PERMANENCE: the captured instance never recovered (serial frozen, fs_permop never PASSED).
  FIX (do-it-right, ROOT -- the directive's PRIMARY "decouple the lock from the I/O"): the per-inode seqlock only ever protected the 128-byte leaf->inode snapshot irtree_get copies (it NEVER protected directory data blocks -- those go through bcache separately), so the sequence must be held odd ONLY around the brief IN-MEMORY publish of leaf->inode, never across disk I/O. inode_lock now takes ONLY the embedded write_lock (a plain spinlock -- preemptible, so writer-vs-writer contention self-heals; held across the I/O to serialise same-inode writers + protect dir data blocks) and leaves the sequence EVEN; new inode_pub_begin/inode_pub_end (seq_write_begin_unlocked/seq_write_end_unlocked -- bump only the sequence, write_lock already held) bracket every leaf->inode mutation (9 sites: ext2_vfs_write, dir_add_entry, create-overwrite, create+mkdir new-inode, mkdir/rename parent link counts, and ext2_drop_link_locked which was refactored to compute on a LOCAL copy so free_inode_blocks' bitmap I/O never mutates the cached inode in place). The load path keeps its self-contained brief seq_write_begin/end publish (no I/O under it). Readers now get a consistent pre- or post-publish inode WITHOUT spinning during the writer's I/O -> the preempt-disabled spin (and thus the deadlock) is gone; no fs semantics change.
  VERIFICATION (real-proof, a falsifiable repro): a temporary inode-lock-hold watchdog made the deadlock RELIABLY catchable (fired within ~3s of the hang). PRE-fix the hang reproduced ~1 in 5-6 SELFTESTS=1 boots (caught on boot #5 in two separate runs, with the full [WD] capture above). POST-fix: 40/40 boots CLEAN, ZERO [WD], all fs_permop PASSED (pre-fix that many boots would have shown ~6-8 hangs). All capture instrumentation was then REVERTED; the shipped change is ext2.c-only. Final fix-only boot: 80 selftests PASSED, fs_permop PASSED, DHCP 10.0.2.15, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], full 174-line boot. SCAN #13 (lock-ordering/deadlock) CLOSED. main untouched.
- 2026-06-27 - F136 FIXED (SCAN #14 integer-overflow, lead item): the DRM_IOCTL_MODE_CURSOR (SET_CURSOR/SET_CURSOR2) backing-size guard in drm_ioctl_mode_cursor (kernel/drivers/video/drm.c) computed `(uint64_t)a.width * a.height * 4 > d->size` to reject a cursor whose ARGB pixels exceed its dumb backing. a.width/a.height are u32 copied straight from the user cursor struct (copy_from_user, no cap). The first multiply `(uint64_t)a.width * a.height` is a correct u64 product (two u32 -> max ~2^64-2^33, fits), but the trailing `* 4` then OVERFLOWS u64: with a.width == a.height == 0x80000000 the product is 2^62 and *4 == 2^64 -> wraps to 0, so `0 > d->size` is FALSE and the guard is bypassed. The same `(uint64_t)w*h*4` expression also fed the pin-page count `pages = (w*h*4 + 4095)/4096`, which wraps to 0. Result: user-supplied absurd cursor dimensions (e.g. 2^31 x 2^31) slip past the bound into b->resource_create(id, fmt, w, h) and b->resource_transfer(res, w, h) -- the GPU is told the cursor is ~2^31 x 2^31 while the backing is the small real dumb buffer (host-side OOB read of the backing on transfer/scanout), with a wrapped-to-zero pin count (the pages the device scans are not ref-pinned). This is the canonical "w*h*bpp wrap defeats the size bound" class (siblings F23 drm_dumb_size, F49 vgpu_fb_bytes) -- the one drm.c sizing path that had NOT been routed through a checked primitive.
  FOUND by a codebase-wide SCAN #14 integer-overflow sweep (5 parallel subagents over net / fs / drm+fb / syscall+io_uring+ipc / storage+input). The sweep confirmed the rest of the tree is heavily hardened: net (every total_len-header_len / off+len / count*elem already guarded or min-clamped), fs (every on-disk block# range-checked by ext2_block_valid inside bcache_get, LBAs formed in u64; the one raw wrap is in build-excluded fat32.c), syscall/io_uring/ipc (all backstopped by ckd_add_u64 / _access_ok / per-index npages checks), storage/input (AHCI/nvme DMA sizing via mul_within_u32/xfer_bytes_ok, rings power-of-2 masked). The residual lower-severity items (nvme `1u << lbads` device-shift, hda u8 loop counter, tcp send-window underflow saved-by-next-clamp) are noted in AUDIT_FINDINGS for follow-up. The DRM SET_CURSOR guard was the single user-reachable overflow-defeats-a-bound bug.
  FIX (do-it-right, safe-primitives -- extract a named tested primitive, reuse checked.h): new `// PRIMITIVE drm_cursor_bytes(width, height, backing_size, *bytes)` (drm.c, next to drm_dumb_size) computes width*height (u64 product of two u32, cannot overflow) then guards the *4 with `ckd_mul_u64` and checks `<= backing_size`, returning the byte size. The SET_CURSOR guard now calls it (rejecting 0-dims and any wrap/over-backing) and REUSES the returned cur_bytes for the pin-page count, so the two can never drift. d->size is u64 (capped <= 2^30 by drm_dumb_size's 16384 dim cap), so the check is exact. No behavior change for legitimate cursors; absurd dims are now rejected with -EINVAL. drm.c gained `#include "checked.h"`.
  VERIFICATION: added `drm_cursor_bytes_selftest` (registered in main.c after the other DRM selftests) driving the boundaries -- exact-fit, over-backing, zero-dim, and the THREE overflow edges the old guard accepted: w=h=0x80000000 with a tiny backing (*4 wraps to 0), w=h=0x80000000 with a UINT64_MAX backing (proves the *4 overflow is caught independent of the backing), and w=h=0xFFFFFFFF (w*h*4 overflows u64). Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1). Boot-verified: `[drm_cursor] SELF-TEST PASSED (overflow-safe cursor backing-size)`, alongside [drm_dumb]/[drm_atomic]/[vgpu_fbsz] PASSED and [fs_permop] PASSED (F135 deadlock fix holds), 82 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD]. (Login/DHCP render is gated by the pre-existing flaky F55 net/userspace-start stall, orthogonal to this DRM change; re-booted to confirm.) main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.
- 2026-06-27 - F137 FIXED (SCAN #14 integer-overflow residual #1, the nvme LBADS undefined shift): nvme_init (kernel/drivers/storage/nvme.c) derived the namespace sector size as `s_ns_lba_size = 1u << lbads` where `lbads = (lbaf >> 16) & 0xFF` is the 8-bit LBA Data Size exponent from the device's Identify-Namespace LBA-format descriptor (idbuf, untrusted, 0..255), UNBOUNDED before the shift. `1u << lbads` is UNDEFINED BEHAVIOUR for lbads >= 32 (shift count >= the 32-bit operand width); on x86 the shift masks the count to & 31, so e.g. lbads=32 yields `1u << 0` == 1 -- a bogus 1-byte sector size. That bogus size then feeds nvme_rw's DMA-size guard `mul_within_u32(nlb, s_ns_lba_size, 8192u, &bytes)` (the F47/F48 mul_within hardening): a malicious/buggy controller reporting a small or UB-inducing LBADS makes our computed byte length UNDER-count, so a transfer slips past the 2-PRP (<=8 KiB) bound while the device DMAs at its real (larger) sector size past the PRP region -> OOB DMA write. A sub-512 LBADS (< 9) is the same shape without the UB (size 1..256, guard under-counts); LBADS 13..31 (sectors 8 KiB..2 GiB) is already safely REJECTED by the mul_within guard (size > 8192 fails even nlb=1), so the dangerous inputs are lbads < 9 and lbads >= 32. Recorded as a SCAN #14 residual (sweep of the integer-overflow type) -- nvme is not the boot device, so this is a device-trust-boundary hardening, not a live boot bug.
  FOUND by the SCAN #14 codebase-wide integer-overflow sweep (the storage/input subagent), confirmed against the real code (no-assumptions): line 778 `lbads = (lbaf >> 16) & 0xFF` (u32 masked to 8 bits, the only producer), line 780 the raw `1u << lbads`, line 547 the lone consumer `mul_within_u32(nlb, s_ns_lba_size, 8192, &bytes)`; s_ns_lba_size has no other sizing consumer.
  FIX (do-it-right, safe-primitives -- a named, tested validator, the bug class made impossible): new `// PRIMITIVE nvme_lba_size_ok(lbads, *size)` (next to the s_ns_lba_size declaration) accepts ONLY the driver-supported 512..4096-byte range (lbads 9..12) and computes `1u << lbads` with lbads <= 12 (no UB, no wrap), returning the byte size; everything else returns false. nvme_init now calls it and REFUSES the namespace (`return 0`, nvme unavailable) on an out-of-range LBADS rather than deriving a bogus size -- safer than clamping, since a device we cannot size correctly should not be used as a block device. The raw `1u << lbads` on an unbounded value is gone (forbidden pattern eliminated). nvme.c already includes checked.h.
  VERIFICATION: added `nvme_lba_size_ok_selftest` (registered in main.c after nvme_cid_valid_selftest) driving lbads = 9/10/11/12 (accept, sizes 512/1024/2048/4096), 8 and 0 (sub-512, reject), 13 and 31 (oversized, reject), and the UB edges 32 and 255 (rejected BEFORE the shift, so `1u << 32` is never evaluated). Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1). Boot-verified: `[nvme_lbads] SELF-TEST PASSED (valid 512..4096 LBA size, no UB shift)` alongside [nvme_cid]/[drm_cursor]/[fs_permop] PASSED, 83 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], DHCP 10.0.2.15. (Login render still gated by the pre-existing flaky F55 net/userspace stall, orthogonal.) main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.
- 2026-06-27 - F138 FIXED (SCAN #14 integer-overflow residual #2, the last one: hda.c u8-loop-counter infinite loop): codec_configure (kernel/drivers/audio/hda.c) enumerated the codec node graph with two `for (uint8_t n = start; n < start + count; n++)` loops (the function-group loop at ~225 and the per-FG widget loop at ~233) where start/count are the subordinate-node start + count fields of the device codec's NODE_COUNT parameter (`get_param(cad, nid, PAR_NODE_COUNT)`, two device-supplied u8s). The bound `start + count` promotes to int (max 255+255 == 510), but the loop COUNTER is uint8_t: once start+count > 255 the u8 counter wraps at 255 (255++ -> 0) while the int bound stays ahead, so `n < start+count` is always true -> INFINITE LOOP issuing codec verbs. A malformed/malicious HDA codec reporting an oversized NODE_COUNT thus HANGS audio init (DoS). DoS-only: the counter is only a `nid` arg to get_param (which takes uint8_t nid), never an array index, so there is no OOB -- but a raw u8 counter past 255 would also TRUNCATE and re-process low-numbered nodes, mis-configuring the codec.
  FOUND by the SCAN #14 integer-overflow sweep (the storage/input subagent). VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): both loops confirmed (grep found exactly these two uint8_t loop counters in hda.c, no others); start/count are device NODE_COUNT u8 fields; the counter is a nid arg, no array index (DoS not OOB). hda.c IS compiled (only ac97.c is in KERNEL_EXCLUDE); QEMU has intel-hda on the default machine but the test bootclean.sh omits it, so hda init does not run at boot -- the fix is verified by clean build + the pure-helper selftest + code-proof.
  FIX (do-it-right, safe-primitives -- a tested bound primitive, both sites converted): new `// PRIMITIVE hda_node_scan_end(start, count)` returns the half-open scan end `min(start + count, 256)` -- HDA node ids are u8 (0..255), so the iteration must stay in 0..255; clamping to 256 makes the loop (now driven by a uint32_t counter) ALWAYS terminate AND never iterate into the truncation-wrap zone. Both loops rewritten `for (uint32_t n = start; n < hda_node_scan_end(start, count); n++)` with a `uint8_t nn = (uint8_t)n` local for the get_param nid arg (n <= 255 by the clamp, so nn never truncates). Legitimate codecs (start+count well under 256) are unaffected. The raw u8-counter-vs-device-sum pattern is gone (both instances).
  VERIFICATION: added `hda_node_scan_end_selftest` (registered in main.c after nvme_lba_size_ok_selftest) driving normal small ranges (2+10, 1+14, pass through), empty (0+0 -> 0), the 256 boundary (128+128 -> 256), max-in-byte (0+255 -> 255), and the three infinite-loop inputs the old u8 counter wrapped on (255+1 -> 256, 200+100 -> 256, 255+255 -> 256). Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1). Boot-verified: `[hda_nodes] SELF-TEST PASSED (codec node scan bound clamps to u8 nid space, terminates)` alongside [nvme_lbads]/[drm_cursor]/[fs_permop] PASSED, 84 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], DHCP 10.0.2.15. (Login render gated by the pre-existing flaky F55 net/userspace stall, orthogonal.) SCAN #14 (integer-overflow/wrap) is now FULLY CLOSED -- F136 (DRM SET_CURSOR), F137 (nvme LBADS), F138 (hda node loop); the only remaining noted item is the tcp.c send-window subtraction (saved by its next-line clamp -> not a bug; an optional saturate-to-0 hardening, no fix required). main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.
- 2026-06-27 - F139 FIXED (SCAN #15 error-path-resource-leak, lead item: vmm_get_user_pages permanent pin leak on mid-loop OOM): vmm_get_user_pages (kernel/mm/vmm.c) pins each resolved frame (pmm_pin -- the DMA-target commit) inside its per-page loop (lines 356/376/382), but every mid-loop failure exit -- CoW-break OOM (332), demand-alloc OOM (364), PT-page OOM (371) -- did `ret = 0; goto out;`, and the `out:` label only ran the CoW TLB shootdown and `return ret`. It NEVER unpinned the frames already pinned in iterations [0..i). The sole caller ahci_read_user (kernel/drivers/storage/ahci.c:~907) does `if (!vmm_get_user_pages(...)) return 0;` and only runs its pmm_unpin loop on SUCCESS, so it does not compensate. Because pmm_ref_dec REFUSES to free a pinned frame (pmm.c: "leaking" guard), every frame pinned before the failing page becomes PERMANENTLY un-reclaimable. An unprivileged read into a multi-page user buffer that OOMs mid-pin (CoW break or fault-in of a later page failing under memory pressure) thus leaks pinned pages on every attempt -> memory-exhaustion DoS. This is the REF/PIN-LEAK-ON-ERROR HIGH-value subset of SCAN #15.
  FOUND by the SCAN #15 codebase-wide error-path-leak sweep (6 parallel subagents over fs/net/mm/drivers/syscall+io_uring/proc). The mm subagent flagged it as the one un-handled, caller-unmitigated leak. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions, traced EVERY exit): the three goto-out failure points all precede the iteration-i pin, so at failure exactly out[0..i) are pinned (out[i] is not); the success path returns ret==count and the caller owns/unpins all of them; pmm_pin/pmm_unpin are a balanced g_frame_pincount counter SEPARATE from the buddy refcount (pmm.c:1415-1429), so unpinning a still-mapped frame only drops the DMA pin -- the PTE ref keeps the frame alive (NOT a free, no double-free/UAF).
  FIX (do-it-right, single-exit cleanup at the existing out: label): hoist the loop index `i` to function scope, and at out: (after the CoW shootdown) when ret==0 unpin out[0..i) -- `for (uint32_t j = 0; j < i; j++) pmm_unpin((phys_addr_t)((uint64_t)out[j] - HHDM_OFFSET))`, mirroring the caller's own success-path unpin. Now the function leaves NO pins on failure, matching the caller's contract (success -> caller unpins; failure -> nothing pinned). verify-all-angles: success path unchanged (ret!=0 -> no unpin, no double-unpin); failure at i==0 -> empty loop (nothing pinned yet); count==0 -> i==0 empty loop (no-op); CoW-broken frames stay mapped after unpin (PTE ref holds them), so the partial resolution is a valid state, just without the aborted DMA's pins.
  VERIFICATION: no clean deterministic selftest fits -- vmm_get_user_pages is a fault/DMA path needing page-table + mid-loop OOM injection, not a pure helper -- so this rests on code-proof (the cleanup loop) plus the no-regression boot. Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1). Boot-verified: the AHCI user-read path (ahci_read_user -> vmm_get_user_pages) is exercised during boot (binary demand-paging / reads) with 0 faults; all selftests PASSED (84, incl fs_permop/nvme_lbads/hda_nodes/drm_cursor), 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], DHCP 10.0.2.15. (Login render gated by the pre-existing flaky F55 net/userspace stall, orthogonal.) main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.
- 2026-06-27 - F140 FIXED (SCAN #15 error-path-resource-leak residual #2: process.c task-create PML4/mm leak + NULL-deref): task_create_kthread (kernel/proc/process.c) did `task_mm_t* mm = task_mm_alloc(vmm_alloc_pml4(), NULL); if (!mm) { kfree(t); return NULL; }` -- on task_mm_alloc OOM the PML4 frame from vmm_alloc_pml4() (its ONLY reference was the inline temporary) is LEAKED. task_create_user did `pml4 = vmm_alloc_pml4(); mm = mm_create(); tmm = task_mm_alloc(pml4, mm); if (!tmm) { kfree(t); return NULL; }` -- on task_mm_alloc OOM it leaks BOTH the PML4 frame AND the mm_t; AND because task_mm_alloc stores its args verbatim with no validation (process.c: kmalloc the wrapper, m->mm = mm, return), `mm_create()` returning NULL on OOM makes task_mm_alloc(pml4, NULL) SUCCEED, after which `mm_vma_add(mm, ...)` (a few lines down) NULL-DEREFS -> #PF crash. Neither create path checked vmm_alloc_pml4()==PMM_INVALID_ADDR either (an OOM there stores an INVALID pml4 that later faults loading CR3). The reference-correct sibling task_fork already unwinds fully (mm_destroy + vmm_free_user + pmm_buddy_free + kfree) and guards the PML4 OOM -- the two create paths had drifted from it.
  FOUND by the SCAN #15 error-path-leak sweep (the proc subagent flagged it as the "alloc A, alloc-B-fails, forgot-to-free-A" drift vs task_fork). VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): task_mm_alloc (process.c) stores pml4/mm as-is and frees neither on its own kmalloc failure (caller owns them); mm_create() returns NULL on OOM; vmm_alloc_pml4() returns PMM_INVALID_ADDR on OOM; task_fork's three pml4-level unwind sites (vmm_clone_user_ex fail, mm_clone fail, task_mm_alloc fail) are exactly `[mm_destroy] vmm_free_user + pmm_buddy_free + kfree`. Traced every exit of both create functions.
  FIX (do-it-right + safe-primitives -- extract the shared unwind, convert all sites, kill the drift): new `// PRIMITIVE task_create_unwind(t, pml4, mm)` = `if (mm) mm_destroy(mm); vmm_free_user(pml4); pmm_buddy_free(pml4, 0); kfree(t);` -- the single source of truth for the "PML4 (+ maybe mm) allocated, a later step failed" cleanup. Both create functions now (a) guard `pml4 == PMM_INVALID_ADDR` (bare kfree(t), no pml4 to free), (b) task_create_user guards `mm_create()==NULL` via task_create_unwind(t, pml4, NULL) BEFORE task_mm_alloc -- so mm_vma_add never sees NULL (NULL-deref killed) -- and (c) both release pml4 (+mm) via task_create_unwind on the task_mm_alloc-failure path (leak killed). task_fork's THREE hand-rolled unwind sites were converted to the same helper (byte-equivalent: it does mm_destroy-if-mm then vmm_free_user then pmm_buddy_free then kfree, matching task_fork's exact order including the populated-mm clone case where mm_destroy unrefs each VMA's shmem). task_mm_release (the refcount-0 free of a CONSTRUCTED task_mm_t, via vmm_free_user_ex) is a different contract and correctly left alone.
  VERIFICATION: no clean deterministic selftest fits an alloc/OOM unwind path (it frees real PML4/mm/task resources, not a pure computation) -- so code-proof (the unwind helper + the two new guards) + the no-regression boot. The SUCCESS paths of all three functions are heavily exercised at boot: task_create_kthread (kernel threads), task_create_user (sys_spawn of /bin/login, /bin/svcmgr, /bin/net), task_fork (every process fork) -- the boot showed those binaries demand-paged + running, DHCP 10.0.2.15, 84 selftests PASSED (fs_permop/nvme_lbads/hda_nodes/drm_cursor), 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD]. Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1). (Login render gated by the pre-existing flaky F55 net/userspace stall, orthogonal.) main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.
- 2026-06-27 - F141 FIXED (SCAN #15 error-path-resource-leak residual #3, the only REMOTELY-triggerable one: tcp.c established-child-PCB leak on a full accept backlog): in tcp_recv's TCP_SYN_RCVD case (kernel/net/tcp.c ~466), once a half-open child PCB receives the handshake-completing ACK it is promoted to TCP_ESTABLISHED under s_pcb_wlock, then pushed onto the listener's accept queue via accept_q_push(lst, pcb) under the listener lock. accept_q_push returns false when the queue is FULL (accept_count >= TCP_BACKLOG == 8) -- and the old code dropped the child on a fall-through (`if (queued) pcb_wake(lst);` with no else). That child is now ESTABLISHED, sock_file == NULL, and on NO accept queue, while the only reclaimer (the SYN-flood half-open reaper, tcp_timer_tick) matches ONLY state == TCP_SYN_RCVD && !sock_file -- so an ESTABLISHED unaccepted orphan is NEVER reclaimed and stays on s_pcb_head forever, leaking the PCB + its ~128 KiB tx/rx ring buffers. A remote peer completing MORE handshakes than TCP_BACKLOG faster than accept() drains leaks ~128 KiB per excess connection -> remote memory-exhaustion DoS (the one network-reachable SCAN #15 leak; the others were OOM/device/local). The SIBLING orphan case `establish && lst == NULL` (the listener was freed, NULLing child->listener) leaks identically.
  FOUND by the SCAN #15 error-path-leak sweep (the net subagent; flagged as the one genuine leak, a fall-through drop the comment even acknowledged as "the child is dropped, as before"). VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): accept_q_push (tcp.c:208) is a pure ring push that returns false when full; the reaper (tcp.c:652-666) matches SYN_RCVD-only; tcp_pcb_free (tcp.c:727) unlinks under s_pcb_wlock + RCU-defers the buffer/PCB free via call_rcu_expedited; tcp_recv processes the PCB INSIDE rcu_read_lock and after the switch does only rcu_read_unlock + skb_free (never re-derefs pcb); the establish transition is single-CPU under s_pcb_wlock (a 2nd CPU sees state != SYN_RCVD and does nothing); a retransmitted ACK after establish lands in the ESTABLISHED case (never re-establishes/frees).
  FIX (do-it-right): on the not-queued branch (accept backlog full OR listener gone), REFUSE the connection -- tcp_send_rst(child local->remote, seq=snd_nxt, ack=rcv_nxt) -- and free the child via tcp_pcb_free(pcb). Restructured to `if (establish) { queued = lst ? accept_q_push(...) : false; if (queued) pcb_wake(lst); else { RST; tcp_pcb_free(pcb); } }` so BOTH the backlog-full and listener-gone orphans are reclaimed (the old code only handled `establish && lst`, leaking the lst==NULL case too). verify-all-angles: the normal queued path is unchanged (pcb_wake outside the listener lock preserved); a refused connection RSTs + frees exactly once; safe under rcu_read_lock (free is RCU-deferred, pcb untouched after the break); no double-free (reaper is SYN_RCVD-only, the establish is single-CPU, a concurrent retransmit takes the ESTABLISHED path); the listener + other PCBs are untouched (tcp_pcb_free's orphan loop is a no-op when pcb is a child, not a listener).
  VERIFICATION: no new selftest -- the fix is the straight-line composition of two already-selftested behaviors (accept_q_push-returns-false-when-full is covered by tcp_accept_q_selftest's full-reject case; the tcp_pcb_free RCU-deferred teardown is covered by tcp_listener_orphan_selftest); end-to-end would need TCP segment injection the harness lacks -> code-proof + boot. Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1). Boot-verified (re-booted past the flaky F55 net stall to a DHCP boot): all 5 TCP self-tests PASSED ([tcp_ring]/[tcp_reserve]/[tcp_accept]/[tcp_orphan]/[tcp_synreap]), [fs_permop]/[drm_cursor] PASSED, 83 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], DHCP 10.0.2.15 (net stack healthy -- my change is only on the handshake-to-full-backlog path, never hit at boot). main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.

- 2026-06-27 - F143 FIXED (SCAN #15 error-path-resource-leak residual #5: vmm isr14 unchecked vmm_page_map leaf-frame leak + silent re-fault loop): isr14_page_fault's kernel-mode not-present demand-map (kernel/mm/vmm.c ~1229, the kheap-expansion path) did `frame = pmm_buddy_alloc(0); if (frame == PMM_INVALID_ADDR) goto kernel_panic; memset(frame); vmm_page_map(g_kernel_pml4, fault_addr & ~PAGE_MASK, frame, VMM_KDATA); return;` with the vmm_page_map RETURN UNCHECKED. vmm_page_map returns 0 (uint8_t) when vmm_pte_get cannot allocate an intermediate page-table page under memory pressure (vmm.c:244-255), so on that double-OOM the leaf `frame` is neither mapped nor freed -> leaked; WORSE, the handler then `return`s with the fault UNRESOLVED, so the faulting kernel access re-executes and re-faults, alloc'ing + leaking ANOTHER leaf frame on every pass until the buddy allocator is exhausted (a silent re-fault loop, not just a one-page leak).
  FOUND by the SCAN #15 error-path-leak sweep (the mm subagent). - 2026-06-27 - F147 FIXED (SCAN #16 ignored-error-return residual #2: ext2_rename ignored dir_remove_entry(src) + dir_set_dotdot -> fs corruption, the only race-reachable, on-disk-corruption SCAN #16 item): ext2_rename (kernel/fs/ext2.c) adds the dst dirent pointing at src_ino via dir_add_entry, then (~3249) called `dir_remove_entry(src_parent_ino, src_base)` and IGNORED its return. dir_remove_entry returns 0 on failure (inode_lock fail, read_block I/O error, kmalloc OOM for its 4 KiB block buffer, OR the name not found -- which a concurrent ext2_unlink(src) causes, since unlink takes the parent-inode lock NOT s_rename_lock and races this window). On failure src_ino keeps BOTH the new dst name and the old src name at i_links_count==1 (rename is a MOVE, the count was never bumped); a later unlink of either name then drops the count to 0 and frees the inode + data blocks while the OTHER name still references it -> dangling dirent / inode-number reuse / cross-link / data corruption. The dst-removal 14 lines earlier (~3235) is EXPLICITLY gated on its dir_remove_entry return (with a double-free comment) -- the src-removal being ungated was an asymmetry, not a considered best-effort. SECOND site (~3261): a cross-parent directory move ignored `dir_set_dotdot(src_ino, dst_parent_ino)` then UNCONDITIONALLY swapped both parents' i_links_count -- if ".." was not repointed (I/O error / OOM / ".." not found), ".." still backlinks the OLD parent but src_parent's count was decremented anyway, making it too low so an over-decrement elsewhere could free it while this dir's ".." still references it (the exact cross-link the swap exists to prevent).
  FOUND by the SCAN #16 ignored-error-return sweep (the fs subagent flagged the asymmetry vs the gated dst-removal). VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions, whole ext2_rename traced under s_rename_lock + per-inode locks): dir_remove_entry returns 1 iff it cleared a matching entry (ext2.c:2178-2228); dir_set_dotdot returns 1 iff ".." was found+repointed+written (ext2.c:2279); the order is dir_add_entry(dst) -> dir_remove_entry(src) -> [cross-parent] dir_set_dotdot + link-count swap; the dst-removal gating at 3235 is the model.
  FIX (do-it-right -- make the rename ATOMIC, mirror the dst gating): (1) on dir_remove_entry(src) FAILURE, ROLL BACK -- remove the dst dirent dir_add_entry just added (dir_remove_entry(dst_parent_ino, dst_base)), spin_unlock(&s_rename_lock), return 0 -- so the move is all-or-nothing and src_ino is never left with two names. (2) gate the parent link-count swap on dir_set_dotdot SUCCESS via `&& dir_set_dotdot(...)` (short-circuit): if ".." was not repointed the counts are NOT moved, so they stay consistent with the (un-repointed) ".." and src_parent's count can't go too low. verify-all-angles: the success path (both ops succeed) is UNCHANGED; on src-removal failure the dst is removed + failure returned (no two-name inode, no later double-free -- handles both the I/O-error case and the concurrent-unlink race, where the rollback leaves the file cleanly unlinked); on dir_set_dotdot failure the link counts are not desynced; same-parent rename + non-dir rename skip the dotdot block via the `!=` short-circuit (unchanged); s_rename_lock is released on the new failure exit; the rollback's own dir_remove_entry is a best-effort cleanup (a double-fault is the only un-rolled-back case, no worse than before). Residual (separate, lock-ordering not ignored-return): unlink-vs-rename do not mutually exclude (unlink uses the parent-inode lock, rename uses s_rename_lock) -- the rollback makes rename atomic w.r.t. its own ops but the deeper race is a future lock-scan item.
  VERIFICATION: forcing dir_remove_entry to fail needs I/O/OOM injection that the ext2 self-test harness lacks -> code-proof + boot. - 2026-06-27 - F149 FIXED (SCAN #17 memory-safety OOB lead: tcp tx-ring 64 KiB-wrap heap-OVER-READ -> remote kernel-heap info-leak): the per-PCB transmit ring txbuf is exactly TCP_TXBUF_SIZE (65536) bytes (kmalloc'd, power-of-two), and the WRITE path masks every byte index (tcp.c ~867 `pcb->txbuf[(tail0+i) & TCP_TXBUF_MASK]`), but the two READ paths passed a flat (pointer, length) into tcp_send_segment, which does `memcpy(p, data, dlen)` (tcp.c:268) of dlen contiguous bytes: tcp_send (~877) sent `pcb->txbuf + send_off` for `sendable` bytes, and tcp_timer_tick's retransmit (~671) sent `pcb->txbuf + (txbuf_head & TCP_TXBUF_MASK)` for `rlen` bytes. send_off / (txbuf_head & mask) are masked into [0, 65536) and sendable/rlen are clamped to TCP_MSS (1460), so whenever the unacked/to-send span STRADDLES the ring wrap (off + len > 65536) the memcpy OVER-READ up to ~1459 bytes PAST the 64 KiB txbuf -- adjacent kernel heap was copied into the TCP segment and TRANSMITTED ON THE WIRE (a remote heap info-disclosure: an attacker who keeps a connection's send window crossing the wrap point harvests kernel heap bytes) AND the wrapped tail bytes were never sent (silent stream corruption). Reachable on any TCP connection that sends > ~64 KiB total (so txbuf_head wraps) with an in-flight/to-send span landing across the boundary.
  FOUND by SCAN #16's net sweep as an out-of-class note (a heap-OOB-read, not an ignored return); promoted to lead the SCAN #17 OOB/over-read type. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): tcp_send_segment flat-memcpies dlen from the passed pointer (266-268) and advances snd_nxt += dlen (285) so two consecutive segments carry contiguous seq numbers; both send sites pass txbuf + masked_offset + a TCP_MSS-clamped length with NO wrap handling; the RX producer path already uses masked per-byte indexing (correct) -- only the two TX reads linearized; send_off up to 65535 + sendable up to 1460 = up to 66995 > 65536, so the over-read is up to 1459 bytes.
  FIX (do-it-right, safe-primitives -- a tested no-wrap-chunk bound + a wrap-aware send): new `// PRIMITIVE tcp_tx_first_chunk(off, len)` returns min(len, TCP_TXBUF_SIZE - off) -- the largest prefix that stays before the ring wrap (off + return <= TCP_TXBUF_SIZE always) -- and `tcp_send_ring(pcb, flags, off, len)` sends one segment (no wrap) or TWO consecutive segments (head [off, end), tail [0, len-first)) so tcp_send_segment's memcpy never reads past txbuf; snd_nxt advances per segment so the seqs are contiguous and the full data is sent. Both send sites (tcp_send and the retransmit) now route their buffered data through tcp_send_ring; the retransmit's SYN/SYN-ACK/FIN-only (rlen==0) cases still go through tcp_send_segment directly. verify-all-angles: a non-wrapping span is UNCHANGED (single segment, identical bytes); a wrapping span reads only within [0, TCP_TXBUF_SIZE) and is transmitted in full across two segments with correct seqs (no OOB read, no kernel-heap leak, no dropped tail); each split segment is < the original (< TCP_MSS), so skb sizing + the MSS/window clamps still hold; on a mid-split skb-OOM the first segment's snd_nxt advance leaves the tail for the retransmit (best-effort, matches existing send semantics); callers pass pure-data flags (no SYN/FIN) for wrapping spans so duplicated flags on a 2-way split are correct.
  VERIFICATION: added `tcp_tx_first_chunk_selftest` (registered in main.c after tcp_ring_reserve_selftest) driving the bound at the wrap boundaries -- 65000+1460 -> 536, 65535+1460 -> 1, 1+65536 -> 65535, full-ring, zero-length -- asserting off+chunk <= TCP_TXBUF_SIZE for every case (the over-read inputs). Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1). - 2026-06-27 - F150 FIXED (SCAN #17 OOB-class residual: ext2_vfs_pread missing-EOF-clamp -> phantom past-i_size bytes, info-EXPOSURE, MED): ext2_vfs_read and ext2_vfs_pread both have an aligned fast path that DMAs whole consecutive blocks in one run -- `inode_build_run` returns `run` blocks and the byte count is `bytes = run * s_block_size`. The per-iteration `file_blks_left = (file_size - cur_pos + s_block_size - 1) / s_block_size` rounds UP, so a run is allowed to cover the file's FINAL partial block, making `bytes` overshoot i_size by up to `s_block_size - 1` (the on-disk slack between EOF and the block boundary). ext2_vfs_read clamps this at ext2.c:1327 with `if (bytes > remain_file) bytes = remain_file;` (the comment there notes a real 7447-byte file returning 8192 phantom bytes that tripped sway's "config file changed" guard); ext2_vfs_pread's fast path (ext2.c ~1390-1418) did `total += bytes; cur_pos += bytes;` with NO such clamp -- so a pread whose final block is partial returned the block's tail slack PAST end-of-file. Those phantom bytes are stale on-disk content of the final block (whatever the filesystem left there), copied into the caller's buffer and counted in the return value = an information-exposure (a reader gets bytes it should never see; the mmap/demand-paging path preads every binary's final, partial page). A bounded over-return (<= s_block_size-1), never an OOB write, and the slow partial-block path was already correct (it copies the already-clamped `to_copy`), so only the pread fast path was affected.
  FOUND by SCAN #16's fs sweep as an out-of-class note (a missing-clamp, not an ignored return), promoted into the SCAN #17 OOB/over-read continuation. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): the read/pread asymmetry was exact -- ext2_vfs_read:1327 has the clamp, ext2_vfs_pread's identical fast path did not; `remain_file = fd->file_size - cur_pos` is recomputed each iteration (current at the clamp point); the slow path's `cur_pos += to_copy` uses the min(remain_blk, remain_file)-clamped count so it never overshoots. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, mirror the existing tested clamp -- 2 paths, not 3+, so no new helper per safe-primitives): inserted the SAME one line `if (bytes > remain_file) bytes = remain_file;` into ext2_vfs_pread's fast path immediately before `total += bytes; cur_pos += bytes;`, so pread can never return or advance past i_size -- identical semantics to ext2_vfs_read. verify-all-angles: a fully-aligned file (i_size a block multiple) is UNCHANGED (bytes == remain_file at EOF, clamp is a no-op); a sub-block file never enters the fast path (to_copy != s_block_size -> slow path, already clamped); a multi-block file with a partial final block now returns exactly i_size-offset; cur_pos advance is clamped too so the next iteration's EOF break is correct; no other read path touched.
  VERIFICATION: added `ext2_pread_eof_selftest` (registered in main.c after ext2_perm_op_selftest) -- it writes a MULTI-block file with a partial final block (`s_block_size + 100` bytes) via the real ext2_write_file path, ext2_open's it, preads MORE than the file (`fsize + s_block_size`) from offset 0 across the partial final block, and asserts the returned count is EXACTLY fsize (with the bug the aligned run would return the full final block) AND the returned bytes match what was written (no slack corruption), then unlinks. Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1). Boot-verified: [ext2_pread_eof] SELF-TEST PASSED (pread clamps to i_size, no phantom tail past EOF) alongside [ext2_link_drop]/[fs_permop]/[ext2_dotdot] PASSED (no fs regression), 87 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD]. main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.
- 2026-06-27 - F151 FIXED (SCAN #16/#17 ignored-error-return MED residual: sys_readlink + sys_times reported SUCCESS on a faulted copy_to_user -> false-success on a bad user buffer, 2 sites in kernel/syscall/syscall.c): both syscalls write their result into the user destination via copy_to_user but DROPPED its return and reported success regardless. (1) sys_readlink (syscall.c:5517) did `copy_to_user((void*)buf_ptr, target, tlen); return tlen;` -- a caller passing an unmapped/kernel-range buf got back tlen (a positive byte count) as if the link path had been written, when copy_to_user had already rejected the pointer and copied nothing. (2) sys_times (syscall.c:5663) did `copy_to_user((void*)buf_ptr, &tms, sizeof(tms));` inside `if (buf_ptr)` then `return ticks;` -- a faulted tms* still returned a valid-looking tick count. copy_to_user returns -EFAULT (it _access_ok-range-checks then VMA-prefaults the dest, the arbitrary-kernel-write LPE guard) on exactly those bad pointers, so the ignored non-zero return is a dropped error: the POSIX contract (readlink/times must fail with EFAULT when the buffer is outside the accessible address space) was violated -- a correctness/contract bug, unprivileged-reachable, though not a kernel leak/crash (copy_to_user already prevented the bad write; only the return code lied).
  FOUND by SCAN #16's ignored-error-return sweep as MED residuals, carried into SCAN #17's STILL-OPEN list. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): read both bodies -- each truly discards copy_to_user's int return and returns the success value; confirmed the file's canonical idiom is `copy_to_user(...) != 0 -> return (uint64_t)-EFAULT` (sys_getrusage, sys_gettimeofday:2980, sys_uname:4120, sys_stat:1917 all do exactly this) so the fix mirrors existing code (DRY, no new helper -- copy_to_user is the primitive). FIX (do-it-right, ROOT): sys_readlink now `if (copy_to_user(buf_ptr, target, tlen) != 0) return -EFAULT;` before returning tlen; sys_times now `if (copy_to_user(buf_ptr, &tms, sizeof(tms)) != 0) return -EFAULT;` inside the `if (buf_ptr)`. verify-all-angles: the happy path (valid buffer) is UNCHANGED (copy returns 0 -> the original byte-count/tick return); a faulted buffer now returns -EFAULT; the readlink bufsz==0 edge is PRESERVED (tlen clamps to 0, and copy_to_user(valid_ptr, src, 0) returns 0 because _access_ok skips its range math for len==0 and a zero-page prefault is a no-op, so a 0-size readlink still returns 0, not -EFAULT); times(NULL) is still valid (the copy is inside `if (buf_ptr)`, so a NULL tms* skips it and returns ticks); no other caller/contract touched (both are leaf handlers reached only through their jump-table wrappers).
  VERIFICATION: no deterministic selftest fits a copy_to_user -EFAULT path (the boot harness has no faulting-user-buffer fixture -- it would need a user mm with a deliberately-unmapped page, which the in-kernel init_kthread selftests do not set up), so code-proof (the fix is the file's own canonical EFAULT idiom, applied identically) + clean boot. Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1; only pre-existing unused-label/format warnings, none at 5517/5663). Boot-verified: userspace (bash et al.) exercises readlink/times on VALID buffers and the boot reaches the full selftest battery with 87 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD] (the happy path unbroken; the -EFAULT path is the only new behavior and is code-proven). main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.
- 2026-06-27 - F152 FIXED (SCAN #16/#17 ignored-error-return MED residual: hda verb_send returned STALE RIRB data on a poll timeout -> phantom codec topology, kernel/drivers/audio/hda.c): verb_send (hda.c:195) wrote a codec verb to the CORB then polled the RIRB write pointer for the reply in a bounded loop (`for i in 0..500000: if r16(HDA_RIRBWP) == exp break;`), but FELL THROUGH unconditionally after the loop to `uint64_t resp = s_rirb[exp]; s_rirb_rp = exp; return resp;` -- so on a TIMEOUT (the codec never advanced RIRBWP to exp) it read the RIRB slot s_rirb[exp] that was NEVER written for this verb (s_rirb is __builtin_memset to 0 at init, so the slot is zero before the first response and a PREVIOUS response's leftover after) and returned it AS IF it were a valid codec response. get_param (hda.c:212) wraps verb_send and feeds codec_configure's enumeration: NODE_COUNT (root + per function group), FUNC_TYPE, WIDGET_CAP, PIN_CAP. SECOND defect in the same fall-through: `s_rirb_rp = exp` advanced the RIRB read pointer on EVERY timeout even though the codec wrote nothing, desyncing the ring by one slot so every subsequent verb's `exp` is off by one. Class, 2 call-site groups (task_fork's 3 unwind paths + sys_thread's 2).
  FOUND by the SCAN #19 mm/pmm refcount sweep (one of three parallel agents). VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): confirmed vmm_clone_user_ex incs only shmem not MMIO (vmm.c:640) yet sets the child MMIO PTE present (641); confirmed vmm_free_user(pml4)=vmm_free_user_ex(pml4,NULL) (vmm.c:534) and the skip_free guard needs mm!=NULL (vmm.c:512); confirmed the SMOKING-GUN internal inconsistency -- the OTHER fork teardown paths (process.c task_mm_release -> vmm_free_user_ex(pml4, m->mm), mm-aware, skip MMIO) and the normal child exit are correct, only task_create_unwind + sys_thread dropped mm-awareness; confirmed mm_destroy (mm.c:261-272) frees ONLY the VMA structs not the leaf frames (so the mm-aware free is the same single frame-free, no double-free); confirmed sys_exec (syscall.c:1051/1107) and elf.c build a FRESH ELF image (elf_load_into, no inherited MMIO) so their vmm_free_user(NULL) is SAFE -- only the two vmm_clone_user_ex callers were buggy. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT -- fix the fragile design, a bugfix-as-refactor): task_create_unwind now takes a layout_mm (separate from the destroy_mm) and frees via vmm_free_user_ex(pml4, layout_mm) BEFORE mm_destroy (which frees the VMAs it consults); the 3 task_fork unwind sites pass parent->mm_shared->mm (the fork's identical VMA layout) so MMIO PTEs are skipped, the empty/kernel-pml4 sites (kthread/fresh-user) pass NULL (no MMIO present); sys_thread's two error paths now call vmm_free_user_ex(new_pml4, g_current->mm_shared->mm). The MMIO frame is no longer dec'd on these error paths -> the parent's device frame keeps its refcount. verify-all-angles: the happy path is UNCHANGED (these run only on a fork/spawn OOM); non-MMIO frames (anon/CoW/shmem PTEs) are still dec'd exactly once (skip_free=0 for them); a partial clone (clone failed midway) is handled -- the child's present PTEs are a subset of the parent's VMAs so every present PTE resolves in parent->mm; no double-free (mm_destroy never freed frames); the empty-pml4 task_create_user/kthread paths are unaffected (layout NULL, no PTEs). 6 process.c call sites updated to the 4-arg form (verified by grep, no stale 3-arg), vmm_free_user_ex declared in vmm.h and visible in both files.
  VERIFICATION: no deterministic selftest fits -- driving it needs a userspace fork/spawn with a VMA_MMIO buddy-RAM region mapped AND a forced PMM OOM at the exact clone/mm_clone/task_mm_alloc step, which the in-kernel init_kthread harness cannot orchestrate (no user process + no fault injection at a chosen alloc). So code-proof (the fix mirrors the already-correct mm-aware teardown that the normal-exit and task_mm_release paths use) + clean boot. Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1; only pre-existing unused-label/format/unused-variable warnings, none on the changed lines). Boot-verified: the fork/spawn HAPPY path is exercised throughout boot (every process spawn: svcmgr/net/login demand-paged, userspace runs), DHCP 10.0.2.15, 87 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD] -- so the clone + (successful) teardown changes did not regress process creation; the error-path MMIO fix is code-proven. main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII. NOTE: SCAN #19 also surfaced two more findings recorded in AUDIT_FINDINGS for follow-up -- sys_openpty force-closes installed fds via ->close() instead of vfs_close/sys_close (refcount-bypass UAF/double-free under a shared-fd-table sibling race, MED) and listener-close leaks queued-but-unaccepted ESTABLISHED child PCBs (~128 KiB each, unbounded DoS, the residual F141 did not cover, MED).
- 2026-06-27 - F157 FIXED (SCAN #19 follow-up #1: sys_openpty force-closed installed fds via ->close() -> refcount-bypass UAF/double-free, kernel/syscall/syscall.c): sys_openpty installs the master+slave fds via fd_install (which TRANSFERS the single refcount==1 ref into the SHARED fd table), then on its three error paths NULLed the fd_table slot manually and called `master->close(master)` / `slave->close(slave)` DIRECTLY. ->close() is the pty DRIVER teardown (frees the pty_t, decrements master_open/slave_open_count) and is non-idempotent; it bypasses the atomic vfs refcount AND does not free the vfs_file_t. So (a) on the slave-install-fail and copy_to_user-fail paths, where master (and slave) are already INSTALLED in the shared table, a CLONE_FILES sibling thread that fdget/dup's the just-installed mfd in the window after fd_install publishes the slot but before the error path runs bumps refcount 1->2; the manual-NULL + ->close() then frees the pty_t while the sibling still holds a ref -> use-after-free, and the sibling's later fdput/close is a double-free of the pty_t (single-threaded is harmless: refcount==1, one clean teardown); and (b) even the mfd<0 branch (neither end installed) leaked the vfs_file_t, since ->close() runs only the driver teardown and never frees the vfs_file_t struct. sys_openpty was the LONE hand-rolled ->close() in the file -- every sibling (sys_pipe copyout/fail, socketpair, sys_accept, sys_recvfd) already uses the safe primitive.
  FOUND by the SCAN #19 fs/vfs/fd refcount sweep. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): read sys_openpty whole + the three error branches and classified each fd's installed state (mfd<0: neither installed; sfd<0: master installed, slave not; copy_to_user-fail: both installed); confirmed fd_install transfers the ref on success and LEAVES it to the caller on failure (socketpair syscall.c:6649 `if (fd1<0){ sys_close(fd0); vfs_close(pair[1]); }` is the exact canonical pattern); confirmed sys_close (syscall.c:558) clears the slot under tf->lock then vfs_close's outside the lock (atomic dec, driver teardown + vfs_file_t free only at rc->0); confirmed sys_pipe's comment (syscall.c:2252-2259) spells out the same INSTALLED->sys_close / un-installed->vfs_close rule and that a bare vfs_close on an installed end double-frees. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, mirror the established safe idiom -- DRY, never ->close() outside single-owner selftests): mfd<0 -> vfs_close(master)+vfs_close(slave) (neither installed; vfs_close frees pty_t via ->close at rc->0 AND the vfs_file_t); sfd<0 -> sys_close(mfd)+vfs_close(slave) (master installed, slave not); copy_to_user-fail -> sys_close(mfd)+sys_close(sfd) (both installed); the manual fd_table-NULL + spin_lock dance is removed (sys_close does the slot-clear atomically). verify-all-angles: the SUCCESS path is unchanged (returns the two fds); a single-threaded error path still tears down exactly once (rc 1->0); a shared-fd-table sibling's extra ref now KEEPS the pty alive until it drops its ref (no UAF, no double-free); the never-installed ends are freed exactly once with no vfs_file_t leak; no other caller/contract touched (leaf syscall).
  VERIFICATION: no deterministic selftest fits -- driving the UAF needs TWO threads sharing an fd table, one racing a deliberately-failed openpty (bad user_fds pointer) while the other dup/fdget's the in-flight master fd, which the in-kernel init_kthread harness cannot set up. So code-proof (the fix is the file's own sys_close/vfs_close idiom, identical to socketpair/sys_pipe) + clean boot. Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1; only pre-existing unused-function/label/format warnings, none at sys_openpty; the removed tf0 locals produced no unused-variable warning). Boot-verified: the pty close paths are exercised by [pty_life]/[pty_reopen]/[pty_mring] -- all PASS -- alongside 87 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD], DHCP 10.0.2.15. (One boot of the SAME image showed 86 vs 87 with DHCP up but no userspace login; a re-boot of the identical binary gave 87 -- same binary, two counts, so the dip is a flaky pre-login race, not this change; all 77 in-kernel selftest tags incl. the pty tests were present and PASSED in BOTH boots.) main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII.
- 2026-06-27 - F158 FIXED (SCAN #19 follow-up #2, the LAST: TCP listener-close leaked queued-but-unaccepted ESTABLISHED child PCBs -> unbounded memory-exhaustion DoS, kernel/net/tcp.c): a LISTEN pcb holds a TCP_BACKLOG(8)-entry accept_queue ring of children that completed their handshake (SYN_RCVD -> ESTABLISHED) but have not been accept()ed yet (sock_file==NULL). The ONLY consumer of the ring is accept_q_pop, called only from tcp_accept. tcp_pcb_free(listener) (tcp.c:780) walked s_pcb_head and NULLed each child's ->listener backpointer (the F141 late-ACK-UAF guard) but NEVER freed the children or drained the accept_queue, and sock_close's SOCK_STREAM branch (socket.c:237) freed only the listener's own pcb. So closing a listener with a filled backlog before accept()ing left each queued child ESTABLISHED, sock_file==NULL, ->listener==NULL, still on s_pcb_head, referenced by NOTHING that will ever free it: tcp_accept is unreachable (listener gone) and the half-open reaper (tcp_timer_tick, SYN_RCVD-only) never matches an ESTABLISHED child -> each leaks ~128 KiB (its 64 KiB txbuf + 64 KiB rxbuf) + the pcb, bounded to 8 per close but UNBOUNDED across repeated listen/fill-backlog/close cycles = a local memory-exhaustion DoS, remotely amplifiable (a peer completing handshakes faster than the app accept()s, then the app closing the listener). This is exactly the residual F141 did NOT cover: F141 RST+frees a child that establishes AFTER its listener is already gone (the orphan path, tcp.c:503-520); F158 covers the children queued BEFORE the listener closed.
  FOUND by the SCAN #19 net/socket/pcb refcount sweep. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): confirmed accept_queue is a ring in the listener (accept_queue[TCP_BACKLOG]/head/tail/count, tcp.c:82-85) whose only mutators are accept_q_push/pop under the LISTENER's pcb->lock (tcp.c:200-221); confirmed tcp_pcb_free NULLs ->listener but does not free children; confirmed the reaper is SYN_RCVD-only and tcp_recv never frees an ESTABLISHED child (tcp_pcb_free is called only from the orphan path + sock_close + selftests), so the queued children have NO other freer -> a true leak, and the drain has no double-free partner; confirmed tcp_close sets a closing LISTEN pcb to TCP_CLOSED BEFORE tcp_pcb_free (socket.c:241-242), so the drain must key on accept_count (not state==TCP_LISTEN); confirmed the F141 orphan dispose is tcp_send_rst(local,remote,snd_nxt,rcv_nxt)+tcp_pcb_free; confirmed the establish path releases s_pcb_wlock BEFORE taking the listener pcb->lock (tcp.c:489-496), so the drain must not hold the listener lock across tcp_pcb_free (which takes s_pcb_wlock). FIX (do-it-right, ROOT, single-source-of-truth + DRY): tcp_pcb_free now drains the accept backlog after its s_pcb_wlock section and before the RCU defer -- `while (pcb->accept_count > 0) { lock; child=accept_q_pop(pcb); unlock; if(!child) break; tcp_send_rst(child...); tcp_pcb_free(child); }`. Keyed on accept_count so connected-socket frees pay nothing; pops under the listener lock (accept_q's required lock) then RST+frees OUTSIDE it so the child's tcp_pcb_free never nests under the listener lock (matching the establish path's lock order); it is the single chokepoint so EVERY listener free (sock_close, the socket_open-failure path socket.c:293, future paths) drains. verify-all-angles: a listener with 0 queued children is unchanged (accept_count==0 -> loop body never runs); N queued children are each RST'd + freed exactly once; disjoint from a concurrent accept() (each child popped once under the lock) and from the reaper (SYN_RCVD only) -> no double-free; an ALREADY-ACCEPTED child (popped, sock_file!=NULL, owned by its own socket) is never in the queue so untouched; the recursive tcp_pcb_free(child) does not re-drain (child accept_count==0) -> bounded depth 1; tcp_accept, the F141 orphan path, and tcp_close are all unchanged.
  VERIFICATION: added tcp_listener_drain_selftest (registered in main.c after tcp_synreap_selftest) -- builds a listener, fills its backlog with TCP_BACKLOG ESTABLISHED children (sock_file==NULL), frees the listener WITHOUT accepting, and asserts the queue drained (accept_count==0) AND none of the children remain on s_pcb_head (tcp_pcb_on_list pointer-compare, RCU-safe); with the OLD code the children stay on s_pcb_head -> the test FAILS, with the fix they are drained+freed -> PASS. Built clean (NO_QEMU=1 SELFTESTS=1 and shipping NO_QEMU=1; no tcp.c/main.c warnings). Boot-verified: [tcp_lstdrain] SELF-TEST PASSED (listener close drains + frees queued ESTABLISHED children) alongside [tcp_accept]/[tcp_orphan]/[tcp_synreap]/[tcp_txwrap]/[tcp_ring]/[tcp_reserve] PASSED (no TCP/accept/listener/reaper regression), 88 selftests PASSED (the new test is the +1 over the 87 baseline), 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP/[WD]. (DHCP did not reach this boot -- the known flaky F55 pre-login net stall -- but the fix is in the TCP listener-teardown path, which the deterministic [tcp_lstdrain] selftest + all tcp_* selftests exercise and prove directly, far more rigorously than a DHCP/UDP check.) main untouched; commit on bughunt as mstampfli, plain ASCII. With F158 the SCAN #19 follow-up backlog is EMPTY; SCAN #19 yielded F156(HIGH UAF)/F157(MED UAF)/F158(MED DoS).
- 2026-07-01 - F159 FIXED (concurrency: the recorded "T4" tcp_timer_tick two-thread data race): tcp_timer_tick mutates pcb->snd_nxt/snd_una-relative rewind, ->rexmit, ->rto_deadline and ->state under rcu_read_lock but NO pcb->lock, and its own code asserts the single-writer invariant ("only the timer thread writes rexmit -> no lock needed", tcp.c:659). That invariant was broken: net_rx_thread ALSO called tcp_timer_tick every ~10 RX wakeups (net.c) on top of the dedicated net_tcp_timer_thread's ~200 ms tick, so two threads could concurrently rewind snd_nxt to snd_una and resend, double-increment rexmit, or tear rto_deadline -> corrupt retransmit accounting (duplicate/garbled segments, an off-by-N reaper cap). ROOT fix (restore the assumed single writer, cheapest + no lock-order risk): the net_rx_thread call was pure redundancy -- the dedicated net_tcp_timer_thread already fires the timer independently of RX traffic (the reason it was added) -- so drop it (and the now-unused tick counter). tcp_timer_tick now has exactly one caller in steady state, matching the lockless-writer invariant; no new lock, no lock-order change. verify-all-angles: retransmits/TIME_WAIT-expiry/SYN_RCVD-reap still run (dedicated 200 ms thread); DHCP + [tcp_synreap]/[tcp_lstdrain]/all tcp_* selftests still PASS, 88/0 faults. Code-proof + clean boot (a lockless double-tick race is not deterministically reproducible in the harness). Terse by request (bug/token).
- 2026-07-01 - F160 FIXED (PHASE 5 concrete-security scan: fd-rights capability confinement was ~80% UNENFORCED -> restrict_fd/sendfd downgrades were silent no-ops): the rights model (kernel/security/rights.h) stamps every open fd with a RIGHT_* mask and documents "the kernel checks the relevant bit(s) before executing any fd operation", but only RIGHT_READ/RIGHT_WRITE were actually checked (read/write/mmap-read). RIGHT_SEEK, RIGHT_IOCTL, RIGHT_MMAP_R/W/X were defined + settable via restrict_fd (AND-downgrade) / sendfd, yet never enforced -- so a process handed a read-only-confined fd could still lseek it, ioctl it (device/tty control), and mmap it, INCLUDING mmap(PROT_EXEC) to execute code from a fd it may only read (a W^X / exec-confinement bypass). ROOT fix (enforce the model's stated contract at each op chokepoint, mirroring the existing RIGHT_READ pattern `f->rights != 0 && !rights_check(...) -> -EACCES`): sys_ioctl gates RIGHT_IOCTL, sys_lseek gates RIGHT_SEEK, sys_mmap's file-backed path gates RIGHT_MMAP_R/W/X per the requested PROT bits. Regression-safe by construction: normal opens carry the full mask (rights_from_oflags sets IOCTL/SEEK/MMAP_* per access mode) and device/pipe/tty/proc fds use rights==0 (exempt), so only an explicitly-downgraded fd is denied. sendfd already enforced RIGHT_SEND_FD + new_rights subset. Left unenforced (LOW, noted): RIGHT_POLL (poll readiness is not a confidentiality/integrity boundary) and RIGHT_EXEC (execve is path/unveil-gated here, not fd-based). Verification: no in-kernel selftest fits (rights are syscall-boundary, need a user process); code-proof + clean boot -- 88 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15, no spurious EACCES (kernel/boot fd ops run on rights==0 or full-mask fds). Built clean. Terse per efficiency mandate.
- 2026-07-01 - F161 FIXED (PHASE 5 concrete-security: sys_kill had NO cross-uid authorization -> any process could signal any task = unprivileged DoS/LPE): sys_kill (kernel/syscall/syscall.c) looked up the target by pid/pgrp and called signal_send_pid/signal_send_pgrp/kill_bcast with ZERO cred check, so an unprivileged process could SIGKILL init/svcmgr or another user's tasks (and kill(-1) broadcast to all). The send helpers are shared with kernel-internal signals (SIGCHLD to parent, tty Ctrl-C/WINCH job control, exit_group) which must stay unchecked, so the fix gates only the USER kill() boundary: new signal_may(sender,target) (POSIX -- permitted iff sender root, self, or sender ruid/euid == target ruid/suid) + signal_send_pid_user (returns -EPERM/-ESRCH) + signal_send_pgrp_user (per-member checked) + a signal_may check in kill_bcast_cb; sys_kill's four cases (pid>0 / pid==0 / pid<-1 / pid==-1) now route through them. Regression-safe: boot/init run as root (euid 0 -> allowed), and internal signal paths (SIGCHLD/tty/WINCH/exit_group) still use the unchecked helpers. Selftest signal_perm_selftest added (registered in main.c) -- root-any/self/same-uid ALLOW, cross-uid + non-root->root DENY. Verified: [signal_perm] SELF-TEST PASSED, 89 selftests PASSED (was 88 + the new one), 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15. Built clean. Terse per efficiency mandate.
- 2026-07-01 - F162 FIXED (PHASE 5 concrete-security, sibling of F161: sys_setpgid moved a FOREIGN process's group with no ownership check): sys_setpgid (kernel/syscall/syscall.c) looked up ANY task by pid and set t->pgid, guarded ONLY against a session leader -- so a process could relocate another process's process group (job-control tampering / confused-deputy: hijack a victim into an attacker-controlled pgrp, then signal it via kill(-pgid)). POSIX allows setpgid only on self or a child, within the caller's session. Root fix: reject if `t != g_current && t->ppid != g_current->pid` (-EPERM, not self/child) or `t->sid != g_current->sid` (-EPERM, cross-session), before the existing session-leader guard. Regression-safe: shell job control (setpgid on self / own children, same session) still passes; the check is ownership-based, not uid-based, so boot/root are unaffected. Verified: 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15, no setpgid EPERM in the boot. Built clean. Code-proof + boot (needs task ppid/sid relationships, no clean pure-helper unit test). Note: the other target-PID syscalls (setpriority/sched_setaffinity/prlimit/wait4) are ABSENT in this kernel, so the target-PID authz surface is now closed (kill=F161, setpgid=F162). Terse per efficiency mandate.
- 2026-07-01 - F163 FIXED (PHASE 5 concrete-security info-disclosure/capability-theft: /proc/<pid> exposed ANY task's data with no owner check): kernel/fs/proc.c resolved /proc/<pid>/{fd/<n>,status,cmdline,maps} via sched_find_pid(pid) then dup'd/emitted the target task's data with ZERO caller-ownership gate. The severe vector is /proc/<pid>/fd/<n>, which returns a vfs_tryget DUP of the target's fd n -- cross-uid CAPABILITY THEFT: an unprivileged process opens /proc/<root-daemon-or-other-user-pid>/fd/<n> and gets a working handle to a file it could never open itself (read its contents, and per the fd's rights even write) -- plus status/cmdline/maps leak layout/args of foreign processes. ROOT fix: gate all three /proc resolvers (open, readdir, getattr) on signal_may(g_current, t) -- the same POSIX predicate F161 added (root, self, or same ruid/euid==target ruid/suid); a foreign task is treated as not-found (hidden, avoids leaking pid existence to other uids). Regression-safe: a process reading its OWN /proc passes (self), root reads any (euid 0), and the boot runs as root; the check is ownership-based. Verified: 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15 (self/root /proc access unbroken). Built clean. Code-proof + boot (cross-uid /proc read needs a user process; no clean in-kernel selftest). Terse per efficiency mandate.
- 2026-07-01 - F164 FIXED (PHASE 5 concrete-security resource-DoS: no per-process fd cap -> unbounded fd/object exhaustion): fd_table_grow (kernel/proc/process.c) doubled the fd table (new_cap = old_cap*2) with NO upper bound, so an unprivileged process could open()/dup()/socket() until kmalloc failed -- each fd holds a kernel object (a socket = a ~128 KiB tcp pcb) and the doubling array itself grows unbounded, exhausting shared kernel heap and degrading every process (no RLIMIT_NOFILE existed). ROOT fix: cap the table at FD_MAX=4096 (`if (new_cap > FD_MAX) return 0;`), which reuses fd_install's existing grow-failure path (-EMFILE/-ENFILE), so a process is bounded to 4096 fds. Regression-safe: 4096 dwarfs any legit use (boot/shell/graphical session use tens-to-hundreds of fds); no grow refusal at boot. Verified: 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15. Built clean. RECORDED (next, higher severity): FORK-BOMB -- no per-uid/global nproc cap; pids are globally bounded (PID_MAX=65535) but a single unprivileged process can fork until it exhausts the 65535 pid space + ~650 MiB of task_t+8KiB-kstacks, wedging everyone. task_fork bypasses task_init_common (sets flags=0 directly), so the fix needs a live-user-task counter (inc at fork/spawn/thread success, dec at task_destroy) + a root-exempt cap -- a dedicated turn. Terse per efficiency mandate.
- 2026-07-01 - F165 FIXED (PHASE 5 concrete-security resource-DoS, the recorded fork-bomb: no per-uid/global nproc cap -> a non-root process could fork() until it exhausted the 65535 pid space + ~650 MiB of task_t+8KiB-kstacks and wedged everyone). ROOT fix (RLIMIT_NPROC via a global live-task count + a non-root cap, root exempt): s_live_task_count is inc'd in pid_alloc (at the bit-commit) and dec'd in pid_free (only on a real set->clear transition, so a double-free cannot skew it) -- symmetric BY CONSTRUCTION via the pid bitmap invariant, side-stepping task_fork's non-uniform creation paths (task_fork bypasses task_init_common) and the scheduler-invoked task_destroy. user_task_over_cap() = (g_current && euid!=0 && count>=USER_TASK_MAX(4096)); checked at the top of task_fork + task_create_user (return NULL) and sys_thread (return -EAGAIN). Root (euid 0, incl. every boot/system task) and early-boot creation (g_current==NULL) are EXEMPT, so boot -- which runs as root -- never blocks: ZERO regression. 4096 dwarfs a normal session; bounds non-root tasks to ~40 MiB. Verified: 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15, processes spawn normally (root-exempt). Built clean. Code-proof + boot (user_task_over_cap reads mutable globals -> no clean pure-helper unit test). With F164+F165 the resource-DoS surface (per-proc fd cap + non-root nproc cap) is closed. Terse per efficiency mandate.
- 2026-07-01 - F166 FIXED (LARGE workflow-scan lead: bind/connect/sendto prefaulted their READ-ONLY user buffers -> file-backed page corruption): sys_bind/sys_connect/sys_sendto validated their read-source buffers (the sockaddr, and sendto's data) with user_buf_check (syscall.c ~3327/3414/3433/3447), which calls user_buf_prefault -> maps+ZEROS absent pages. For a READ source that is a file-backed mmap not yet faulted in, the prefault zero-fills the page: the send reads zeros instead of the file content, and for MAP_SHARED the zero-fill is written back to the file / visible to other mappers -- deterministic, unprivileged data corruption. The kernel already documents this exact hazard (syscall.c:3684-3688) and uses the non-prefaulting user_buf_readable_ok for write(2)'s data buffer for precisely this reason. ROOT fix: swap the four read-source checks to user_buf_readable_ok (validates range + requires a VMA so the raw read demand-faults the REAL content, no prefault-zero); accept()'s peer sockaddr stays user_buf_check (it is a WRITE destination the kernel fills, where prefault is correct). Verified: 89 selftests PASSED, 0 faults, DHCP 10.0.2.15 (UDP sendto now routes through readable_ok and still works). Built clean. Found by a 14-subsystem multi-agent workflow scan with adversarial (double-refuter) verification.
