(b) [MED, concurrency] tty->fg_pgid read/written via copy_to/from_user with NO tty->lock in the TIOCGPGRP/TIOCSPGRP path (drivers/tty/pty.c ~487) -> torn pgid -> signals to the wrong pgroup; the locked helper pattern already exists for termios (tty_get/set_termios); fix = tty_get/set_pgid under tty->lock. (c) [MED, concurrency] ephemeral-port allocation (net/tcp.c ~1032) non-atomic read-inc-write of s_eph_port on SMP -> duplicate ports (collision only for an identical 4-tuple); fix = atomic fetch-add. (d) [LOW, hardening] wait_queue_wake_one (wait.c ~199) calls fired->func with no dead-check / func-whitelist (unlike wake_all) -- only reachable on an already-corrupted chain. NOTE (assessed NOT bugs by the second-pass synthesis): AHCI count>65535 "overflow" is a FALSE POSITIVE (the 248-entry/PAGE-cap PRDT loop clean-fails before issue_cmd); tcp.c:928 send-window underflow is memory-safe (clamped to <=MSS per SCAN #20) -- a minor flow-control nit; ext2 seek 32-bit truncation is the already-recorded accepted-LOW nit.
- 2026-07-01 - F167 FIXED (workflow-scan backlog (a): fat32_open two unguarded kmalloc NULL-derefs -> panic on OOM): fat32_open (fs/fat32.c ~239-262) did `fat32_fd_t* fd = kmalloc(...)` then derefed fd->start_cluster with NO NULL check, and `vfs_file_t* f = kmalloc(...); if (f) memset(...)` guarded ONLY the memset while lines 249-262 derefed f unconditionally -> a kernel NULL-deref panic on either kmalloc OOM. Fix: `if (!fd) return NULL;` after the fd alloc, and `if (!f) { kfree(fd); return NULL; }` after the f alloc (frees fd so no leak), mirroring the ext2/proc/vfs alloc pattern. fat32 is not the boot fs (ext2 is) so code-proof + clean boot: 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF, DHCP 10.0.2.15; built clean.
- 2026-07-01 - F168 FIXED (workflow-scan backlog (b): TIOCSPGRP torn-write of tty->fg_pgid): the TIOCSPGRP ioctl (drivers/tty/pty.c ~491) did copy_from_user DIRECTLY into the live tty->fg_pgid. copy_from_user's memcpy takes a RUNTIME len, so a 4-byte copy may lower byte-wise and TEAR the field under a concurrent reader (Ctrl-C SIGINT / SIGWINCH signal routing at tty.c:184/pty.c:500) -> a signal delivered to a garbage pgid. Fix: land in a local uint32 then publish with one aligned __atomic_store_n(RELEASE); TIOCGPGRP snapshots via __atomic_load_n(ACQUIRE) before copy_to_user. No tty->lock needed -- fg_pgid is a SINGLE word, so an aligned atomic store/load suffices (the multi-word termios needs the lock for a consistent snapshot; a single word does not). Verified: 89 selftests PASSED (incl. [pty_ioctl_test] -- bad-pointer -EFAULT rejection intact), 0 faults, DHCP 10.0.2.15; built clean.
- 2026-07-01 - WORKFLOW-SCAN backlog UPDATE: (b)-as-flagged "no lock -> torn pgid" was PARTLY a mis-frame -- the read side is fine (an aligned uint32 load is atomic on x86); the real defect was only the copy_from_user WRITE tearing the field, fixed in F168 without a lock. While verifying (b) I found a SEPARATE real bug, recorded for a focused turn: [MED, authz] TIOCSPGRP sets fg_pgid to an ARBITRARY user pgid with NO validation (no session-membership check) -> a process can point the terminal's foreground group at a FOREIGN pgid, redirecting terminal-generated signals (SIGINT/SIGWINCH) or hijacking the foreground -- a job-control/confused-deputy issue akin to F162 (setpgid). Fix = require the new pgid to be a process group in the caller's session before storing (walk task_idx_pgid for sid == g_current->sid). Remaining backlog: (c) tcp ephemeral-port non-atomic alloc, (d) wait_queue_wake_one dead-check, plus this TIOCSPGRP validation.
- 2026-07-01 - F169 FIXED (workflow-scan backlog (c): tcp_ephemeral_port non-atomic RMW -> duplicate ports on SMP): tcp_ephemeral_port (net/tcp.c:1032) did `p = s_eph_port; s_eph_port = wrap(s_eph_port+1); return p;` -- a bare read-modify-write of a file-static counter with no atomic/lock, so two concurrent connect()s on different CPUs read the same value and return the SAME ephemeral local port (lost update; only bites for an identical 4-tuple but a real SMP race). Fix: `__atomic_fetch_add(&s_eph_next, 1)` hands each caller a distinct index, mapped into the identical [49152,65535] range via `49152 + n%16384`, mirroring vmm's s_mmio_next lock-free bump. Verified: 89 selftests PASSED (7 tcp_* PASS), 0 faults, DHCP 10.0.2.15; built clean. Code-proof + boot (atomic + bounded modulo; a two-CPU collision is not deterministically reproducible in the harness).
- 2026-07-01 - F170 FIXED (workflow-scan backlog (d), LOW hardening: wait_queue_wake_one dispatched on a possibly-dead entry with no func-whitelist): wait_queue_wake_one (kernel/wait.c ~220) called fired->func UNCONDITIONALLY, but its skip loop (199-203) can break out on a corrupted chain (a dead entry whose next is non-canonical) leaving `fired` on a DEAD entry -- unlike wake_all (142/148) which dead-checks + func-whitelists before dispatch. On an already-clobbered wait chain this fires a dead/garbage entry's func (UAF / cryptic #UD). Fix (DRY, mirror wake_all EXACTLY): only dispatch when `!atomic_load_acq(&fired->dead)`, and halt-with-context if fired->func is not task_wake_func/epoll_wake_func. Normal wake path unchanged (live entry + whitelisted func -> identical behavior). Verified: 89 selftests PASSED, 0 faults, no false WAKE UAF, DHCP 10.0.2.15; built clean. Defense-in-depth (only reachable on an already-corrupted chain).
- 2026-07-01 - F171 FIXED (workflow-scan follow-up, MED authz: TIOCSPGRP set the terminal foreground group to ANY pgid with no validation): the TIOCSPGRP ioctl (drivers/tty/pty.c, pty_tty_ioctl_common) stored a user-supplied pgid straight into tty->fg_pgid, so a process could point the terminal foreground at a FOREIGN session's pgid -> redirect terminal-generated signals (SIGINT/SIGWINCH) or hijack the foreground (job-control confused-deputy, F162-class). ROOT fix (POSIX): before the atomic store, require (1) the caller owns this controlling terminal -- g_current->sid == tty->session (the pattern already used for SIGTTIN at pty.c:344) -- and (2) the new pgid is a process group IN the caller's session (fast path pg == g_current->pgid; else task_idx_pgid_walk(pg, ..) confirms some task with that pgid has sid == g_current->sid); else -EPERM. Verified: 89 selftests PASSED (incl. [pty_ioctl_test] -- bad-pointer -EFAULT still returned before the session check), 0 faults, DHCP 10.0.2.15; built clean. Code-proof + boot (the cross-session rejection needs a real multi-session userspace the harness lacks; legit shell job control is same-session so still allowed).
- 2026-07-01 - F172 FIXED (DRY sweep-1 drift-bug LDB-1 = shipped security bug, HIGH: unauthorized set-foreground-pgrp on the console/tcsetpgrp paths -> terminal-signal hijack) + consolidated to ONE authorized setter. sys_tcsetpgrp (syscall.c:4546) and the sys_ioctl TIOCSPGRP tty0 fallback (syscall.c:4600) set g_tty0.fg_pgid from a caller-controlled pgid with ZERO authorization -- neither the session-ownership check nor the in-session-pgrp walk the hardened PTY path (F171/beae63c) enforces -- while g_tty0.fg_pgid is the target of console-generated SIGINT/SIGTSTP/SIGQUIT (tty.c:184-202). So any process, even in a FOREIGN session, could tcsetpgrp()/ioctl(TIOCSPGRP) the console to point the foreground at an arbitrary pgrp and hijack Ctrl-C/Z/\\ (job-control confused-deputy). The PTY path was fixed in F171 but the console/tcsetpgrp paths were never updated -- classic drift (two parallel set-fg-pgrp paths, only one authorized). ROOT fix (DRY single-source-of-truth, per the project prime directive "one shared mechanism, never two drifting paths"): extract the authorization+publish into int tty_set_fg_pgrp(tty, pg) in tty.c (caller must own the tty's session AND pg must be a pgrp in that session; publishes via __atomic_store_n RELEASE; -EPERM otherwise), and route ALL THREE user set-fg-pgrp sites through it -- pty TIOCSPGRP, sys_tcsetpgrp, console TIOCSPGRP -- deleting the pty-local duplicate. Future TIOCSPGRP-like additions now inherit the check. (Adopted the verifier's correction: the earlier F168 "4-byte tear" framing was overstated -- an aligned uint32 store does not value-tear on x86-64; the __ATOMIC_RELEASE is the ordering barrier pairing the acquire reader, kept.) Kernel-internal fg sets on spawn/exit (syscall.c:1481/1703, to a known child) are correctly left unauthorized. VERIFIED reachability + no regression: g_tty0.session is a live field (init=1, set by TIOCSCTTY at tty.c:462, used by tty_get_ctty at 454) so the legit console owner satisfies sid==session; built clean, 89 selftests PASSED (incl [pty_ioctl_test] -- bad-pointer -EFAULT still returned before the auth), 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15, no tcsetpgrp/job-control breakage in the boot. NOTE: DRY sweep-1 was heavily rate-limited (13 of 14 discovery angles failed with a transient server rate-limit) -- only the authz/tty angle ran, yielding this drift-bug + 3 small confirmed consolidations (tty_is_background predicate x4, cred established-id predicate, chmod setuid sanitize) still PENDING; sweep-1 must be RE-RUN for the 13 missing angles (vfs-open-init, dup-functions, drift-paths, prim-bounds/usercopy, rings, refcount, magic-consts, lock-idioms, list-walks, pci-virtio, str-parse, err-unwind).
- 2026-07-01 - F173 (DRY sweep-1, U-preempt): preempt_enable_no_resched() SSOT. 10 IRQ/tick/completion paths (irq_wait, input_core, timerfd, signalfd x2, ahci x4, nvme) hand-rolled `this_cpu()->preempt_depth--` -- a bare decrement that deliberately AVOIDS preempt_enable()'s sched_preempt() (a context switch is forbidden in those contexts). Extracted preempt.h ALWAYS_INLINE preempt_enable_no_resched() = (void)this_cpu_dec_u32_nonzero(preempt_depth) (gs-relative single-insn decrement, matches preempt_disable's style) and routed all 10 through it -- one named primitive for "leave a preempt-disabled section without rescheduling", so the idiom can't drift. Provably behavior-identical (same bare per-CPU decrement). Built clean, 89 selftests PASSED, 0 faults, DHCP 10.0.2.15 (disk.img/serial mtimes newer than the edits -> boot ran the post-edit binary).
- 2026-07-02 - F174 (DRY sweep-1): verified ext2 dual-walker drift-flag = NOT a bug + U-ahci-const consolidation. (1) ext2 path_to_inode (raw, no perm) vs ext2_lookup_path (perm-aware, EXEC per dir component): traced every userspace path -- all go through fs_lookup -> ext2_lookup_path(&cred) FIRST (search-perm gate), open uses ext2_open_ino by the already-resolved inode, ext2_open(raw) only after a perm-aware fs_lookup on the parent, and mutating ops (unlink/mkdir/rename) re-check write via ext2_dir_write_ok(parent, cred) on the same inode they modify (closes path-TOCTOU). path_to_inode is an internal re-resolver reached only after perms are enforced -> NO authz bypass; merging the two would double-check or break internal callers -> justified separation (DRY not a religion). - 2026-07-02 - F175 (DRY sweep-1, U-vaddr): verified the "2 CONFLICTING canonical-VA constants" flag = NOT a bug, then consolidated to common.h. USER_ADDR_MAX (0x00007FFFFFFFFFFF = 2^47-1, last valid user byte) and USER_ADDR_CEIL (2^47, first non-canonical addr) differ by 1 but are NOT in conflict: MAX is always paired with > / <= (reject addr > MAX, end-1 > MAX) and CEIL / (1ULL<<47) / 0x800000000000 always with >= / < (reject addr >= CEIL, addr+len > CEIL) -- every one of the 8 sites accepts exactly [0, 2^47) and rejects the kernel half + the non-canonical gap. They are inclusive-last vs exclusive-first spellings of the SAME boundary, each with the matching operator (no off-by-one). Pure dedup: both were open-coded (USER_ADDR_MAX #defined locally in syscall.c, USER_ADDR_CEIL locally in signal.c, plus raw (1ULL<<47) x2 in syscall.c and 0x800000000000 x2 in vmm.c's stack-walker + 1 mmap selftest vector). Moved the matched pair to common.h (documented invariant USER_ADDR_CEIL == USER_ADDR_MAX + 1 == 2^47, alongside HHDM_OFFSET/KERNEL_BASE_VIRT), removed the 2 local #defines, routed all raw literals through the names. Kept BOTH constants -- collapsing to one value would force operator rewrites and risk an off-by-one on a security boundary (DRY not a religion). Left vmm.c:755's 0x8000000000000000 untouched (that is 2^63, the top-bit kernel/user split, a DIFFERENT concept). Values + comparison operators unchanged -> provably behavior-identical. Built clean; 89 selftests PASSED incl the three that exercise this boundary directly ([access_ok_test] null/kernel/wrap/end-escape rejected via _access_ok+USER_ADDR_MAX, [mmap_range_test] higher-half escape rejected, [user_ptr_test]), 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15, disk.img mtime > edits. NOTE: the first boot STALLED at [pipe_race] (a 1-writer/1-reader 64KiB concurrency stress test); a re-boot of the IDENTICAL binary passed it 65536/65536 -> confirmed a pre-existing rare timing flake in pipe_race, unrelated to this value-identical change (isolated by same-binary re-run, not stashed).
- 2026-07-02 - F176 (DRY sweep-1, U-access-ok): verified the signal path's sig_user_range_ok is EXACTLY _access_ok (not weaker), then consolidated to one shared validator. Proved equivalence across every input class: both reject addr==0; `addr > USER_ADDR_MAX` == `addr >= USER_ADDR_CEIL` (CEIL == MAX+1 == 2^47); the end check `end-1 > MAX` (with end=addr+len) == `addr+len > CEIL`; the wrap guards `!ckd_add_u64(addr,len,&end)` and `addr+len < addr` (unsigned) are the same overflow test; len==0 (skipped block vs addr+0) yields the same accept. So the two accept/reject the identical set [1,2^47) with addr+len <= 2^47 and no u64 wrap -- no security drift (a weaker signal-path check would let a non-canonical sigframe base #GP the kernel at iretq, the makaterm Ctrl+C crash class). Pure dedup. checked.h explicitly forbids subsystem/copy primitives ("NOT a catch-all header"), so created kernel/include/uaccess.h (includes common.h + checked.h) as THE home for user-access primitives, moved _access_ok there verbatim (static inline, byte-identical logic), removed syscall.c's local def + its forward-decl (104), deleted signal.c's sig_user_range_ok, and routed signal_setup_frame's sigframe-window check through _access_ok. uaccess.h is now the destined home for U-uaccess-hdr's copy_*_user decls too. Built clean; 89 selftests PASSED incl the ones that exercise _access_ok directly ([access_ok_test] null/kernel/wrap/end-escape, [user_ptr_test], [copyuser_test]) and the signal path ([signalfd-selftest], [signal_send_pid], [signal_perm]); 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP, DHCP 10.0.2.15, full boot to [evdev_ring], disk.img mtime > edits.

- 2026-07-02 - F178 (DRY sweep-1, U-checksum): the TCP/UDP transport checksum was open-coded 5x (udp recv+send, tcp send-segment+send-rst+recv-validate) while transport_checksum() sat __attribute__((unused)) in ipv4.c. The 5th, tcp_send_rst, OMITTED the odd-byte fold line -- but a RST is header-only (TCP_HDR_MIN_LEN=20 bytes, always EVEN) so `l` is 0 at that point and the missing fold never executes: latent-but-harmless (the reason it never surfaced). Made transport_checksum extern (dropped static + the unused attr), declared it in ipv4.h, and routed all 5 sites through it; the rst fix is by-construction (the shared helper folds the odd byte, a no-op for RST's even length, so identical output while killing the divergence). - 2026-07-02 - F179 (DRY sweep-1, U-fifo): the intrusive singly-linked FIFO (enqueue-at-tail / dequeue-from-head, `->next` field + a count) was hand-rolled 4x -- udp_rx (socket.c), unix-datagram + unix-accept-backlog (unix_sock.c), io_uring CQ-overflow (io_uring.c). Verified all 4 use the byte-identical discipline: enqueue `node->next=NULL; if(tail) tail->next=node; else head=node; tail=node; count++`, dequeue `x=head; if(x){head=x->next; if(!head) tail=NULL; count--}`. The subtle invariant is the `if(!head) tail=NULL` empty-reset -- omit it and a stale tail dangles so the next enqueue writes through freed memory (UAF). Extracted FIFO_ENQUEUE_TAIL/FIFO_DEQUEUE_HEAD to a new kernel/include/ilist.h (chose macros over an offset-based void** helper: casting each queue's `type**` head/tail to `void**` is strict-aliasing UB; macros stay type-clean, BSD <sys/queue.h> precedent; caller keeps its lock, and the udp_rx full-queue check stays before the enqueue). Routed all 9 sites (4 enqueue + 5 dequeue -- udp_rx has 2 identical dequeue blocks). The io_uring dequeue macro is placed at the EXISTING unlink point (n is already == overflow_head there, so the macro's re-read of head into n is a no-op) -- no statement reorder, cqe-copy + CQ-tail publish stay before the unlink as before. Pure structural dedup, no behavior change. Built clean (no redefinition/undeclared); 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC/#PF/#GP. The 3 FIFOs exercised at boot all validate the shared macro: DHCP 10.0.2.15 (udp_rx enqueue on recv + dequeue on recvfrom), [unix_stream_accept] PASS (backlog enqueue on connect + dequeue on accept), [unix_dgram_peer] PASS (dgram queue), [io_uring_test]/[io_ring_idx] PASS (overflow queue) -- no UAF/#PF, proving the empty-reset invariant holds. - 2026-07-02 - F182 (DRY sweep-1, U-ttybg): the POSIX "caller is a background process for this controlling tty" test -- `g_current && tty->fg_pgid && g_current->sid == tty->session && g_current->pgid != tty->fg_pgid` -- was hand-rolled 4x: tty.c and pty.c, each in the SIGTTIN (background read) and SIGTTOU (background write) job-control gates. Job control (Ctrl-Z/fg/bg) isn't in the headless selftests, so the predicate is code-proven behavior-identical + the tty/pty tests confirm no regression. Full boot to [evdev_ring], disk.img mtime > edits.
- 2026-07-02 - F183 (root-cause fix for the DHCP boot "flake" the loop kept re-booting around): the interface came up at 10.0.2.15 on some boots and sat at 0.0.0.0 for what looked like forever on others. ROOT: userland/apps/net/net.c do_lease() retried DISCOVER 5x with 4/8/16/32/64s exponential backoff = up to 124s BEFORE the QEMU SLIRP static-lease fallback (10.0.2.15) fires. QEMU SLIRP ignores a DISCOVER "when it considers the guest already bound" (RFC 2131 4.1, already documented in the fallback comment), so on those boots the real DHCP exchange never completes and the interface sits at 0.0.0.0 until the 124s backoff drains -- every observation window in the loop (~30-45s) caught it mid-backoff and read it as a random flake (it was NOT code-per-turn: a clean-F179-baseline repro in F180 confirmed env, but the env cause is this 124s wait, not true randomness). FIX: bounded fast backoff -- timeout 1000ms, max_retries 3 (1s+2s+4s ~= 7s), so the fallback fires within ~7s and the interface is reliably up well before any selftest-boot completes. A real DHCP server answers in <1s so 3 quick tries still cover transient loss, and the post-bind renewal loop re-leases. VERIFIED: 5 consecutive boots all reach 10.0.2.15 at serial line ~38 (was intermittently 0.0.0.0 across the prior ~10 boots); 89 selftests PASSED, 0 faults, each boot. Also fixed a real out-of-bounds read in the same file: log_msg did `write(1, "[net] ", 9)` on a 6-byte string literal (3-byte over-read into adjacent rodata) -> corrected to 6. NOTE: this leaves the deeper "why does SLIRP sometimes ignore our DISCOVER" (qemu-SLIRP-internal, not our kernel) unaddressed by design -- the fast fallback is the correct handling and makes it invisible; if a real NIC ever needs true DHCP the renewal loop + 3 quick tries still perform it. build.sh net.svc stays stdio=null (a diagnostic flip to stdio=inherit confirmed /bin/net's stdout does not chain to the serial console anyway).
- 2026-07-02 - F184 (DRY sweep-1, U-cred-id): the 3-slot "id in {real,eff,saved}" membership test was hand-rolled at 6 sites (sweep flagged 2, I found 4 more): cred_seteuid + cred_setegid (security/cred.h) and, in syscall.c, spawn_cred_allowed's uid_ok + gid_ok AND sys_setreuid's euid_ok + sys_setregid's egid_ok (4256/4274). Verified all 6 byte-identical (order-independent OR over ruid/euid/suid, resp rgid/egid/sgid). Extracted cred_uid_is_one_of / cred_gid_is_one_of static inlines into cred.h; routed all 6. spawn's gid_ok keeps its `|| cred_in_group(c,gid)` supplementary-group term; setre*'s real-id checks keep their DISTINCT 2-slot {real,eff} set; cred_setuid/cred_setgid keep their DISTINCT 2-slot {real,saved} set (POSIX -- NOT merged, per plan). Behavior-identical. Built clean; 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/FAULT/PANIC/#PF/#GP; the credential paths validate directly -- [spawn_cred] PASS (no spawn escalation), [ksec_setuid] PASS (setuid-exec fails closed), [signal_perm] PASS (kill authz). DHCP hit the DEEPER flake this boot (see F185) -- unrelated to this cred-only change (spawn_cred selftest exercises the exact predicate and passes; /bin/net runs as root and never setuids).
- 2026-07-02 - F185 (TRUE root-cause of the DHCP "flake"; F183 was a mis-attributed partial fix): the interface came up 10.0.2.15 every boot all along -- the flake was a LOG-DETECTION artifact. Root: kernel/net/net.c logged via a hand-rolled ser_putc that wrote COM1 (port 0x3F8) char-by-char with NO serial lock, while kprintf takes serial_lock_irqsave. During the concurrent SMP selftest kprintf storm, net.c's "[net] ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15\n" (printed one char at a time) interleaved with other CPUs' output and got shredded mid-word, so the harness grep for the contiguous "ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15" intermittently missed it -- but net_set_config() unconditionally sets s_our_ip BEFORE logging, so the network was configured regardless. Isolated by kernel-instrumenting the DHCP path: on a "fail" boot the full DISCOVER->OFFER->REQUEST->ACK exchange completed, socket_deliver_udp delivered both replies, sys_net_ifconfig was entered with ip=0x0f02000a (=10.0.2.15) and net_set_config was reached -- only the print was garbled/absent. FIX: route all net.c log lines through kprintf_atomic (whole-line serial lock) and delete the unlocked ser_putc/ser_puts/ser_put_dec/ser_put_hex8 helpers entirely. VERIFIED: "[net] ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15" now appears on 5/5 consecutive boots (was intermittently missing); 89 selftests, 0 faults. HONESTY: F183 (do_lease 124s->7s backoff) was based on the WRONG root (I thought the net wasn't coming up) -- it is still a valid improvement (fast SLIRP-static fallback vs a 2-minute wait) so it stays, but THIS is the actual flake fix. REMAINING (separate, minor): the occasional 88-vs-89 miscount is the SAME class -- selftest result lines use per-char kprintf (byte-interleavable BY DESIGN; see the kprintf.c comment) instead of kprintf_atomic; it is a grep-count artifact (the test PASSED, only its line garbled), fixable by routing the ~89 selftest result kprintf()s through kprintf_atomic, deferred as a focused sweep.
- 2026-07-02 - F186 (DRY sweep-1, U-msi): the standard PCI capability-list walk (read cap ptr at 0x34, follow next-ptr, match a cap id) was hand-rolled IDENTICALLY across 4 drivers to find MSI-X (id 0x11) and, in ahci/virtio_net, legacy MSI (id 0x05). Extracted pci_find_cap(bus,dev,fn,cap_id) as a static inline in kernel/drivers/pci/pci.h (no new .c/build change; uses the already-declared pci_cfg_read32), returning the cap offset or 0; added a 48-hop bound so a malformed/cyclic cap list can't spin the kernel (a safe-by-construction hardening the hand-rolled loops lacked). Routed all 6 sites: nvme_msix_enable, ahci (0x11 + 0x05), virtio_net (0x11 + its MSI 0x05 fallback), virtio_input. Behavior-identical (finds the same first-matching cap offset). DELIBERATELY LEFT per-driver (DRY not a religion -- interrupt-critical, genuinely divergent): the MSI-X table BAR-map, the per-vector program (0xFEE00000|apic<<12 addr / data=vector / vector_ctrl mask) and the enable/mask bits -- nvme steers one vector per CPU, virtio_net one per queue, ahci/virtio_input a single vector, with different masking and target-CPU; a wrong merge there = a misrouted/lost interrupt = silent I/O hang. Built clean; 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/FAULT/PANIC/#PF/#GP. MSI-X is exercised at boot and all paths work through the routed walk: virtio-net DHCP 10.0.2.15 (OFFER/ACK delivered via its MSI-X vector), ahci disk I/O (ext2_* selftests read/write the disk via the AHCI completion interrupt), virtio-gpu init -- a wrong cap offset would have wedged these. (nvme has no device in the QEMU config so its path is compile-verified + identical-by-construction.) Full boot to [evdev_ring], disk.img mtime > edits.
- 2026-07-02 - F187 (DRY sweep-1, U-align): pmm.c (align_up + align_down) and kheap.c (align_up) each hand-rolled the identical PAGE-fixed single-arg round helper -- (addr + PAGE_SIZE-1) & ~(PAGE_SIZE-1) for up, addr & ~(PAGE_SIZE-1) for down; kheap's took virt_addr_t (== uintptr_t == 64-bit), so all three are byte-identical 64-bit pow2 rounders. Moved to common.h as page_align_up/page_align_down static inlines (next to PAGE_SIZE/PAGE_MASK, using ~PAGE_MASK -- identical math). RENAMED from the bare align_up/align_down: a global single-arg align_up in a shared header is a footgun (it implies the usual 2-arg align_up(x,a)); page_align_* is unambiguous. Removed the 3 local defs, renamed all 15 call sites (13 pmm + 2 kheap; nothing outside mm/ used them). Behavior-identical. Built clean; 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/FAULT/PANIC/#PF/#GP -- the mm/allocator paths that back these all pass: [slab_test], [kheap_test] (heap base = page_align_up(__kernel_end)), [mmap_range_test], [pmm10-test]; and the very fact the kernel boots proves pmm's page_align_up/down (used to bracket every e820 region + the kernel image in the physical memory map) are correct, since a wrong mask would #PF in pmm_init before any selftest. DHCP 10.0.2.15. Full boot to [evdev_ring], disk.img mtime > edits.
- 2026-07-02 - F188 (DRY sweep-1, U-pgid-twin): sys_getpgid and sys_getsid were byte-identical -- pid_arg==0 returns the caller's own field, else rcu_read_lock + sched_find_pid + (null||TASK_ZOMBIE ? -ESRCH : field) + rcu_read_unlock -- differing ONLY in which field is returned (pgid vs sid) and the pid==0 self-case; neither has a permission/visibility check the other lacks (both are unrestricted POSIX reads). Extracted pgid_sid_lookup(pid_arg, want_sid) and made both syscalls thin wrappers (want_sid 0/1). The looked-up field is still read INSIDE the rcu section before rcu_read_unlock, so the RCU-alive window is preserved (no use-after-free of the task pointer). Behavior-identical. Built clean; 89 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/FAULT/PANIC/#PF/#GP; [tgleader] + [signal_perm] (the process/session-id machinery) pass, DHCP 10.0.2.15. Full boot to [evdev_ring], disk.img mtime > edits.
